O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Oh, you, very wise sons, I have completed this book that is the end of the science of medicine and its fulfillment, and I have finished it by his explanations and by his declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is fortified in our region and is drawn from all things, it has perished and been lost, and nothing remains of it except the small descriptions in books of the ancients that the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this comes the error and the foolishness, and the minds are closed and the knowledge is distant.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I can revive this treatment along with the order of exposure and declaration and abbreviation; and I will bring together the forms of the cautery irons, and other tools of the work with the assistance of declaration and preparation of it, as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	Because for the reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is extended.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for him who undertakes this to surpass in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, until he knows the judgment of the bones, and their forms and conjunctions and separations of all, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and tendons and the number of joints, and the movement and resting of them, and the origin of their issue.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And because Hippocrates says that with the hand alone is not much, and with work is little; and specifically in the art of surgery.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We say in the introduction of this book that those who are not familiar with the things mentioned before, if they try to perform surgery may make mistakes and harm people; therefore, I have often seen many times that those who practice this science and abandon their knowledge and lack experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish man who lanced an abscess of scrophules or the neck of a woman, and lanced the arteries of the neck; because so much blood issued out that the woman died between her hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And another mirror that treats a stone from a man of age, and the stone was large; it took with it a piece of the bladder, and died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	I had already been called for the extraction, and saw the misalignment of the limb and the size of the stone, and if they cut it, it would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And another mirror that took in the care of our lord who had his leg broken, and with the breaker got a wound; and the mirror, due to ignorance, kept the fracture above the wound as a splint for a long time, and did not allow any drainage, and thus left it; and commanded that it not be removed, and delayed so that the leg was entirely infected and the foot and came to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I was urged to come to dislocate his leg; and when I heard it dislocated, it was in place and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all ways of the corruption were already confirmed in the member, and it could not be healed; and the corruption did not cease to spread through the member until the member was completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another method that crushed the abscess and became putrid, and then it inflamed due to its evil nature.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For putridity, when it is free of melancholic humor, does not need much if one only touches it with iron if it is in a place where everything can be completely removed that is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And therefore, dear son, you should know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: that is, where it is in many positions; and I will show in every chapter of this book where it has fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	For this reason, it is important that you guard yourself, so that the foolish may not speak evil of you if you take up your arms firmly and courageously, and use the best means so that by the grace of God you come to safety and are healed; and leave behind the spreading diseases of sorrowful health; and remove your weapons from what causes you doubt, and be in such a way that you may come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galiens advises in some of his warnings: "Do not take on the care of an illness that you are not called to be a foolish physician.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatment in three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are about fire cauteries and medical cautery abscesses, and the chapters are ordered from the head to the feet; and about the forms of instruments, and the irons of cauteries, and all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapters are about cutting and incising, and about wounds, and about the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and the chapters are ordered and about the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; it is ordered from the highest to the lowest, and the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	As we remember the work, it is necessary that I tell the quality of the aid and the harm of each ingredient.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of aid and harm is the longest and most subtle science and secret knowledge; and for this reason many wise people spoke about it and agreed on this; and I do not speak much about it because I want to keep it long.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that the fire cautery helps universally in all ingredients where there is matter, whether it is a hot ingredient with matter, or a dry ingredient without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry conditions, some said that the fire cautery is great help; while others said the opposite, that the fire cautery is only helpful for diseases that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be used to treat hot diseases by heat or dryness; while those who said the opposite claimed that the fire cautery helps greatly with hot and dry diseases that come from within people.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of the person and its moisture to the hot fire, you heat the body.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this saying.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it once by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in all ways, no one interferes with it except those who have experienced it, and who know by long use the chapter on cauteries, and the variety of human constitutions, and their dispositions and causes of diseases, and the remedies and space of time; for other constitutions we do not fear, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the patients gathered and agreed to the cauterization.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, my sons, that cauterization with fire is one of the secrets of cures, and of greater benefit than cauterization with hot medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For the fever is simple, and comes only to the member that is cooked, and does not harm other members unless it is named.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The burning medicines come from one member to another by moving away, and bring diseases of grief to the affected member; and by chance it is the fever that makes the suffering high and because of the goodness of its substance does not cause much harm, if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this is what I have found by experience and by the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and it has been based on the truth of things; and because I do not like to speak too much, I will only give you the secret which is hidden or fire, and the quality of the work, how it heals diseases of the body, as the philosopher says in demonstrating; now receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, child, that they should be done with cauterizations in what manner they should be made, and they will ask for them.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that the cauterization is beneficial in all times, because the harmful things that come from it are removed by the help of the cauterization; and even if the cauterization is for necessary pain, except for those that cannot wait until the time when greater malice does not come to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think like the foolish; for the disease that is cured by cauterization has no return; and they say it thus, but it is not so because cauterizations are only medicine that moves the complexion, and dries the humors that are the cause of pain, and is as good a medicine for its swiftness of value, and for the virtue of its work and its lordship.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And the thing is that the disease comes only once according to the nature of the illness and its kind; and it is gathered in him the superfluities by the acquisition of foods and similar things, if not cauterize administered in the place where there is little superfluity and moisture, as cauterizing for pain, and similar things, and the pain does not return much; but this happens little.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	Many people do not understand why cauterizing is called the last resort of medicine, and it is true; but they do not believe that cauterizing works after medicine, but rather their intentions are false, and it is cauterizing the last resort of medicine because when we administer methods of treatment in any illness and they do not work, then we administer the cautery, and it is better.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, it is important to understand that cauterization is a part of medical treatment, not according to the intention of those who are misled.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cauterization with a gold instrument is better than iron, and they did not say why except for the quality of gold and the high value of its substance; and they said that the wounds of cautery do not putrefy, but I have found that this is not always true, as I have experienced it, and cauterization with gold is better than iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And in any case, when you heat a gold instrument, do not be deceived by its color of gold, and it has cooled for a while; and if it is heated too much, they put it in the fire; and thus there is enough precaution.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And therefore we use the fire cauterization that we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or I have ordered this chapter on the shoulder joints from the feet, because it is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	The fire cauterization oil.
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cauterization is valuable against moisture and cold on the head, and it is done for two reasons: because of a disease called "soda", and because of many humors that descend from the joint to the ears, and due to many dreams and tooth pain and throat pain, and indeed for all diseases that come from cold as paralysis and soda and apoplexy and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the hairs should be removed by medicinal means, changing the skin three or four times, according to the virtues and age and custom of the hair, so that it can suffer; and then repeat the head of the hair.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make it sit crossed between your hands, and put your hands on its feet; after putting the root of your palm above the root of its nail between its two eyes; and where your fingers come out, if it bleeds, then heat the cautery called "olivare", of which this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the bone in its signet of ink, and do by gently pulling and gradually stretching your hand little by little; then release your hand slowly, and reward the bone if you see the bone is small; and if you do not see it, then restart the cauterization until you see the bone as I have told you; after take a little of silk, and put in heat and soft cotton inside, and place on the bone, and let it rest for three hours; after put on a moist cloth in butter; and leave it until the burn is healed; after care the wound which is called «tetrafarmaçon» until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the ancients said that the longer the wound remains open, the more it purges; and for this reason, it helps to heal.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And none of these said that one should burn the cauterizer until a part of the bone is charred, and then remove what has been charred from the bone, and treat it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And the others said that one should burn the cauterizer until it is as hot as the iron that women put in their hair for the reason that the humors issue out moist; and the wound should remain open long; after that, it must be treated and healed.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cauterization do not seem to be good for all, except in those men where there is a fear of poverty; and it seems to me that I should leave it; for the affected ones are weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we testify in other members; and even when the affected one is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cauterization is safer and less painful for me, and from this use I work in such a way.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the ancient pain of the main
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When the main pain comes from chronic conditions and lasts a long time, one should use the remedies of years and pills called "cochie", and cleansing of head and eyes and plasters; and if one does the cauterization that we have already mentioned, it is not good.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take a small piece of the cloth that the patient has, and it is not too cold; then cauterize with that fire that we have mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After performing the fire cautery on each of the horns of the head up to the bone, as we have mentioned before, and then perform the cauterization with the tool called "vasselz"; and place the vacuum tubes in it; and raise your hand so that you do not touch the bone: the pain from this cauterization is much greater than from other methods, and I will explain why; and it is necessary that the cauterizations of the horns be more subtle than the one used to cauterize the midline of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	for the fire cauterization
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When in one part of the head sudden pain comes, and the disease is spread to the eye, and the patient is purged by medicines that are not modified, and the other cures that I have mentioned in the division of diseases do not help: then you must cauterize it in two ways, namely with medicine or fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauterization with medicine is such that you press a piece of lard, and remove the skin and scrape it lightly on the two eyes, and then make a hole in the temple where the pain is located in such a way that you can replace the piece of lard outside the skin; and when it is replaced, bind it well and hold it for twelve hours; then remove it and treat it with honey for two or three days; then place a cotton pad soaked in butter on the wound.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment of burns until they are healed; and if you see that some medicines cause blisters, which I have written or treat such medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cauterization is done in this way.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cauterizing iron of such a shape:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the head is made in the shape of a clover or it has a small beak, and in the middle has a small appearance; and put it on the painful part, and hold your hand and gently press the iron until half of the sharp edge is burned; and release your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is before, and there is abundant bleeding.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After applying gauze wrapped in silk to the wound for three days; then apply moistened boric acid to the wound and treat it with ointment until it is healed; and if you wish to cauterize this wound with the cauterizing iron called "cultellare", do so at the tip, and be careful not to cover the artery in this wound which is quite ancient.
de emigraine	of the wound
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat the wound as we have mentioned in the division of diseases, and it does not improve, and you see that the cauterizing iron before mentioned does not cause much pain and does not suffocate the patient, then it is necessary to extinguish the cauterizing iron called "cultellare" until it is cool; and then apply it to the wound along a line half an inch deep, and take your hand once, and avoid covering the artery and do not let it come close to the bone; and be careful of the jawbone that moves when it is moved, and the nerves should only have regard for the moving part and that spasms do not cause pain, and be careful of the bleeding from the artery when it is cut, or when it is cut, there will be great fear and immediately to that one who does not know and has not experienced; and leave the work in one way; but I will tell you how to stop the bleeding when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it appears in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	If you see that this fire cautery does not suffice for the disease, and the patient is suffering, apply the cautery to the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed; and if you see, administer the cautery that we have said in the chapter of extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two blades; and this fire cautery is better than that and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain of the ears from cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When the ear hurts from cold, and medicines have been applied and other treatments that we have said in the division, and the pain does not move, then warm this cautery called "poins", of which is the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After pointing all around the ear, where the pain is felt on both sides, and separating it slightly from the root of the ear until you have signified the ear is clear; then apply X points around each ear; after that, cure the ear as long as it is healthy.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture that must be treated by cauterization is only those that move from fluid, such as we have said in the divisions of diseases; and do not apply cauterization to similar things that come from excretion and spit of people.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this similar torture that moves from fluid of idros and excretions of the head and gargling, and it does not work, then it is necessary that you cauterize the pain with III cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and another a little further from the temple, and the third in the positioning of the II lips; and put the cauterie in the part that opens healthily, and the cauterie above a little bit away from the horn of the ear, and another in the temple as long as a little bit; and leave the cauterie as long as half of the skin is burned; and this is the form of the cauterie:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it is similar to the cauterizing knife that we have placed before, but it is a bit more subtle and requires that the knife be a bit thicker; after caring for the wound as I have described before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have described before, and it does not improve, and the pain does not have fever, then make four cauteries: two on each of the two horns of the head, and one in the middle of the head, and one on the part called "vasselz" as we have described before, and the back cauterize through the mouth of the stomach; and care for it as we have described before.
de litargie	For laziness
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this disease, it is recommended to give the patient large and modified brain pills; after removing the entire head of the disease, place the mustard plaster on the occipital region, which is written or treated with plasters; and this is the way of the fire cautery: if you do as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If he is thus healthy, it is good; and if not, make three fire cauterizations on the head in descending from the neck, and leave one inch of space between each cauterization; and the treatment is as with the others, and if you have seen it swell, and the pains are severe, make one cauterization in the middle; and if the profession is, two more on the two horns, and the treatment until he is healthy; and let the cauterizations called "olivare" be as I have already said.
de la froidor dou chief	of the cold of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary to clean the head of years and mucus that we have previously mentioned; after that, you should apply pressure to the head and each of the horns, and behind and three times on the spine of the neck; if you have more trouble, and the body is moist and the pain is severe, and the disease is not far, then you should apply four cauteries on the spine of the back; and let it remain until the most painful part is healed, and remove your hand; afterward, cure it as long as it is healthy, and the cauteries that are called "olivare" that we have previously mentioned.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Those who suffer from epilepsy should not use cauterization except for that which is fleshy, and it is first necessary to modify the brain of years and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division when the pains are large and severe with pain medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot bear the pain, give him gargarisms and mastication modifying the brain often with good meats; afterwards, relieve the head in the middle, and then apply cauterization as we have mentioned before, and cauterize on the vessel, and on each horn; and if the pains are outside and severe, apply cauterization as I have said to those who have paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauterization be done with olive oil in the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the pain is intense, then perform the following delicate cauterization method:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy, the excess or corrupted moisture and fluid is large, then use the following cautery made of parts as we have said for those who have paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to melancholy, the excess or corrupted moisture is declining towards melancholy, and the course of the bad pain is wet, then give it to drink something by which the brain is cleansed, according to what it is before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After removing the head of the bad pain; after making a well-made tortilla, like a circle, and placing it on the head; and if the pains are crossed, and held firmly from all parts; then present the liniment, and use old bearberry butter; and heat it gently in fire, so that the patient can bear it; after emptying the circle from inside into the head, and let it cool; and do this to the bad pain every week once with other good government until it is healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Where you have seen cauterization with making points all over the cauterizer.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This method of cauterizer moistens the skull greatly; then put on it soft cotton in butter and in green goose fat.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes'
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the eye comes firstly to the eyes by the signs that I have said in the division, then begin and give to the patient a remedy mundifying the head, and keep it from all moisture, and make it sweat or bathe it several times at fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After the patient commands to turn his head, and you make cauterizer into the head, and you make two cauterizers on the two temples simultaneously, or in one; and cover all the cauterizer with all the veins and the arteries that are outside the skull, and so be the cauterizer long according to the width of the temple; and keep from blood flowing, and if you see too much blood flowing, then stop it as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of veins and in the incision of the cauterization how you would perform it; and once done, never cauterize or sear the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	The path of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are above the veins or below the arteries that appear to be in the shape of the main body; and one sees that it is superfluous cold phlegm, then apply the cautery I mentioned at the beginning of this chapter: the first cauterization is applied to the forehead, and the second cauterization is applied to the two temples, and the third cauterization is applied outside the two bones; and if there is more, then apply the cautery gently above the eyebrows with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	through the courts of tears by through the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you medicine according to what we have said in the division, and it does not work, then drink a bad concoction of three herbs; after that, apply the head, and do cauterization or the middle of the cauterization of the oil lamp; and do two cauterizations of the cauterization called "clavilis" above the two sorciers, a little outside the chest; and beware of the artery that you do not cover it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cauterization called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the oil is softened by disease and moisture, then cauterize with this cauterization called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	For this reason, this is the shape:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see that it is necessary to apply two cautery irons above the two sorcis as long as the sorcis are; and do not leave your hand off except until the third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	the hairs that do not point the oil
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Never has it been seen that the hairs of the oil are converted to parchment, and prick at the oil, and it is made to cauterize in two ways: that is to say, by fire, or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they grow long and even, then place the hairs in your hand; afterwards, hold the eyelids steady with a figure that is as similar as possible to the shape of the eye, and start the sign below the hairs; then put cotton moistened in oil and musk on the eyelid, then heat the cauterizing iron:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing the figure a few times, as much as possible without burning the eye; and the sign of the health of the work is that you see the eyelid retreating, and the hairs raised to the point of the oil; then remove your hand, and leave it thus for three hours, then put cotton moistened in butter until the burn is healed; after treating with ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if afterwards the hairs come back, and the paper is softened, then restart the cauterization on that same spot, as you did before; and if the hairs are missing, then cauterize until the paper is raised to its natural place, and is even, and do not prick at the hair while it grows.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The fire cauterization of medicine is that you command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make a parchment in the shape of a mint leaf; then take French soap and live quartz, one of each, and grind them together well; and apply it hotly, so that it does not cool, then spread it on the shape you have made like the mint leaf, and put it on the eyes; and if the disease remains only in the eye, then open it, and do the same way; and put cotton moistened with oil behind the eye; and the one who has the disease should be in a healthy state and show the medicine above, and press the pouch and move it every time the patient feels the stinging of the medicine, for it feels like a burn.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then take the medicine to your mouth.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the burn is passed, raise the limb upwards, and check if you see the paper lifted as it was raised by constraint of fire or by incision; and if it is thus, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, then put the medicine back on top of the limb or where the medicine has not worked, until your work is equal, and your eyes are fixed; then put cotton moistened in water over it until the wound is cleaned, after which care for the limb that is called «dyafenis» and others, until they are healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you have the task to stay within your work, do so with great care, lest you not cut into the wrong parts of the medicine.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes thin after, and the hairs prick in the oil, then restart the medicine on the side that is softened properly with the paper, as you have done before; then cure it until it is healed; and this is the form of the fuel of the mire.
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And since the eyes of men are different in size and smallness, and according to what is your constraints; and do not be answered with the right way to that who is the study of this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	of the treatment of a fistula by fire cauterization
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have described in the division of diseases, and your treatments are not effective, then it is necessary to cauterize it in this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Command the patient to place his head in your safe hands; and hold the minister's head between your hands in this manner that it does not move, nor remove its head; afterwards put cotton moistened with wine or vinegar on the oil; afterwards heat the cauterizer which is next to the head: and it is fixed at the head as if it were a pen of vulture, similarly the other end of the cauterizer; if you see, so that it is appointed from one head to the other, and if you see, so that it is also like a tent; but whatever this which is fixed is worth for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula, it opens, and in its trail is pus and dirt; if it closes, open it again with a probe; after that, apply the cauterizing iron thoroughly, and hold your hand on the cauterizing iron at the part of the neck above the oil, so your hand does not burn; put the cauterizing iron in the grease of the oil, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cauterizing iron at the bone, that would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, if you have experience, and then let it for three days; after that, put cotton wool in butter, and the cure of the drying ointment until it is healed, and if forty days pass without it being healed, then put medicine corrosive acid until the bone is revealed; and the king according to what he would come in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a certain method of cauterizing a fistula that no one of the ancients mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	To the fistula, and make the hole; after put into the wound a thin piece of cloth of this shape:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And they make in the amount of a palm; and hold your hand firmly, and do not move the hairs until the plasters have fully set and not stick to their oil; and it is necessary to put above the hair cotton moistened in some water or milk: the plaster sets the bone and the wound with marvelous health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cauterization that we have mentioned, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then it is necessary to administer purgatives to the nose, and to bring the fistula back to its proper place in the nostril as it should be.
des crevaices en levres	cracked lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times there are cracks in the lips that are called "hair", and at the same time in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks as we have mentioned in the divisions, and the treatment does not help, then heat a small cauterizing iron in this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the patient in those positions until they can no longer bear it; then apply the clay bandage as long as it is necessary to heal.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the groin
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes at the root of the groin or in the thigh, or in the buttocks, or at the roots of the teeth, after it has been perforated and drained and has become fistula; and you cure it as we have said in divisions, and it does not improve: then it is necessary to apply cauterization according to the quantity of the fistula; afterwards, plug or puncture the fistula, and keep your hand on the spot until the iron comes to the end of the fistula, and behind the bone; and do this once or twice, after curing as we have said in cures, until it is healed; and if it is cured thus, it is good; and if not, then it is necessary to expose the limb and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat them with medicines but it does not work, then put the tip of a sharp instrument in front of the tooth; apply the cauterizer deeply and hold your hand steady so that the pain reaches the root of the tooth; then remove your hand and continue the cauterization as you wish; afterwards fill the gums with salt water, and let them rest for an hour and then repeat.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way, the tooth that was moving is confirmed, and the softened gums are held back, and the moisture is corrupted and dried up.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When the pain of the teeth comes from coldness, or there is coldness or wetness, and medical treatments do not work, then it is necessary to use cauterization according to two methods: cauterization with butter and cauterization with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cauterization with butter is such that you take butter from a freshly killed animal, and the end in an iron or tin spoon; afterwards take cotton and wrap it around the point of a tent, and moisten it in warm butter, and put it on the painful tooth firmly and hold it until it is cooled; and thus do often enough until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth, and if you see that moistened wool and cotton in warm butter is applied to the aching tooth, and put on the hot iron until the heat comes to the movement of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The fire cautery is such that you grasp a hot iron or brass instrument, and it should be large enough that the heat does not reach the mouth of the wound; after heating the cauterizer, from which the form will come out afterwards, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cauterizer is cooled; do this often, for the pain will be alleviated the same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the wound fill its mouth with good butter in the urgency of this cauterizer, and then remove it; and this is the form of the cauterizer:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make the fire cautery on the head wherever you want, according to what you have available; and it is in the form of a tongue:
des scrophules	of a tongue-shaped piece of wood.
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrophules are thin and cold, wet, and not obedient to digestion by medicines, then heat the fire cautery on the head with this form, and have two openings for the fumes to escape from the other side; and put the cautery hot above the abscess once, or as often as it comes to the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, put cautery according to the quantity of the abscess, and leave it for three days; and put on it soft cotton moistened in butter until the burn is healed; after that, care for the wound with ointments and bandages until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the jaw:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moisture overcomes the channels of the body, and especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then you must first clear the hairs by medicines that dissolve; after that, apply cauterization to the root of the neck, and be careful not to come too close to the throat, and do not burn too much but just a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, apply another cauterization to the joint of the collarbone and the top of the spine, and let the cauteries which are called "clavicles" because of how we have the shape in front; and treat the limb as we have described until it is healed.
de la toust	of the whole
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and disease of the womb are of cold moisture, and the pains have no fever or sweat, and is the ancient disease, then make two cauteries on the eyelids in their sight; and the other cautery goes between the breasts; and let the cauteries that are called «clavile» according to the form that is before said.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see, make cautery by holding the whole cauterizer that is called «poins» because of the form that is before in the disease of the ears; and let the points be just to thirty, or around.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After the treatment of the patient according to what has been said previously, and let the cauteries be applied at three points according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because the cauteries are lighter, because you make three times as many.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	After, shave the hairs above the back and on the side; then relieve the pain within the tenderness, as much as you can with your right hand; and if the joint is misaligned inside, then heat the cauteries which have two needles in this form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	And cauterize the wound until it pierces just at the coste, and bring four cauteries together with the cauterizing iron that has three points; and because of this, the cauterization is made with the cauterizing iron that has three points, for the reason that the four cauteries are like the shape of a tent, and it is the form of the cauterizing iron that has three points.
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And never place the cauterizing iron on this one nerve because it has eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After placing the cauterizing iron on it, break it with a string; after resting the injury, do not move the limbs for a long time until it is well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated above, that thing happens quickly, then make a cautery on the thick part of the cautery clavi, or many of cauteries in pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and it is healed by the moisture and is free from the pain.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When in the stomach come cold and much moisture until it reaches its condition, and they multiply the diarrhea to him, and are customary ways of cures and he does not improve, then it is necessary that the pain be supported on his back, and extends his legs and his hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	After the first application of three blisters on the comb's bad side due to its quantity, apply the entire cauterizing iron, and two blisters after the second ribs until the figure of the blisters is at three angles, and have equal space between them so that they are not joined together as they grow; and let the cauterizing iron be so sharp that it pierces both parts of the curvature, and let the figure of the blisters be in this form without twisting:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you see that the blister is being cauterized with a large cauterizing iron in the stomach according to this form, and if someone has fear of this cauterizing iron, cauterize by pricking and holding above the stomach at the point, then cauterize the entire cauterizing iron that is called "point".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the care of the care that we have had before, as long as they are healthy.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver comes with pain from heat and moisture and great swelling, as long as it is not removed from its natural condition by excess; and the hairs are cured of what we have said in divisions, and it does not help them much, so it is necessary that the hairs be raised above their natural position; and the sign of three cauteries according to this form and this figure and this quantity above the liver, deferring the hypochondres, where the bones of the stomach come; and there should be space between each cautery the width of one; and let the cauteries be long and straight, and do not press much with your hand all over the cauterie; and let the hairs lie down only on half of the body, and let the hairs be raised above their feet; and if it cannot, let it lie down and extend its legs, and raise its arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if you wish to cauterize these cautery tools with fire, if you are skilled and wise in the art, and that you do not burn everything at once, for you would make the whole body harder; and that it does not come up to boiling, for the tools are very delicate in that place, and the sages should see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When it has an abscess in the liver, and you see if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the mesh: if it is in the flesh, it does not cause much pain; and if it is in the mesh, it causes great pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And when this treatment is completed, it is necessary that the hairs be shaved over the patient's head; then the doctor should examine the wound or the abscess, and then heat the cauterizing iron which is similar to a thorn, because of this:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize the wound until the pus is gone, and it comes just to the surface, until the pore is completely closed; after the treatment according to the treatment of bandages as long as they are healed; and it is necessary that this cauterizing iron be used only by those who have studied medicine for a long time, and by whose hands these diseases have never been corrupted.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Therefore, it can be boldly attempted, and in all ways, it seems to me that it is worth leaving it.
dou cautere de pleuresin	fire cauterization
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The old said that one should perform fire cauterization with the roots of aristolochia, and in this manner: take a long root of aristolochia, the longest you can find, and dry it, and as large and long as your finger; and grind it into oil, and take the fire cautery, and cauterize between the eyebrow and the forehead, and two small cauteries a little down in the part that is outside the beard; and two cauteries between the fifth rib and the spine, declining back a little; and one cauterizes the least, and the other above the stomach, and one between the shoulder blades, and two on the sides of the least forward the cauterization that is between the shoulder blades; and do not press your hand, but do it openly as in smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And they said that no man uses fire cauterization similar to the razor, and they scrape it and put it between the ribs, until it comes to the abscess; and out it goes like the pain in the liver apostem.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work, there is fear or the pain kills now, or a fistula comes that cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse as we have said in the divisions of treatments, and it does not improve, then they resort to three methods of cauterization that are all good.
