Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	In this method, you should make three or four cauteries, or four, aligning them along the length of the wound, according to the shape of the heart cautery we have mentioned before; and do not press your hand on the entire cautery, and let the hairs be near its back; and another method of cauterization is that you heat the cautery that has two needles, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and relieve the curvature that is near the wound, or where the pain of the ear comes from the right side, and relieve the elevation according to the curve, according to the length of the body, and let the cautery be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After applying the two fingers, the skin should be pricked on the other side until it is perceived from that part, and then remove the cauterizing iron, and thus insert one and a half fingers. If you see, then cauterize the entire cautery with three fingers.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After treatment when he has had a fever for a long time, and it is worth trying the other remedies mentioned before.
de ydropisie	of hydrops
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cauterization is not useful for hydropsy, except in the manner called "ascletyes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat it according to the methods that we have mentioned in the divisions, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you make four cautery around the abdomen, and one above the stomach, and one above the liver, and one below the mouse, and two behind the back above the spine, and one at the worst place; and let the cautery be close to the source of the disease.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After the fire cautery is applied for relief of pain long and tightly, and do not leave the care of the wound after the cauterization; and healing would hasten, and together with God's help, the two intentions would be accomplished.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the fire cautery for the abdomen is the clamp that we have shown before; and for the back, it is an oil lamp, according to what is written above.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen to the one who is hydroptic, and they are plain of a yellowish hue, it is necessary that you cauterize above the foot between the auricular and the annular; and relieve your hand with the cautery towards returning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply, thus avoiding the yellowish parts, and let the cauteries be done according to this form:

de la menoison	of the bandage

de la cure des emorroydes	of the treatment of worms
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. de plaie mal curee	of a poorly treated wound

When any comes with a fistula, and it is inflamed and discharged putrid and corrupted moisture, then you must provide for the whole of a thin tent, and guard that you cleanse the tent as much as possible.

de la maladie des reins	of the disease of the kidneys

de la vessie	of the bladder

de la marris	of the marsh
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit. de la hainche	of the waist

When the viscous moisture descends to the waist, and for this reason it moves out of its place, and the signs are that one thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and it is found that the legs are twisted, therefore it is necessary to cauterize the pain above the waist with a cautery similar to a circle, and sign before the bone around the waist as it turns, so that the waist is inside the circle; and if it is such cauterizations as those that have been cauterized the stomach.

When pain comes in the back of the backbone, and it is from cold and moisture, and the hairs are cured of what we have said in the division and the care does not help, and the disease is ancient: then it is necessary to purge the hair of the large humors with fetid pills, or other good pills similar.

de la dolor dou dos	of the pain is doubled.

de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain of joints is from moisture that has spread to every member of the body, and when the pain comes in the feet, which they properly call "gout", and when it is a cold cause and medicines do not cure it, then it is cured by cauteries in this manner: apply much cautery around the joint, and let the cautery be made of oil in this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is a place that you can prick on the face of the foot, then let the cauterizing be done with the whole cautery called "needle".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come to the knees and other joints, and they often have it, then let the cauterizing be done with three or four cautery needles on each part of every side, with the whole cautery being olive; and if you have more skill, then do more, but do not hold your hand farther than the spirits of the patient's courage allow.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend just above the genitals and in the back, administer the cauterization that we have mentioned in our chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make points two lines wide; and if there is no pain at the wrists, make points over each joint and over the hair of the hand; and if the pains come just above the elbow or shoulder, cauterize each part, and give good governance to the patient and many medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give good governance and purge the humor, it will be healed by the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the toothache
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When toothache comes suddenly, and the bile descends to the groins, and it is not new, if you see that it needs treatment, that he does not move much that day; and that he uses things that relieve the stomach, so that the pain decreases from his belly; afterwards, make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his jaw as long as the bile has returned, and twist it to both sides, and press against the tooth above the bone of the little finger, and at every sign that is similar to half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery with this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until it is white and sweats scented drops.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then remove the pus from the joint; and the ministers taint their hands with it so that they do not return to it; and work well on the knees at the dislocation, and put some ointment and sergeant on the knees, and the other on the worst hand that taints their hands; then put the cautery on the sign all over your hand, and hold it straight and firm until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, start again with another one until you come close to the bone; and be careful that the pus does not escape when you are doing the cautery; that you do not burn it; and that by this way the dislocation does not kill, or other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And if you do not come to the bone with the cauterization, your work is worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And the cauterization of children should be subtle according to their size, and large people likewise according to their size; after three days, care for the wound with the cauterization of butter until the eschar is formed; after that, care for other inflammations as long as they are healed, and grind the hairs on their back for forty days until the wound is well closed; and it is necessary that their excretions be cleaned thoroughly, so that the sweat does not leak when they move around.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wishes to rise, let him apply a well-made bandage for ten more days; and have good rest, that he works little and avoids too much drinking and eating, and too much high breathing; and if he follows this instruction, he is completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will tell you about the cure after cutting into his chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they do not grow any more, then let him have the fire cautery according to its quantity, and let one-third of the healer be applied; after the cure according to what we have said; and none of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with the cautery at three angles according to this form.
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	1. But the first sign is the shoulder dropping and make a line across the width of the rent, and another below, and keep your hand on all the cauterizing iron.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	1. But the first cauteries are lighter and more painless.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	1. of ancient pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	1. When pain comes in any limb, whether to fall or to strike, and this pain lasts long, and the medical cure does not help, then it must be cauterized with the cauterizing iron called "poins", and the cauteries should be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and weakness and its strength and its position of twists and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If it is safe to apply the first cautery, it is well; if not, begin another cautery above the first one, for it is usually the case that it should be applied to the member that is closest, because it is necessary to apply the cauteries until the hairs are healed.
de meselerie	of cauterization
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	Cauterization is never used without great help, and simultaneously the disease that comes from the putrefaction of fluids and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	If you see that the cauterization is not curing the disease at the beginning, and if it has been cured according to what we have said in the division, and if it does not stay or remain, and if you doubt that the corruption will not spread throughout the whole body, then you must apply several cauteries: I on the forehead and bring the head forward, and the other towards the front at the end of the eyebrows; and II on the two horns, and I behind the ears; and leave your hand so that the cauterization comes close to the bone, and as long as the scabs do not come out so that the vapors of the large humors can issue forth; and then cauterize again according to what is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	If the injury is scattered throughout the body; and it is clearly evident, so you should cauterize with these cauteries that we have said or chief, and the cautery in the back of the neck, and two cauteries above the spine of the neck, and six cauteries above the spine of the back, and one great one above the buttocks and one other below, and two above the shoulders, and two above the elbows, and two above the knees, and one above each joint of the hands and feet, and above the wounds of the hands; and be careful of those that are behind calcifying, that you do not burn them; and never make a cauterization above the bone of the little finger, and one above the bone of the stomach, and one above the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And the more you do cauterization, the less you need to help, and it benefits him; and know that the wounds do not feel pain as the healthy ones do, because the body is already corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	It should be great and small according to the members and the joints, according to what you will find in the manner of irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treating the limb with flour several times with honey and other treatments until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When inflammation comes to any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and it is not healed, then you do cauterization on the member according to its size and smallness; and let the cauterization be a little inside the affected area; then treat the wounds until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And never done cauterization by hand and at the wrist and at the elbow, at the end of the nerve that moves the limb, and thus it is often ossified where it inflames; and in any case, no one interferes with it unless they are knowledgeable about the limbs and the issues of the nerves moving the body.
de albaras	I'm sorry, I don't understand your request
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is awakened, and medical treatment does not help, then cauterize it with a cautery a little in front, according to the quantity of the curd, until the bone is ossified and its color is restored. Then treat it with flour of wheat and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and of each one part; and mix them all together, and apply it to the wound, and bind it to the affected area for as long as it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of chancre by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When chancre appears at the beginning, and you see it stop growing, if you cauterize it with a cauterizer that seems like a circle, all around the edge of the chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And everyone says that one should also make the cauterizer in the middle of the chancre; and I do not think this is good, because I believe it should not be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have never seen it happen; and the more important thing is that it be cauterized around, with the cauterizer that is called "circle", as we have said in many cauterizers.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the withered who cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When anyone has a disease called "adubelati", and it lingers to die or due to the excess it causes or due to the age of the pain when they are old (that is, too old) and they have little blood, or due to the tension; and you see it hastening to die: then cauterize around with many small cauteries in pinching; afterwards leave it thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it piercing through the entire cauterization, then heat the cauterization from where it is formed:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of this disease called "adubelati" until the cauterizer has pierced through, and let the cauterizer be such that the hairs feel afterwards in a similar manner as the course of the porridge is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment until they are completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The treatment of fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another way of disease is called "corrodens", and it is nothing but a piece of member, for it twists the members as if the dry reeds would.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in the limb that can suffer cauterization along with fire, then heat the cauterizers clay very small and great, according to what is needed for the limb or the disease; after cauterizing all parts until you reach all the corruption, and nothing remains of it, so that all that is corrupted is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	Then leave it for three days, and apply a poultice of cauterized herbs on the wounds, suffering with oil until the burned skin is removed, and all corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of wounds, scars are generated.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that healthy scars do not arise, it is good; but if not, then begin the cauterization again on the part that remains corrupted.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this method has never been treated with medicine in the place of fire cauterization; but fire cauterization is always greater help, and I have already mentioned the treatment of medicine in the division: take it when you have occasion.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of the bones that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that the feet by deficiency give birth to a disease called "clubfoot" according to our understanding, and it is a great deformity that makes the foot look like a ball.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauteries for this disease are in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, fire cauterization, and needle cauterization with hot water.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cauterization is done by heating the cauterizer as if it were a pen of hot iron, and it should be made of good iron at the measure that it can penetrate the nail from all parts, and that it has thin margins; afterwards, place the whole hot on the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it comes to the root of the nail; and leave it thus for three days until it begins to rot; then make an ointment of wild herbs ground with silk, and leave the ointment all night, and the nail will fall off and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the wound by applying heat until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted by defilement of the body, and often in the hands and feet, it is necessary that you reapply the fire cautery of very hot; and in this way: take a needle of iron or steel, or a pen of quill, and place it over the nail and the cuticle, that is to say, the verucae; and place the needle over it so that it pierces all around, then put a drop of very hot water, and hold your hand well, and press your hand turning so that the edge of the needle comes to the root of the nail, and find the very hot water deep to the root; and let the pain of the very hot water for an hour; then leave it in this way, and it will all come out at its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Then do another one, until you have relieved all those who are in the body, then cure the wounds that cause harm to the heart.
li cure dou trembler	cure of the shaking
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When anyone shakes from the cold, or from a quarter-fever, or from another, it is necessary that you make four cauteries or four on the spine of the back; one cautery between each spine; and one at the waist, and one above the stomach at the olive cauterizing; it will allow the shaking, and hasten the healing from the disease of the cold.
des pustules puans	of stinking pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	No time appears when the body is bathed, or pustules appear that come from large corrupted matters.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If it is necessary when they appear that one make a cauterization above each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery of willow bark, of which the point should be held in the fire, or of the root of aristolochia long, or with the lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And no time should one cauterize them at the beginning when they appear, in this manner, and it cannot grow more, but is destroyed by the excess from which they come, and are healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often, there is great bleeding from the cut artery at the wound that comes to the surface, or at the incision of the abscess, or in the cauterization of the limb, and similar things; and it is a very painful thing to stop.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And whenever this happens to anyone, quickly place your second finger on the wound of the vein, and press very tightly until the blood stops flowing from your finger, and there is no more blood; then put the cauteries of olive oil in the fire several times, both small and large, until they are all red; then take I, or a great or small one according to the wound and the limb in which the artery is located, and place the cauteries on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cauteries there until the bleeding stops.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if the first one suddenly breaks while you are lifting it above the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, then quickly take the other cautery that is in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing this one after the other until the bleeding is stopped; and be careful that you do not burn the nerve that is next to it, and that no other harm comes from the wound; and see that when the artery is not cut, it cannot be extinguished directly when the artery is large, unless by one of the four methods that we have said: or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not yet treated, or by a strong thread, or by medicines placed on it that have power to stop blood; and it must be tied and held firmly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever administers tight bandaging of cloth or other things burning above, or similar things, does not benefit unless not.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and he does not have any remedy present, then he should place his finger index above the wound of the vein as we have said, and tightly bandage as much as possible until it is stopped above the wound and above the vein; and he should not move it, but he should frequently moisten with cold water often that it is very cold until the flesh is frozen and swollen and stopped.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This begins the second book of remedies for tails
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter of all diseases where it is necessary to cauterize with fire or burning medicine, and the patients and causes and instruments and forms of cauteries; and I will put this chapter at the beginning of the book of the foot, and I will go to this chapter by this same way because one finds more easily what one wants.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And therefore when I begin this chapter, it is necessary, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and for this reason it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you should not undertake foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many methods of people come to healing.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	If they come from such people who have become so with their disease that they die suddenly because of the harm they receive from their disease, and because of the greatness of their wickedness; and of these one should fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And of these there are those who give you their sense, and say: "Wait, I am in pain"; and the illness is spiteful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It does not matter only to those who come to you who have this way, but put greater caution in your honor than in your desire, and do not open foolishly but wisely of what you are certain, and which you have taken and lost; and use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your ailments for health to be converted; and this will help you to achieve good reputation, glory, and memory for a long time.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, Our Lords give you good understanding and truth, and if you wish to breathe from the holy inspiration of his hand, indeed.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	I have ordered you to write this chapter by examining other chapters, according to what is before the chapter on cauteries, which I have previously described from head to foot, so that you may find it more easily.
dou chief plein d’aigue	full of sharp
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	This disease often occurs in children at birth, and when the child's head is held too tightly; and sometimes it comes from a reason that is not known.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	I have never seen this disease except in children, and all those that I have seen died; and because it seems to me that it is better to avoid this work in such treatments.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	I saw a child who was in pain from a sharp object, and the head was swelling each day until it could not be supported; and it died of the moisture, and this moisture is assembled outside the bone above the sinus, between the skin and the bone; and the procedures are such that if the moisture is between the skin and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you should make a wide incision in the head; and it should be as long as twice the width of the sinus, until the moisture flows out; and take the shape of the space:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more extensive, and the abscess is larger, make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and the signs that you see are the commissures of the jaw opened from each part, and the sharp pain when you press it with your hand inside, and it does not return to you: then you must make three cuts in the jaw like this:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, remove all the moisture.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After applying dressings and powders, and putting in wine and oil, and leaving it like this for five days; then remove it, and treat the wound with bandages and counter-irritants, and keep the jaw straight, and gradually give dry food with a little moisture until the member is comfortable and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look for the largest opening of the abscess, and the gathering of the sharp edge; for it is never before, never behind, never on the right, and never on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Then cut where the abscess is open, and fill it with the sharp edge, and make the incision according to what you can do; and be careful not to cover the artery; and if there is blood flow, so that the hairs die from the corruption of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	I'm sorry, I don't understand
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When it happens to someone with a disease called "cataract" in the eyes or the pupil, and the disease is ancient, and medical treatment does not help much, then the cure is to cauterize with what covers the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is therefore necessary, while you view the wound, that the hairs make their head; afterward, rub the shoulder with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then hold the hairs back against the cloth; then look where the vein is bleeding, and the veins on both sides are behind the ears, and they are not returned; then sign the veins to close, then cover both with a piece of lint soaked in two parts, until the wound comes just above the bone, and it should be through the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, press the lint away from the artery and cover it above, cutting as much as it should be through the middle.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, the blood spurts continuously outwards.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open at first feeling, you should measure the amount of space between three fingers, then insert it into the bone; and what is needed to put in the abscess is six drops, and perhaps a little more or less depending on how much the pain can bear, and the refilling of the artery. Then look at the wound: if it remains above the bone pointedly, if the suture that we have put does not come out, then strain the wound and tie it, and the treatment of ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	Of the head
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When an ancient headache comes, and the catarrh is sharp, due to the moisture of tears and chills in the temples and old age and similar things, and it is treated with methods of medical cures and nothing seems to help, then we should cauterize the arteries of the temples, as we have said.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of their extraction is that the hairs of his temples face backwards, and understand to the artery that opens in the temple, because it opens well by its beating, and it is only restored after in any men who are too cold; and if it is restored, then strain the skin with some cloths, then rub the leather with some rough cloth, and boil the leather until the artery clearly appears; then take the spatula of which this is the shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then gently scrape the skin until you reach the artery, then cut it at the top with pincers, and remove all the threads that are stuck to each part; and if the artery is thin, turn it to the point of the needle, then cover that part according to the amount of the two wounds.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not covered, it will not heal completely.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out blood from the sixth day, up to the third; and if the artery is large, it is necessary to tie it in two turns of a strong silk thread, which does not allow any blood to come before the wound heals, and does not cause any discharge of blood; then cover the excess that is between the two threads in the same hour, and then, if you see, cauterize the wound with a cauterizing iron up to the bone as long as the wounds are covered; and this is the best work, if the wounds do not have fever and he is of hot constitution.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the fire cautery is to finish the moistures: because it is of greater help against moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For the extraction of arteries, it is necessary to fill the limb with old cotton and place wool bandages on top; and when they are removed, be careful of dry medicines that make charcoal and bandages until they are healed; and if without court of the artery as you work, so hurry to cover it with a cauterizer, or fill the limb with vinegar and strain it in your hand that the wound is not frozen; and if you do not have this present, place ice on the limb until the wound is frozen, and raise the limb with cold water until it is frozen, and be careful to keep it frozen; and what is more difficult and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein with a cautery of II parts, but the cutting should be well spaced to last longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	When the instruments are too tight, it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the two knives a large space, and then when you have marked the two lines, and you melt the iron hot until it comes just short of the bone, and cover the vein in two lines; and they should be separated between the two cuts because it is not safe to do all of this cauterization at once; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are flowing down the veins that are above the top of the chief of the forehead, and it does not help the cure of medicine that we make, and you see the face of the patient becoming twisted, and feels like a trembling; and they are held and moistened so much that the hair of the papers is soaked, and the papers are wrinkled, and burned by the heat of the tears, if there is need for this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called the old "wound healer," and you should make three cuts or front equally according to the length of the front; and one of the cuts as two totally above the jaw, and the others two at two ribs above the papers, and be careful not to incise the arteries that are at two ribs above the papers; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two mandibles, and each wound the quantity of three drops through the joins; and have equipped a piece of sponge and much cloth for sucking the blood, then boil the sponge in two parts of which this is the form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the first incision to the second; scrape off all the flesh that is between the two cuts from the top of the cheek to the gum, then make another cut from the other side of the same incision to the second; then extract this spatulable matter.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you insert the tool called "cultellaire" into the first cut, it is very sharp on one side and blunt on the other, and its shape is:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the sharp edge of the tool towards the cheek and the blunt side towards the bone, and push it until it reaches the other cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And for all the vessels that descend from the chief as far as the eyes, continue the incision until the wound is open enough to see through it, then make another cut in the same place on the other side; then extract the arrow evenly, and express the blood for the arrow taken; then put a piece of old cloth in each cut, and put moistened cloths with wine and oil and vinegar on top, and ensure that abscesses do not come; then remove the bandage, and apply a great amount of ground ivy, then treat the wound with basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other cures for treating wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	repetition of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When anyone comes to have a fire cauterization done as usual, and you see the eyes closed and small, and weakened vision, and burnt papers; and the hairs are shaved, and where the shaving is done, there is great pain, and the hairs are discharged; therefore, by these accidents that those matters and that cautery come from is only from many wounds, and the healing that is, if this is.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you command the patient to turn his head back, then make a deep cut across the forehead, and another one wide at the top of the nose.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	Starting from the right temple wound to the left temple, and make the incision just above the bone; and keep your hand away from the temples that move at the joint; and when the bone is exposed, soak up all the blood with an sponge, then clean between the two bones of the wound and put in old cotton, and then tent with linen; then bind it with softened cloth mixed with wine and oil, and guard against abscess forming; when it is removed, it is necessary to rub the bone until charcoal begins to form, then care for things that are cauterized, which are done by burning.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of flour, and make a poultice; and administer it in these wounds to pour in oil through all.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the disorientation of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that which enters the ears is one of the four things: grains, or thorns, or stone from the mine or similar thing like iron; or seeds, such as beans, peas, and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it enters the ear as a stone or other thing that does not fit well in the ear, it does not grow in the ear, so put the ear to the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the arrow, if it is possible to drop a little bit of purple oil or hemp oil, then apply extraction; and this method causes vomiting of condition, and when the patient sneezes, cover the nose with pieces of cloth or wool; and place the ear above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often vomiting comes from this method; and if it does not come, then apply extraction with small pins, of which this is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it vomits with the pins, it is good; if not, then apply extraction with a thin needle of small doubled-up thread; and if it does not vomit by this method, make a rain candle and blow into the head of the candle or the hollow of the ear very strongly so that the wax cannot enter with the candle; then remove it formally, for often vomiting comes as we have said; and if it does not vomit in this way, take some cloth of which they take the ears, and put any instrument that is sharp for this purpose, and put a little cotton around; then press the cloth on the arrow or whatever else, and remove it.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If she does not jump from all these things that we have said, then quickly cut the ear as soon as the abscess is full and bleeding, and spasms; and the way of the cut is that you first make a small incision into the malignancy of the cephalic, and extract the pus according to the measure of its virtue, then place the malignancy between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear where the grease depends; and let the cut be as a moon, until you come to the bone, then remove it according to your power, and suck it vigorously to your mouth; and the cure as long as they are healthy.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is small grains that are present and they swell, administer extraction; and if it cannot exit, administer the subtle spume according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and administer incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not make a mistake when you think the grains are moist due to earwax, until you have made many pieces; then extract with fine forceps and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the ear therefore that is blocked, it is appropriate to use the blowing of the nose of the condition first, and widen the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let it lie flat across the ear itself or where the sharp pain is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps out due to the sky, it's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, take many small stones according to the length of your finger and lightly, and heat them in the fire; and put the hairs of the ear, or a sprig of herb from another part, and one stone on top of the stone that is in the ear; and do not stop putting the stones on top of each other until the sharp pain is all gone, and thus it will all be gone; and if you see, take the twig, and lightly touch one of the ears, and the other take from the fire until the least twig is burned; then do the same with other twigs until the sharp pain is all gone, as we have said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of an animal, if it is of small size, such as a mouse and similar things, handle it as we have said in the division; but if it is of large size, where one can feel it, then facilitate extraction with pincers; and it is the lighter thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When extracting worms from the ears, if you treat them as we have said in the division and where treating distillations, and the treatment does not help, then it is necessary to look at the ear in the sunlight: if there are no worms, then remove them with subtle pincers, and if they do not come out, take the form of a hook from which this is.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And apply a more subtle blow to the head in the ear according to the amount of pain, then it is often effective for all the pain; do this often until they all disappear.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey to issue, then strike around the head with cotton as I have said in the stone; and if they do not sail as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proven effective in the opening of wounds, and you will find them where treating distillations; and if you distil your oils and medicines into the ear with this instrument, of which this is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And if it is made of silver or tin, it should be narrow at the small holes and wide above to drip; and to press during distillation with a well-made tin tool for this, and if you see take the razor and wrap it around the point evenly with cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicine you see in the basin, and the bowl should be in the ear; then squeeze through the razor all the cotton, and press your hand temperately until the oil is distilled or the steam from the ear; and the bad smells inside, and the distillation should be a little warm at the fire as it is distilled in the ear; and guard that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of ear obstruction
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without some kind of obstruction in the ears; and this same thing happens to men due to ear obstruction from a wound, or from a foreign body inside the ear, and this obstruction never comes from outside the ear, unless one cannot see it; and it always comes from something inside the ear, and one can see it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, if one cannot see it, it comes from great inflammation in many positions, and in this case where one can see, it is necessary to put the ear in bad position towards the sun; and look inside: if you see the obstruction apparent, if the opening has all this space of which there is the form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let the mouth be cleaned from front to back, so that it does not bleed the ear; if the wound is in the flesh or bone of the ear, then hold it with fine pincers and cover it lightly, until that char is completely healed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the wound is in the front of the ear, take a fine knife and lightly heat it over the fire, then place it on the bone of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the wound that causes pain in the ear to be gritty, lightly pierce it, and make sure not to damage the nerves of the ear; then place a tent according to the width of the pore in the ear, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do not perform any action until the wound is healed, or take a tent and moisten it with rose petals, and powder over it with broken glass; and if you see swelling in the ear, then it is appropriate to remove the tent and move another tent made of rose petal oil and wax, until the swelling is removed; then cure it as long as it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if there is a flow of blood, dip an sponge and wrap it in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other treatments that remove the blood flow which are used to treat distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the char of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is the method that comes from papers of arrows when they are wet and are dry, if it is necessary to extend them with tongs and pincers, and the root of a spatula of its roots; then put on the limb vinegar broken.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without decortication, then cauterize with a fine lens caustic, and the cauterizer after the incision is good for muscles; and often they recur, nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the gravel
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Frequently, papers come from the eyes things that seem gravelly in their form and hardness, and for this disease is called "hail", and is an assembly of large moisture above and below; the work is such: if the hail moves from one part to another, and it is a light thing to know; then make it wide, then scrape each part lightly, then take it with pincers, and wrap.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you do not cover it with a thin layer of paper, it does not hurt the patient; and if the wound is large, it gathers at a seam, and the cure until it is healed; and if it is small, do not force it, for the wounds quickly return and inflame.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the splinter is descending into the depths of the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper, and extend the splinter to some pins, and hold and press on both sides; and if the paper is moved by incision, it causes no harm; and when the splinter is cut, pour oil of strong salt, and heal the wound with what is soothing until the wounds are cleansed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that is smeared on strips of paper above, and it has more use in children than in adults, and it hurts their eyes, and they have diarrhea in the morning, and they cannot look at the light of the sun because their tears gather in their eyes; and because they lie on their faces, they are covered with moist paper that swells and appears to cover the exinach that opens in the oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the limb to its place and feel the bone slipping between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of the operation is such that the bones put their head in your hand; then take a strip of linen, and make a tent in the shape of a circle according to the amount that contains the slipping of each part, then place it on top of it; and press from one side and the other, so that the slipping is assembled inside the circle; then cutting in the middle of the moisture at the spatula a wide groove, and not be more than the size of the wound made on the vein; and cutting the skin to the bones until you come to the slipping; and in many positions of the slipping, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
