Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Remove the entire piece of cloth between your two hands, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread out; and be careful not to stick in the wound, that you do not come to the whole length of the oil, that you do not hurt it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if it does not open at the beginning of the wound, slightly scrape the wound until it opens; then spread it out as we have said, then wipe the cloth gently and sharply, and put it on the limb, and spread it well.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who break the cloth and put it on to corrupt the moisture that remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the healer as long as they are healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the abscess that is swollen, then the healer should apply wet compresses until they are healthy.
des poilz des papieres	of hairs of papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs of papers are born other than their nature, and are awake, they harm the eyes, and bring on diseases as if tears accustomed and softening of papers and albumen, until it is the cause of the destruction of the eyes; and the cure is according to four methods: either by cauterization with fire, or by medicine boiled according to what is before or in the chapter of cauterization, and is done either by incision and stitching or by cauterizing, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary to place the head of the hurtful (harmful) thing in your hand, then return the paper of oil to your right hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, if there is a needle at the end of all the thread above; and so that it is on the other side of the margin of the paper where the hairs grow between these hairs, and draw the thread above the whole paper, and return to the razor; then in the part outside the paper, outside the hairs arranged, covering everything from the great leg to the little one; then draw the thread, and place outside the paper a small cotton and cloth tent, then above the paper a figure of a cup, as the belly of a gourd, and all at once it is necessary that the figure be according to the amount that you saw raise the paper which is divided to all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	If the patient has skill in handling great quantities of paper according to how the paper is softened; then make all the space above the two lines that you have marked, and begin from the great leg down to small; and so be one of the tears near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then bore the needle into one of the two angles of the curved part, then scrape off the skin; then bring together the two lips at a seam of an needle all along the thin thread of silk, and squeeze out the blood, and dry the excess hairs above the two edges to any things gluing, if you see that it is done; and if not, if you have no care, then leave the seam and the threads for three or four days; then treat the wound with drying and constricting things, because the paper revives at the moment of the wound and its assembly, but the seam is loosened (as they say of the ancients), and it is work without fear; and if in another way: and that you sign the paper in a figure that is as alike as the foot of the martyr, as we have said, at three holes according to the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cover the wound with a bandage evenly according to the form that is there:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the needles, and the thing is not even, take a needle or it has a thread, and put the thread in the shape; and put the other thread over the big arm, and the second thread over the small one, and gather the threads evenly between your fingers; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin where you have sewn, as we have told you, then gather the two lips of the wound by stitching, and treat it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with plaster and similar soothing ointments; and never once has the hair of the paper been converted: if you should use what we have said about the incision, but stitching on one side and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The care of the dogs is as follows: and it is that you convert the paper and the paint inside according to what I have said, and then make two dogs by art, and two subtle leashes as long as the paper and the width of the space is; and hold the two threads in the two parts where you hold the threads; then bring them together subtly above the paper of the oil, and stretch the two dogs from the two parts formed; and leave it in this way for some time, and the skin that was stretched will die and rot and putrefy, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it lingers, if the copper has too much force, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound has been soothed, and if it has been lifted off the paper, and they will not grow back; and this is the form of the two cauldrons that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you grasp a thin needle, and beat the silk thread softly and thinly; then assemble the heads and one and the other thinly, and let the length of the threads be a palm long; then order the other thin silk thread briefly in the trap, and do not pull the heads of the thread; then put the hairs on your skin; and so it is beyond the sun so that the work is declined, for it is a thin and small work, then beat the needle through the whole trap at the root of the hair raised, and push it into the paper firmly until you pull it over the natural hair; then pull the hair up to the trap, and push in the trap that hair, if there is one or two or three or more; then pull your hand so that the hairs come out over the whole trap with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hunt is treated and the hair does not come out with it, then treat the hunt with the oil as you have ordered, until the hunt becomes very thin and you can see it through the oil; then apply the oil and let it sit for two or three days, until the hair grows back in its place and grows on top; and if the hair is small, then accompany it with a long hair from the goats naturally, and raise it with that one until it is lengthened and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the purity of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease, which is called "alecateri" or the putrefaction, comes from within the body, there are two methods: one natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it occurs by a wound, or a cut, or cauterization, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of treatment is to remove that suture, and dry the lips of the wound, and place within tents of linen, and bind it until it is healed; and one should only use in its cure things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the disease becomes worse than before; but work with things that are softening, such as fenugreek; and the rose of vinegar or altee and seeds of linseed boiled, and ointments of quicksilver melted in any of the oils, and there wrap a tent, and cure it.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your care are that you take heed that it does not sound as it did before; and this work that we have said is only to direct you concerning this disease, that it does not return as it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the oil which comes in the jar
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is dislocated, which truly is called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accidental comes from wound and cutting and cauterization and things similar; and the way of the work is that you hold an needle, in which it has the thread double, and the suture in the jar, and make it perforate from the left leg to the right, so that the thread comes out in the second joint of the jar; then the jar is placed above the entire needle, and the cope at a span wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the paper's shape returns according to what it should be, it is good; if not, take the razor and put it in the incision, and turn the paper, and make two cuts inside the paper; and let the ones who have the two cuts of the angles of the incision you have made, and make an angle so that when they are assembled, the shape is as if it were a letter with no «I griech»; then take that char, according to the quantity that its cost is away from, of what is taught by the paper, then add the two parts that are missing, and the cure of the medicines that make it soft, and tents, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the illness comes from a cut or stitch or cauterization, it is necessary to make a plain slit between the hairs and papers, according to what has been said before; then cleanse between the two layers of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters apply various methods to all sorts of power so that they can bring the figure back to its natural shape; and the patients themselves, according to what is necessary for the work and instruments in many different positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture has been done by many people in a somewhat manner that the paper above is soaked with the white of the oil, and cannot move or do its work naturally, then it is necessary to go outside the paper with the point of a razor, and lift it up; and extend it with pincers, until you cut off what is hard at the subtle spatula, which should not be too sharp nor too thin, so that the pain cannot suffer that the spatula is too sharp and does not burn the oil; and let your incision, from which you scrape that assembly, lightly, so that the paper returns to its natural form; and that whole assembly is healed, and never put in vinegar acid oil, and lift with vinegar water, and collodion; then place between the paper and the oil a linen cloth, and place above the oil moistened wool in abundance of urine; and after the joint uses collodion and other remedies until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the elbow of the oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	There are two ways in which the elbow is: one is nervous and similar to a hard, rough surface, and another that is not nervous, but similar to frozen white moisture, so that when touched with iron and heated with pincers, it cannot be moved; and both begin near the great arm and grow little by little until they cover the whole eye and the light and movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the way of the incision is that the hairs put their head in your hand, then the work the eyes; and hold the paper in your hand, then bend the elbow with pincers of little doubled, and extend it above; then take a needle, and put the hair of a horse, or a cow, or a cow, and the thread strongly; and double the point of the needle a little and stick it in the elbow, and push the needle through the whole needle, and tie the elbow with a thread and extend it above, and scrape all the hair on the side of the elbow that points to the pearl and the silk to the hair just below, then cut the remaining at the root of the arm with very subtle and small forces, and leave the natural flesh of the arm, so that by the incision the usual tears do not come out; and once it has been extended only once, and at the thread, as we have said; then scrape all the soft tissue of which this is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the spatula does not touch the gristle and break it, and that the pumice is not perceived; and after the incision pour a little bit of broken silk thread oil, and a collar made of litharge, and leave it just above the other side; then care for the wound as it needs to be until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the joint is not very sensitive, and you cannot insert the needle, and the incisions cannot enter, many times this appearance of a joint in medicine; and they are born as I have said in the division, and if you see it covered, then work the oil of the pain, and take the spatula lightly sharp according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And gently rub the angle above subtly, and if you see that it does not ease and the reason is close, then pour from your mouth into the oil collier made of litharge and red collier and beaten silk, and dampen the oil just above the other side; then proceed with the other work according to this same method until it is completely open.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary in the oil, as with an abscess, then milk, and cure first the abscess until it is healed, then proceed with the work as before until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh on the arm is black due to great harm, then soak it in oil at night, and apply a part of it and not all at once, until tears do not come; then pour in the oil, red wine which is made of litargire.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that comes out above the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Some men's flesh never comes out red, and covers the pupil and is rolled up on papers and turned back, and it looks like a balauste rose; and the work is that the hairs put their head in your clean, then work the eulz, and cope all that char with concave shapes to the eye, and support it with force; then cover the first char, and go all scraping to the razor just at the end, and guard that you do not bleach the oil at the work; and let the incision of the spanworm that we have said in the incision of the nail and as small forces of because we take the previous, like the form after this chapter demonstrates; and when the incision is accomplished and all the char is taken, then use the oil of silk broken or you distill red wine and similar corrosive medicines, and put on the oil behind cotton with abin of oil, so that it is assured of aposteme chaut; and if nothing remains, and the skin does not cover, and you doubt aposteme chaut, then leave the oil and cure the aposteme with things calming aposteme chaut; then return to your work until it is healed, and thus make many chars are treated in the oil by this similarity.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, it is necessary that you apply care to each of the weaknesses of the natural way; and of the accidental way, in the work of iron; and do not put your hand into any of these works until you see that this member is suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	red veins that are covered over the eye, and they harm the view and weaken the eye always.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	The work is therefore to the first that you look at this eye, in which these veins are, and outside, and there is no other disease besides these; then the work in this way: command the evil that it put its head in your healthy, then suspend those veins all around according to its wisdom, and let the edges be subtle double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And they should be done twice a day, gradually increasing in intensity according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then apply those forces gradually, and massage the blood clot an hour after another, until you can remove those forces from the oil; and be careful not to pierce the oil with points of the spatulas, and do this work at noon in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not cope with those forces; and when you have done this, then pour green and red wine vinegar into the oil to corrupt what is remaining.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot collect all the blood in that hour, then apply a plaster on top of the oil with things to ease the pain of the eyes, and let it rest for some time until the pain is eased and you are sure there is no abscess, then start again according to this method as long as they are healed; and this is the form of the forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the oil fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mirror calls this "arissati" fistula: when you treat it with cauterization and medicine as I have previously mentioned, and it is not healed, then it is engaged in what you did above the abscess, where it should die, and remove all the moisture that is there, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and blackness, then form all the instruments with which this is made; it is called "rough head", and it should be made of iron from the same head, and it should not be pointed as a lime if it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place the broken bone above the joint, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand slightly until you feel that the corruption is removed; and do this once, then restore the bone with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the bone is not sound, and the flesh is new, and the body of the wound is sound, it remains thus for forty days, and it does not return and is not inflamed, and no bad accident happens to it until it is healed; if so, there is no other remedy than to bring the fistula to the opening of the neck according to this form: and you should uncover the bone the second time with a knife, and with wet medicines, and when it is uncovered, take the forehead according to this form, and let the chosen one be at three angles, and let the fistula be attenuated just to the top as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it above the bone of the arm, and keep your hand away from the oil for a moment, then return to the full extent of the arm until it pierces the bone and the patient feels the pain because if he holds his hand above his neck; and since the dry medicines have been restored as I have indicated, and when the char is born and hardens the bones, then the matter goes to the neck; this is a lighter thing for the pain.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the end of the oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes open wide and all together, and it does not disturb the neck, nor is it unpleasant, then you must bind the pain; then cleanse, then apply bandages or haterel without causing injury to draw out the pus, then place above the oil a mixture of acid, aloe, incense, and sarcocollis, and then strain the oil, and apply the plaster with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths that are sufficiently moist, and double each in four, and then place one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eyes had in hand; then strain it through a cloth that is quite firm, and then start the bandages again without causing injury; then remove the bandages and leave the oil strained day and night, and if the eyes are not restored, it is good; if not, then restart the plaster and the cloths and the mixture and the bandages until they are healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	The breaking of a silk cloth
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions come to the silk cloth, then open, and it comes from a strong paper like a grain of resin, and it is easily seen; therefore, if you see it covered, the work is such that you should stick a needle at the root of the part below this above, then stick another needle or there is a double thread of the arm part; and let it pierce, and leave the first needle according to the arrangement; then cover the thread of the double thread around the affected part, and hold it well, then remove the needle and put the oily balm on the wound in abundance of honey; and let it stay until the thread cuts with the wound, then care for the oil of things comforting until the wound is healed; and never the wound is restrained by the bandage from each part of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes appear greatly swollen, pierce them with a thin needle that comes from the front of the oil, and draw out the moisture and wipe the eyelids, and enter thus immediately; then extract it as much as it is healthy.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the front of the oil
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing other than a drop that is assembled in the oil, resembling a sharp descent, and it is not a sharp one; and the manner of its appearance is such that you make the patient sit with the sick side leaning and straight, then take the head between your hands from both sides, and move the muffle as much as you see the drop coming up to your eyes; then it should be fished, and not wiped and dissolved, and the light should be seen, and you will see the things as they were; and if it does not descend, although it is sharp, and if the things that are dissolved from the drop are not aligned as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you place the painful part between your hands, then take the thin spatula and make it over the cornea of the eye and gently with the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea and the eyelid, until the bow is released; and when it is released, then pour hot honey mixed with honey or mustard boiled and honey, then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the hot oils
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have experienced similar things in the division, and what is necessary to pierce; if it works according to the health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary for you to place the hurt part between your hands crossed, outside of the light by the sun, and with clean oil pressed very tightly; then put the paper of oil in your right hand if the eyes are on the left, or in your left hand if the eyes are on the right; then take in your right hand if the eyes are on the left, the instrument called «almagda», or in your left hand if the eyes are on the right; then place the point of the instrument above the thick part of the oil in the hollow of the arm, then strike the instrument called «almagda» virtuously, and withdraw your hand as long as it pierces into the hollow of the oil, and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the way almagda be at the front of the measure of the space which is from the gold to the end of the needle; and this is the crown of the oil; if you see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the cloth, and then put the instrument above it or where the sharp is, then express it out one way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	if he is now sharp-sighted, then he sees the hairs in front of him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a little while, and if he becomes sharp-sighted again, put the fluid with the instrument, and when it is well mixed and does not rise, gently turn your hand back and forth; then place a small amount of silk gem in his eye and remove it from within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put in its place the oil steeped or ground with rose oil and an abundance of honey, and bind it with clean oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our time, put on it with an abundance of honey.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the arrowhead cannot enter the oil due to its hardness, because there are some men who have very hard eyes, it is necessary that you use the tool called "alberit", of which this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	Therefore pierce only the conjunctive part, and do not move it too much in front, but make the eye subtle, then push the arrowhead, as we have said; and at the end of the work compare the patient to sleeping on his back in the dark room; and move all movements, take light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and tie him according to his disposition towards the night; then release him in the same dark house, and check his vision, and see some things, and then return the bandage for seven days; and it is not necessary that you do this in the morning of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you elevate the eye, because the sharp pain comes quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When abscesses come, you should open the oil in front of the seventh hour, and let it be mixed with what alleviates abscesses; and when it is calmed, then remove the veil and put it on its face again, to cover any day, and let it stay in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then gradually leave the house a little and a little, and turn into its case; and cut that no disciple should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	Some came to us who was in the Yericho, who told us that in some countries they do all kinds of perceptions, where the acute is succeeded by everything, but I have never seen any in our land, nor have I read it in books of the ancients; and perhaps this is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the similarities of the forms of almsgiving, because those who do not know them see them; and they are properly of silver.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And they are the heads of those from this same subtlety, and the others in three angles awake.
de la char sor le neis	of the headache for the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Never are born or nose headaches of various kinds, because there are some that seem like scorpions at the tip of the nose; and if there are such ones, or if there is a headache of a good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that case of those headaches which are a nose, and not increased, it is necessary that you make the pain between your hands against the sun; and work its nostrils, and pour the onyx to those headaches, and remove them; because it is appropriate that you can bear the subtle sharpness of one part, until you know that that headache is entirely gone.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains nothing that can be covered, then open it with all the subtle and delicate instruments, until nothing remains; and if it is an abscess, wipe it clean as it should be; and if it is malignant abscesses, hurry and cauterize it until the wound is no longer wet and all the pus is removed. Then pour or pour out vinegar and hot water.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	And if it does not bleed, and moisture enters the palace, since it is safe; and if moisture does not pierce as it should, since there is bone underneath the bone, to which the instruments do not come to cut: therefore you must go with a thin thread of linen, and be careful not to touch the skin, and leave a space between each thread of about an inch or more; and put the bad parts of the thread in the wound through the nose, and pull it out as it comes out through the nostrils; and many times they do this with children in schools, and it is an easy thing for those who want to do it; then hold the head that comes out through the nostrils with one hand, and the other head that comes out through the mouth with the other hand, and hold them as we are who are or thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you see that the hairs have not been corrupted by the char, then remove the child, stop the bleeding, and wipe the blood with an Egyptian cotton swab, and put it back in its place as before; do this three times or more, until the swabs corrode all that remains of the char; then put on the nose a piece of plaster for several days until it is healed, and if it needs medicated ointments, use them; and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, with which one distills oils and medicines onto the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or bronze, resembling an open lantern, like a cat, and conduct it thus; and if you see, make a closed cat, and let the instruments plain for purging the head; and have one hand at the head to hold when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	for the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease arises from the nose called "telul", and it grows and becomes large, looking like a thing; and because of this, you should cover it at the beginning, and remove all of it, then put the fire cautery or burning medicine on the spot; and if it is slow to cover, take note if it is hard, of poor color, of poor sensation: if not touch it with iron because it is a hidden abscess, for when you cover it once, great mischief comes to the pain; and if the abscess is softly touched, not of poor color, and you see that you can completely cover it, then remove the pain and the cover without fear, and cure the other things that are similar and restrict them.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut off and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	that remedies for continuing come in one of these cartilages, and is of little use, because in some people.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, it is necessary to check if the wound is fresh and full of blood; and then join the two lips together with a stitch, then treat until it is healed; and if the lips are already decayed on one side and the other, it is necessary to burn all the parts that are not healthy, then join the two lips together with a stitch, hold it in place, and powder with powder of dragon's blood and frankincense; and put the powders on a piece of strong or other strong plaster, and leave it until it heals through it, then treat the wound with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The way of the stitch is that you assemble the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the stitch of the belly; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Some people have abscesses inside the lips that are hard and like grains of various sizes, both small and large; therefore, it is necessary to turn out the lips, and puncture each one, and take the pus with forceps and rub it in every part; then apply the wound after crushing broken glass, until the wound is no longer bleeding; then apply an ointment, and cure the wound of dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the crown of the teeth
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a crown is pushed up from the gums, which the ancients called "albulus"; it should be held with forceps at its root, and let the blood or pus flow; then put on the tooth vitriol powder broken into pieces, or other restricting and desiccating powders; and if the crown returns after incision, and often does, cover it again, and cauterize: if it does not return after cauterization, these are the forms of instruments for covering.
des sordens	of the deaf
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes the teeth are gathered at the top of the tooth, between the gums, sharp and offensive scars; and sometimes they are black, yellow, and green, until corruption comes to the gum, and are bad-smelling; it should be placed between your hands, and its roots should be in your holy place, and remove the teeth or scars as soon as possible; and thus remove the blackness and greenness and yellowness and other stains, until they are all cleaned; and if what is at the first level is good, that is good; if not, start again on the second day and the third, until you have removed everything; and know that the teeth have different forms of instruments to remove, depending on what the work demonstrates, because the saw that is used to remove between the teeth has other shapes than those used to remove between the teeth; and these forms and others should be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when treating tooth pain that you delay pulling it as much as possible, for no one should do this; because it is a substance very high and therefore we have no excuse for pulling it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore, when the tooth is painful and must be pulled, then you should be certain of the tooth breaking.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain of the tooth is relieved, and you should check if it is a holy tooth, and have the good tooth pulled; and then the pain does not depart immediately, because we have already done this to these saints; and when you are certain of the broken tooth, then you should burn around the tooth all the way to the gum; then move it with your fingers or subtle pliers at the first and second point, until it is well dislodged, then firmly fasten the pliers; and let the patient hold the tooth between his teeth, and keep it still so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After straightening the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not jump back into place, take any of these instruments and gently tap on each part lightly, and then shake as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is perforated and damaged, it is necessary to fill it with cloths where the pulp is; and if the extraction is subtly caught on hooks, so that it does not break when extracting; and it is very important to cover around the gum to relieve the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be careful not to break it and leave a part behind, and re-insert it with more pain from the root than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware that you do not act in such a way as the ignorant physicians do, who, by their haste and boldness, break the chariot at once, and never bring back what we have told; but they bring forth only once through the opening of this great disease for the roots that they delay, or for the chariot that they break, as we often have seen; and when the dense matter is drawn out, wash the limb with wine or vinegar and oil; and if blood comes out again, which often happens, use the broken glass of vitriol; and if it does not work, cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of instruments, by which one moves the first teeth, should be long and wide-based, so they do not double back when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be thick-bodied so they do not bend when you pull, and they should be made of well-made iron, and they should be sharp to hold.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains when pulling, then it is necessary to place a soft cotton pad on the jaw or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the jaw is softened, then push the forceps called "alligators", of which the patient seems like a beak; and they should be made inside as a hook and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these needles, then it is necessary that you dig around the root of the whole chariot, and put the tool called «althali», that is, a spoon, of which this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And if it is too large and does not break easily, and if the root jumps out of the sky, that is good; if not, then you use all the tools, of which the forms come hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if it helps, then use this tool that has two prongs, of which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are before in the range of the teeth, and of this tool that seems like large needles, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this instrument is not to be broken except that much of the instruments of dense are; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise masters subtly find their own instrument, according to what their work and the disease shows, because there are some diseases where the ancients did not teach the instrument for the diversity of the others and if they broke the cart or other bones, or it hurt, if he looks for the instruments that he needs, as I have said, and helps with gestures, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and well holding to hold the bone so it does not escape, but he can hold and remove; then restore the limb of medicines according to this, and if there is pain in the bone, and it is small, then the whole instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not in accordance with its natural course, and its shape is ugly, and especially in young women, it is necessary that you remove the tooth if it is not in the right place, and cannot be straightened: then the tooth is removed; and if it is erupted with the tooth, take this instrument which has the form of a small beak, and is similar to a spoon made of iron and heated in fire:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the copper coin gently and slowly for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that it can be lamed, then the lame part of a spoon like this is used:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the lime on which we make arrows; and in the lime, the tooth is gently and slowly rubbed with a lighter and lighter tool, so that it does not move until it chips; then the flat end of the tool is used to scrape away any remaining roughness, and if the tooth is too sharp and it cuts the tongue, then one must smooth the roughness until it is even, so that it does not cut the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth are locked
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the teeth in front are locked, either by impact or by falling, and the pain cannot be relieved because it moves too much, and you treat them with tightening medicines but they do not work; then you must use a thin gold wire, for silver wire turns green and rots, but gold never does; and the wire should not be too thick or too thin, according to the amount of space between the teeth; and if you see that the teeth are moving, then take the wire and double it between the two healthy teeth, then place the affected teeth between the healthy ones, as many as there are, until you feel safe on the other side; then start again with the covering from the part where you started, and tighten your hand subtly and safely, so that it does not move at all; and let your wire reach to the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the affected threads with a needle, and gather them together, and place them between the healthy teeth, and set them in such a way that they do not bleed the tongue; and then leave them so tightly as they can hold, and if they slip out, or the thread breaks, if another thread is stretched, it holds and serves thus for the entire time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the binding of the two healthy teeth, and the two bones, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth chips, if it is reset in its place, from fresh to fresh, as we have said; and it does not interfere with those who are wise and suffering, and once made is the form of a goat's tooth bone, and it is placed where the defect is, and it is stretched as we have said, and holds and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut open the vein of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	There are no veins in the tongue that come out of its place or by nature, unless it is due to an accidental wound; and the procedures are such that you open the mouth with caution, and hold the head steady, and lift the tongue; then cut open the nervous vein widely, until the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is hardness or not, and it is due to a wound, if you boil the root and cut widely; and be careful that the wound is not too deep, for the artery that is out; and when you have done, lift the tongue with rosewater and vinegar, or cold water, then place a linen tent outside the tongue; and treat the wound every night, so that the wounds do not close.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if there is bleeding from the wound, apply glass powder to the affected area; and if it does not stop, cauterize with slow-burning charcoal, which is good for the skin; then treat other wounds as needed until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see that it is of a yellow or black or hard color, and the patient does not feel pain, do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is inclined to discharge pus, and there is moisture, pour the spout of a thin syringe from one side and out the other; and if it does not stop bleeding at your work, apply glass powder until it stops bleeding, then return to your work until you remove all of it; then lift the limb up and down, and treat other wounds as needed until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	of throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Never does one find abscesses in the throat which are called "godath", and they are properly called the II amendments, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then take care: if it is an abscess that is hard and of a small size and of a yellowish color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, but leave it until it breaks by itself; and then you will be able to remove it, or it would break by itself; and if it is of a white color and the root is thin, then prepare the instrument for covering, but first check whether the abscess has calmed down and is quiet.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Therefore, place the injured part in front of the sun, and its bones should be in their proper position, and the operator's hand and the instrument between his hands, and press the tongue out of the way with all the instrument, of which this is the form; and it should be made of silver or fine brass as some knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	If you press the tongue with all this instrument, and you see the abscess, take the lancet and the needle in the amber, and draw it up as high as you can; and take nothing else with, then cover the instrument with the cloth, of which this is the form, that seems like a forceps; and the teeth are sharp, and one side and the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, if you have coping with pliers, of which is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And on one side, it is sharp, and on the other side, blunt; and when you have coped one of the pliers, then cop the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the sharp pain with hot, sharp, and cold water, and if blood comes out, then gargle the sharp pain with hot, or pounded green pomegranate seeds, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the mouth is clean; then cure it as long as it is healthy; and never do other abscesses than the two pliers, if they are coped thus.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was lodged deep within her throat, specifically the abscess of small size; and she had almost entirely closed off her entire throat, such that the woman could not breathe through the constriction that was choking her, and could neither eat nor drink, and died if she persisted in such a state for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so large that it had been filled with two handfuls of pus through the two nostrils.
