Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I therefore immediately applied a cloth to one nostril, then removed the pus, and a large portion of pus; then I refilled it through the other nostril, and pressed on the tongue; after removing the cloth from the abscess, and only a small amount of blood came out; thus the woman was able to breathe again, and she began to drink water and wine, and did not cease cutting away at that abscess for a long time; the abscess recurred repeatedly, and filled up the space that I had previously emptied, becoming very large; therefore I applied a probe and cauterized it within her throat: thus it did not grow again; and I left with these parts, and only God knows what happened to her afterward.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When regarding the eye, and it is sunken and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is not too large and round, it is called "uve".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the cure does not improve much, and you see that the arrowhead abscess is calmed, and it is thin, then you should cover it; and the one that is round and not long; and if it is bloody or dark red or black, then you should avoid making an incision in it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger in the pain.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	When you see it, as I have mentioned, according to its length and width, place the painful part in front of the sun, and press the tongue with the tool we mentioned earlier; then make an incision in the vein, and remove it, and treat it with the two tools I mentioned for the incision of the two arrows.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you only remove the excess that is beyond the natural limit; for if you remove more, it will cause great pain to the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we mentioned earlier in the incision of the two arrows, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the pain is not alleviated by copper, then you should use an engine for cauterization of the sensitive pain.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cauterization is sharp and hot.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the pain puts his head in your safe hands, and then press the tongue against the instrument that we have said or chapter of cauterization, and confis with sharp and alive heat, so that it is not too thick or too clear; and in the movement of this instrument, from which is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the head has a hair or one puts the medicine, like the movements of a spoon, and puts the instrument all the medicine above the vein; and the pain lies on his side, so that saliva and mucus flows from his mouth of the medicine inside, so it does not descend to the throat and the blood; then hold your hand on all the medicine and press on the vein for a quarter of an hour, until you see the benefit and the medications of the medicine are calmed; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and wipe the cotton in the medicine, and blow the instrument all the cotton into the channel above, until the cotton is burned on the vein; and do this often, until the cauterization of the medicine is perfect, then leave it to dry, and clean after four or five days. And if you have the task of restarting the cauterization of the medicine, if you restart, and after the cauterization wipe it around the vein with cotton soaked in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and be rubbed with sharp cold, and be treated with gargles until they are healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer from the incision than from the cauterization; if it is cured by fumigation in this way, take camomile and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and vervain and similar herbs, and assemble them all or some of them in a pot, and put oil in it, and make it boil; and the pot should be well sealed with strong earth, and inside the pot have an instrument like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be of silver or lead, and one of the pricks is inserted into the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the eye through the nose, until the eye is dead; afterwards, it is repeated as often as the eye dries, and guard that you do not make heat at the beginning of the outbreak of the abscess, for many things happen; and do not make heat except at the decline of the abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cloth and place it inside the mouth, so that the mouth does not have too much heat; for the cloth does not make too much steam to burden the mouth, and it is good cure together with safety.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it is necessary to remove bones or fish spines from the throat, or nothing at all; therefore, you must take out what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun at all instruments, so that you can see the thing; and what does not open and is returned in the throat, it is necessary to make vomit the bad thing as soon as the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps if the thing is pushed out by vomiting; or the bad things swallowed a piece of sponge, or a piece of naval, or a lettuce root, or the small pieces of dry bread; and tie the sponge with a thread, and then swallow it; and when it comes back to the mouth, it will stick, and then pull out firmly; and if it does not come out of what we have said, take the instrument according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the curved instruments be bent at the head so that they can more lightly enter into the throat, and raise the head high; and guard that you do not touch the epiglottis, that it does not come to him, or push the bone in; and it is better that the hairs push the instrument, because it is softer or the thing is as such; if it pushes down, or it pulls it all along the instrument evenly, as far as it is full.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat opening
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Never use the throat opening, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and if it does not help, then look at the hairs in the throat to the sun, then press the tongue against the instrument that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the sinew, trace it with a small needle or thin needles that are worthy of the eye.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if the eye does not hold, take a hair from the beard, and boil it in the patient's throat, then boil or move the hair with the iron, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the wounds bleed all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take full handfuls of cold water, and open the mouth, and pour it in the direction of swallowing, and move it to his hand often; and as soon as the sinew feels the cold, it contracts.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not break as we have said, then fumigate the bad smell of putrefaction with the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the grape; do this many times, for it will eventually go away.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the way of the fumigation is that you take a pot or where it has charcoal in it, and place it under a perforated cover in the middle, and in that puncture put the instrument; then pour your fumigation, and put the head of the cainne in its mouth, and close its mouth, so that the fumes do not escape, but go just to the throat; and the throat will now be relieved, and if it does not succeed, you must repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salted and other things, and do not drink any sharp; and then it is the task that it will be cured by this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the tool used to treat the throat, if one can see it, resembles a hooked needle to enter the throat; and it has the shape of a beak, and there is roughness from lime, so that whatever it takes, it cannot slip; and here is its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are various kinds of abscesses, according to what memory comes to mind after one and another in this book, and they differ in puncture and incision; and it is in two ways that one is in its own shape, and because it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method is for the arms or when they are at the sides.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the main abscesses are different from those that come from the foundation, and the abscesses of the shoulder joint are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there are abscesses that one should not pierce until the swelling is complete; and if there are such as must be pierced when they are ripe, and do not die according to their completion, like abscesses that are beyond joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come beyond joints, and it is left until it is surrounded by, perhaps because the ligament and the nerve of the joint are corrupted, by which this is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	When the abscess is distant from the main limb, and if you delay perforation until it dies, it will harm the main limb; or if it is distant from the foundation, if you pierce it before it dies, it will not be able to bear weight, and will remain crooked inside, and there may come a fistula; and it cannot be healed in a short time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary to remove the pus from the perforation of the abscess according to its completion, and this is when the pain is eased, and the departure of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and inflammation, and the diminishment of the swelling and the discharge of the main part of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary to make the perforation in the lower part of the limb where it is most open; and let the perforation be long and straight, and if the abscess is near the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all cases where there is no pus.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, according to the affected member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in the limb, it is best to leave the puncture until it is confirmed that digestion has been completed, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you puncture it beforehand, it may follow along the course of the blood vessel from it, and cause much filth; and perhaps harden the lips and penetrate deeper into it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if any abscess that is punctured along the wide course of the blood vessel, according to what the limb has need of.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is best to treat small abscesses with small punctures; and large abscesses with large punctures, and many cuts according to the likeness of the size of the abscess; and if such abscesses or it is necessary to cover them, and close them; when they have become like a cloth, and are softened, then it is best to do as one does with bubbles: and if such abscesses are cut in three angles, and if such abscesses are covered like the fullness of milk, and cover as abscesses; and if such abscesses or one makes a round shape, and other shapes and coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	For those who do not have a head, if the abscess is superficial, it is necessary to lance it completely; and when the abscess is large, and there is great swelling, and you lance it, if you do not draw out all the pus in that hour, but only a part; then stop the abscess with the other side, then take away nothing else; do this repeatedly, many times, until all the pus is out; especially if the wounds are of weak virility, or women carrying, or small children, or old decrepit people.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the experienced never tremble once with the outflow of the pus, because perhaps the wounds might die, and you would not perish.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, suck the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if a tailor complains, soothe him with linen or woolen cotton; and if there are large abscesses, and there is much pus, it is necessary that you put in each one a tent so that they come against each other; and if you have sewn in the abscess a part of the skin, and you have wrapped it around, it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or shredded linen against moisture, and tie it just to the flesh, then open, and treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if there is bleeding in your work, apply sharp cold and wet cloths, and clean the wound, and place it on the affected area for many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, apply proper treatment and care, and use the powders I mentioned in this book, and if it is very tense, and the wound or abscess is very sensitive, it is recommended to place tents and clean cloths soaked in wine and oil; and if it is in a bad state, and the wound is charred, it is recommended to place clean cloths soaked in cold and oil, or warm wine and oil, as we have said; then drain the abscess, dress it, and treat it, as appropriate, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know this universally in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and see this chapter.
des soros	from swellings
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When small abscesses come from the head, and are of various kinds, like the lentils of a girl, and many such there are.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are also large and such ones that are moist like frogs; and there are some that are hard and stony to cut, and there is no doubt if the artery is not against it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the cutting is such that you try all the instrument called "entromissoire", from which the form comes after, what thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	If it contains moisture, then let it dry out from above the long one.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is drained, scrape off any hair that contains that moisture, for it will return if left alone; then apply Egyptian ointment, if present; if not, apply honey and salt, and cover the wound, and leave it there until the next day; and this should continue for several days.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then restart the cotton, as before, the second day, and the bandage, until you are sure it will not remain overnight; then treat the wound with appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess is not too large, then cover it with this form, long; and pour in some onions, and the scrape from all parts, and put all your care into drawing out the pus from where it lies; and if the artery opposes, do as I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also make an incision if it is pierced, and cut and cure as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And if the incision is made over a pierced abscess and wet, it is lighter, for it is of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if any of these abscesses or wounds or they have no moisture, and among these were the abscess or wound that I copied or from an old woman; and found the abscess also like a hard stone, rough and white, and could not be broken; and if anyone had made a cut in it, they would have done as much harm as with a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming or leading, because those who come to the head of children and to the roots of the ears, the opening should always be at the most dependent part, in order to let out the pus; and treat them as appropriate.
des scrophules	of hydroceles
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	often have abscesses at the neck, and dislodge the testicles, and pierce, and sometimes come from other parts or the chest, and are very large, and are inflamed together.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each hydrocele is properly on its side, like the pus in the head, as we have said; and similar to these hydroceles are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are some evil ones that do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In those that you see in good position at the touch, and resembling the color of the flesh, and quiet from every part and not connected to the artery or vein or conduit, and not deep; then it is necessary to remove it from above, and scrape the skin from each part, and close the two lips of the wound as one, if you have skill, as we have said in the chapter on abscesses; and gradually, and be sure that you do not cover the nerve or vein, and not too deep, so that the hands do not escape, and do not see too much before, what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not stop bleeding, put into the wound vinegar broth, or some powders that stop blood flow, and close the wound; and leave it until the abscess is calmed, and the wound is soothed, and then begin to apply a poultice.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is dry, return to your work until you complete it; then consult your own judgment whether there remain any small scabs, if they are removed and cleaned.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scab, it is not advisable to remove that scab at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it drop through, without causing harm; then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian oil, then treat the wound.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you remove the entire abscess, it is necessary to gather the two lips of the wound and hold them together, as there is no need for excess due to the size of the abscess.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary to apply a covering to the root of it, and draw out the pus, and hold it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those abscesses that contain excess pus should be lanced where it is most likely to die; and they are lanced in the same way as before mentioned, depending, then apply dressings with poultice and similar things, so that it does not corrupt what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well dressed, the cure of poultice should be continued until it is healed.
de squinance	of dislocation
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and said of the necklace of the throat; but I never saw one in our land, and it is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	To those who have dislocation, it is necessary that the opening of the throat, which is called "epiglottis," be avoided; and this is not done by means of it, because all the veins and the mouth of the evil are in those who have abscess full in the mouth, or in the throat or in the jaws.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the mouth, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, it is necessary that we cut it outside of three circles or four with a small incision across, between the two circles or by the quantity of the incision through the syfac, but not in the cartilage; and those who do this are suitable for the section of the epiglottis as there is no char, and the vessels are long and do not bleed.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is not careful, it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the neck all around, then cuts the cartilage until it reaches the chin; and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then cop the syfac as we have said; and this is demonstrated by the section of the flap of the chin which was torn by the limb that was broken, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed for which we doubt strangulation, gather both lips of the wound together, and cover it completely without the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause heat to rise until they are healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that we should not do this unless the throat is completely stiffened, and the limbs are judged to be dead, and the defect is lost.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Therefore, we should cut open the epiglottis because the limbs cannot maintain themselves, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is kept from death; and because they commanded the ancients to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease had passed, and it passed in three days or four. And therefore, they commanded to sew up the wound and cure it, as long as it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young lady took a knife and stabbed herself in the throat, and cut part of the windpipe; and I was called to cure her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the arrow that had come out of it, and although she had not coughed blood or vomited, the blood flowed from the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried, and sewed the wound, and cured it so that it was healed; and she did not die until she was about to lose her voice, and then she recovered; because I believe that in the sewing of the epiglottis there is no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a great abscess in the color of a grape, and it is very common in women; and it occurs in two ways: natural and accidental; or naturally without cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental one is in two ways, one of which is similar to a large abscess, and the other way is similar to an abscess that comes from us through an artery; and there is fear, and it does not require to be opened except by a small incision in the center, and the proof and search are throughout the entire introduction: if you find it as if it were a large one, and cannot be cured at all, if the copper, as if on the large ones, and take it out completely, if there is none; and look for it quickly, and treat it as it should be, until it is healed perfectly.
des nous	For the fire cautery
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways we have, of which I will say all the similarities; and now it is necessary for me to tell all the difference between us and the issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that issue is burning and fever-causing, until the boils are passed, and it is accompanied by pustulation; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With ours, there is no burning or fever or pain, and it contains the syphilitic pustule, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the skin, and begins like a small pustule, and becomes large; and they are in two similarities, dry or moist, and many colors are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to treat an unknown case, it is necessary to first examine and test the instrument called "entromissoire", according to its form as described in the following chapter.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the method of examining abscesses is that you press or slightly moisten the skin where the abscess is, and return your two fingers slowly, until you feel that the instrument has pierced the core, then adjust it according to the size of the abscess; then extract the entromissoire, and be careful not to cause injury.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the running pus has a certain color, make it as I have described for other abscesses; and if after the entromissoire does not come out with any moisture, then check if it is greasy, and then cut it in a cross shape, and take it with pincers, and scrape off all the flesh from every part and remove the cotton where it was, so that you can take out the wound cleanly with the new dressing; and if you cannot take it out cleanly, then tear it in pieces until nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	If nothing remains, it returns to us many times; and if it lingers for a short while, and does not bother you, apply some corrosive powders to the wound, and bind the wound, and place soothing things on top of abscesses, and treat other injuries until they are healed; and if it is large, cut out the two lips of the wound, and treat what remains.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if it is against the wind or another direction, and you are in a hurry, apply the wound with broken glass, and leave it for two or three days until the wound heals, and rest the discharge of blood; then return to the previous method that was left.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of instruments used for extracting stones, and there are three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three quarters that are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and there are three kinds: large, medium, and small, to extract the stones of a fistula; and they are also like the needles that one uses for sewing, and they are made of gold, or iron, or silver, and they cost as much as those that are already yellow, and they are more effective in removing black pus from a fistula; and they are three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the fistula.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of needles are of many similarities, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and if there are needles with two prongs in three ways; and if there are needles with three prongs, and they are also in three ways; and if there are needles with two prongs, and a single-pronged needle, and they are also in three ways; and all of these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The main purpose of these instruments is to cut, and there are some that do not cut except from one part, from which we remove the bones, because they do not cut the vein or the nerve; and among these intruments are the forceps, which are repositioned in tongs, so that the pain does not persist at the opening of abscesses; and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one uses only a small one in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and joints, and similar places; and one never uses any other instrument small, resembling forceps for removing pus, according to this form.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is never put back in place that it should be aligned with veins, and arteries, and once again returns according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Never inflate the breasts of some men when they begin to rot, as they seem like breasts of a woman; and they remain swollen and inflamed, and if one wants to cure them, it is necessary to follow this form of this line .b. until .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape the fat, and fill the wound with medicine of charred linen, then sew together the two lips of the wound with stitches, and cure it until it is healed; and if the breast hangs down, and is softened by its greatness as in women, then pierce it through the ribs above, by similar cuts; so that one end holds to the other at the end of each, so that the greatest line contains the smallest according to this form, from this line .b. to the line .g.; then scrape the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary in the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not made completely, for the reason that the pains do not want to rest, or because of the flow of blood, then it is necessary to fill the wound with moistened cotton in a corrosive ointment; and let it remain until it melts the remaining fat, then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the heels
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from the heels are ways of hard scabs or if they have cracks, and there are some that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore, those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from the line b to the line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the whole of the pus in the abscess is drained, apply old cotton to the wound and leave it on the other side, then remove all the cotton, and treat with a poultice suitable for this until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are similar to scrofula, then treat them as we have said about incising scrofula, and if the wound remains open, then cauterize it as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is ruptured, and the skin above it is sore, then often abscesses develop, and there is also blood in the vein and abscess; and if one knows it is for the artery, then the abscess should be lanced longwise; and when you feel it with your fingers, it is stretched; and when it is for the vein, it should be opened laterally; and it is foolish to cover this abscess, and especially when it is outside the joints and angles and collarbone and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, it is necessary to avoid the use of iron, and the one who is in charge should also avoid it, and in the one who is swollen from arterial bleeding through the long skin; then open the belly with small incisions, and remove the artery as far as it is exposed; then insert a needle on the other side, and pierce it with another needle according to what I have indicated in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then do not tie the vein that is between the two threads of an instrument until the missing part is found, and remove the abscess; then cure the wound as it is injured, as long as the sinew is healthy; and if the abscess is for the belly of the vein, it is necessary to stain your hand with what comes from the abscess on all the skin, then remove the needle from the thread that you hold in your hand, and pierce it, and there should be two threads, so that you can pull it from the other side; then tie the abscess as I have said, or with one of the two threads of the needle; and if you doubt that the thread will not stick, then take another needle at the end of all the abscess to the incision of the first needle, and tie the threads in four; then cover the abscess until the excess is removed, then cover the wound and leave what is tied; then put a piece of moist cloth in wine and oil, then cure the wounds and injuries until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses come in the artery and the vein, abscesses also come to the nerves when they are injured, or from too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And they often occur in the assistants and the do and in all those who have joints, and this is the worst abscess, and its color resembles the color of the blood, and it is in many positions with pain; and when it is extracted, it causes great pain, and it is not like the blood, but outside the body; and it moves from all parts, and does not go forward or backward, nor upwards, and those who are in joints do not need to cover them with iron: perhaps they cause contraction; and those who are on the head or on the front, making the skin to the spasm.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, if you have needles, and pierce it at its root; and if it is large, if you suspend it at the base, and scrape, then remove the bone and stitch the wound to the edge, and cure until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of large swollen abscesses
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Never found in the belly and never in any other part of the body, and it is a disease called "fungus" by its appearance, and it has subtle roots, and large fleshy roots; and there are small and very large ones; and I saw the man who had two or more bellies that were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had small roots, and they were torn, and they grew again with moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I copied and found in the one XVIII ounces heavy, and in the other VI З., and the work in the incision is that you look if the hairs are moist, and the color of the artichoke is white and moist and of subtle root; if the copper has a wide spatula, and the fire cautery is in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For in cutting, there often come too great corrections of blood, and if you do not see the hair extending and painful from the incision of the iron, then take the thread of good quality, and tie the artichoke as we have said, and leave it for two days; then restrain it, and do not cease to draw out the thread of good quality until it covers the artichoke, and cut through it with work; and if the roots are large, then put the copper directly on the belly, but you must put the copper half on, then cauterize that it does not return; then care for the wound, and make sure you do not cover the thigh which is of pale color and poor sensation and of no regard.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For these infected abscesses, I will come to treat them with leeches later.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the patient is feverish
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of fever comes from fire cautery or cutting of skin, and is located above the belly and in some of the buboes, as it has in other wounds, of blood which cuts veins or arteries according to what is before, or of pus; and if it is from the rupture of the syphilitic sore and from the issue of the pus, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the blood, and it is a light thing without pain, and open from various issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is for the issue of the intestine, then it is most diverse, and when one presses it to its two sides, it returns, and perhaps it is torn, and enlarges greatly at the entrance of the bath and by much work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is for moisture, it is a light matter, and opens well when one presses it with their hand, without constraining much; and if it is for blood, it opens by these signs of large and hard abscesses, and is swollen according to the quantity; and if it is for windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the appearance of the work indicates whether it is for the blood of the artery or vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If it is necessary to leave the care.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is for the intestine or the boil, then it is necessary to command the patient to dye his clothing, and be extended straight, then sign around the belly; then command him to lie still between your hands, then go around the limb that you have marked with all the space, then extend half of the abscess above the large incision; then tie it around with a very strong thread, or a firm silk cord, and let the intestine rest on the other side; if you find the intestine, if you pull it, and cut the intestine behind the belly; and if you find the boil, if you take it at the base, and cut off the excess; and if the artery makes it against you, or the vein, then go around carefully, then return to your work and take two needles, and two threads of fine silk, and cut the two needles as you have done in the shape that you will make to pierce; then extend the abscess into four pieces above the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and let the limb remain until it can bear weight, and kill the dead flesh by itself; or you cover it when it has become thin and can bear weight, then cure the limb of what is necessary, and cut the abscess as we have said; and draw out the pus or moisture that you have taken, then cure the limb of what is necessary, and soak the limb.
dou chancre	For the fire cauterization, instruct
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	For the fire cauterization, instruct
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For the fire cauterization, instruct
de ydropisie	de l’estomac
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	In the division of the stomach, we have mentioned the similarities of hydropsies, and how the assembly of the sharp is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the treatment by medicines, and that which is treated by iron: if it is only swelling; and one should not touch iron in these two similarities: that is to say, tympanites and hyposarche, for it is a fatal thing; therefore when you treat this similarity of hydropsies which is called "swelling" by medicines, and the treatment does not work, if you look at whether the pain is weak, or if he has another disease besides hydropsies, as all and solution of the belly and similar things; then do not touch iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the pain is very strong, and he has no other disease except hydropsies alone, and he is not too young nor too old, then thus: hold the pain straight up in your hands, and the assistants press the belly at the lowest part of the spine, then take the sharp instrument according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And be slicing of two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And slice of two parts at the tip, and ensure that it is not too thin so that it can come into contact with the intestines when thrown, and it cannot be bleached; then check if there is hydrops near the intestines: if it is for the disease of the liver, then your cut should be on the right side of the third rib above; and if it is for the spleen, then it should be on the left side, and it should not be that the hairs grow over the cut so that the excess does not flow to the weakest leg; then pierce the skin with the instrument, and squeeze, and remove your hand from all the space between the skin and the spleen as when scraping at the quantity of an egg or around; then pierce the spleen until the space comes to the desired length, and that is the legs of the knife, then remove it, and if you bloat this instrument with which this is the shape:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a thin silver chain, and is made of light rain or chalk, and has small perforations; and on one side, three perforations; and two on the other side, and one on the other; and the patient's tail is cut as with a pen, and that is the form of the incision that the scribes make for the pen:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top of the instrument is the awl, so that when the tool comes to the edge, then place it now above the instrument; without the half or the third part, because if you remove more than it should in that hour, by chance if the patient dies from the resolution of his spirit from the arm, or he faints, or approaches death; but in accordance with the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the wound signify, and its hairs; then remove the tool and retain the edge, and it is retained now for the one who stops the perforation that is above the tongue, of which I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner; then start the instrument again the next day, if you see the patient suffering thus, and take from the edge a small quantity; do this every day, and guard against following too much until it is only a little blood.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt the injury and leave it for a long time, the cure of the sepulture or sand bath, and much sweating or bathing and in the sun, and if it becomes tainted from drinking; and the cure of desiccative medicines until it is healed, and cauterize above the stomach and above the liver and above the spleen after the extraction of the splinter, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the removal of the probe
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child is born without a wart in the penis, or the wart is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary to pierce at all times with a very thin needle according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then place or prick the thin thread of the bottom, and tie it and keep it in this way for three or four days, and when he wants to urinate, if it is not convenient, remove the thread and let him urinate, and then put it back; because the urine that comes out does not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the one who is pricked is small, it is treated with a thin thread of the bottom, as we have said, and it will expand.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the prick in their own leg are frostbitten, because no one is born with the prick at the top of the thigh, so that they cannot urinate before they remove their thigh higher; and they cannot urinate because the matter cannot come down to the marsh, and it is a very bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the method of the work is such that the hairs lie sometimes on their backs, with the head of the knife and the coping as wide as the tail of a pen, so that the puncture is made in the middle, and as it should be; and guard against bleeding of blood which often comes, and if it comes, then wipe away the blood that comes from the wound, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the pustules of the knife
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often come blisters on the knife, and it is an ugly appearance of char; and in them there are good and bad ones; if you should prick them at once with a fine needle, wipe them all, then put on cotton moilliet in Egyptian ointment; then treat the ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the wound is malignant, with a putrid color and foul smell, then you must cauterize it with fire.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cleaned it, and if the wound is in the depth of the flesh, and part of it is inside the skin and part outside, then you must first remove the part that is inside; and when it is clean, then treat the part outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat the wound together, if you are not sure that the arrow has been removed, and it turns black and rots in its place and becomes infected; then you must remove everything that is black and corrupted, then apply the poultice of honey and flour made from the shells of green grapes and wheat, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if blood flows, then treat the lunar cauterization according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.
