The cauterization tools are helpful in two situations: when blood flows out and when the wound is corrupt; and if the tip of the tool is corrupted and drawn back, it is necessary to apply a plaster soaked in piss on the hairs, and urinate on the painful areas; and when the flesh has gone as far as the tip of the tool which has been used for those who have not yet been circumcised, or for a wound or an abscess, it is then necessary to burn it with the instrument until the strings are loosened, and the patient is delivered from all parts of the tool; and if it is a difficult thing to decide, it is necessary to burn it at any point on the head of the tool and the skin, then thoroughly clean between them, and apply a subtle linen cloth soaked in cold water, so that it does not grow back.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not like other wounds; nevertheless, when we perform this work of our intention, and properly on children, it is necessary that we do the best work, and the least harmful to health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not practice circumcision on their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the greater part of masters and doctors who performed circumcision in the middle of the day, and with force, and all at once; since it was the most careful because it had two threads, and by chance if one of them slipped or delayed the other.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the recovery is prolonged, and the pain is doubled, and the wound healing is not guaranteed at the tip of the member; and the wound healing of the angle by chance escapes the iron, and corrupts the work, and often they are born in such a way that they have no need of healing and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the wound healing that is done with force to all the member of the thread, I found the best of the experiment, for the forces cut equally as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, it cuts equally in all the thread; but that the thread be well stretched around the skin; and the manner of the first work is such that you make the child think, if he feels, that you do not force him to bind the thread around the stick only, and then throw it in all ways that you can; then place your hand straight on the stick, and pull the forces between your hands or outside your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then press your hand on the stick and blow gently, and take it up high until the end of the stick is in; then clean well the dirt that is gathered there, then tie the limb with a double thread, then tie it outside at the other end; and hold it as two by the second work to the pouch and the correct index, and cover between the two limbs, then lift the gentle one quickly and take the tip of the stick; then let the blood drip slowly and slowly, for that is the most dangerous; and put powder on top and on the powder a piece of cloth glued with one egg cooked improperly with red wine vinegar, boiled and fresh, and let it stay there until the other day, and cure the other cure until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of forces for the mummification is as follows: the two shoulders must be tight and sharp, and the shoulders must also be great like the hands evenly.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of mummification is when the incision is too deep; therefore, it is necessary to extend it to your elbow, and also the bandage, and if you cannot hold it at your elbow, then use tongs and then the bandage.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they exceed three days, and what is outside the rod is swollen, let it remain until the abscess is calmed down, and scrape lightly; and bandage as you can move, and keep away from the part of the rod, it will not harm.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, treat the limb of things soiled wounds from powder poisoning, which we have said to treat powders, and if it is done with excessive care, it will not harm; therefore, treat it as we have said until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	The retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to the opulation of stones, or blood congealed, or bowel, or charred, or similar things that we have said in the division; and if the urine is not discharged, and you see that the retention is due to the stone which is high or col of the bladder, it is necessary that the pain should be raised above his knees; and his feet should be placed on his back, and his belly extended from the upper part of the back, and restrained the pain as much as possible; and thus the lower part of the bladder is pressed against the upper part of the stone, for which reason the urine is discharged; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the pain is great, then you must administer extraction with all the instrument called «siringue», of which this is the form: and it should be made of fine silver hair, like the pen of an owl; and it should be made of a palm length and half, and fine at the top.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of the issue of urine is such that you take a double thread, and tie the head of the thread to the top of a cloth or cotton, and pull the head of the thread through the tube; and cover the excess of the cloth and pull it towards the head of the tube, then oil the tube with oil or butter and egg yolk, and make the patient sit on the chair, and the urine and the wet cloth of oil and olive oil and vinegar; then place the tube heavily in the cloth, as far as it reaches the root of the cloth, then double the cloth over towards the top; then pull the tube forward just before the cloth, and the patient feels the urine coming towards the empty thing, and this is not made according to this order except that the conductor or she goes twisted; then tie the thread to the whole cloth little by little, and the urine follows the cloth, then remove it, and correct the urine; and start again with the tube until the bladder is empty and aligned with the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When blisters or blood come into the bladder, and putrefaction is assembled, and you see distillation of water and medicines, then use all the tool called «clepsedre», and it is the form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and has three holes: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the threads are passed through it by which the medicine cuts so that it does not touch the urethra too much, so that they can draw out the moisture, and put back as necessary; and when you see your medicines entering the bladder, place the tip of the cannula in the moisture, and draw to the drawing which is outside; if you draw the moisture to the cannula, and then press the drawing tightly; then the moisture enters the drawing, and comes to the bladder now, so that it causes the patient pain; and this is the form of the subtle siphon with which one syringes the bladder: if it is in:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or of arnica, and is the highest of the patient's chest; and descends to the seat where the veins lie; then take a sheep bladder and put the moisture that you see clisterizer the bladder, then place it between the two breasts formed by a good woolen cloth doubled, and heat the poultice over the fire; then pour the head of the clister into the rod, then hold your hand on the bladder throughout the moisture evenly, until the hairs feel that this moisture has come to the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce it roundly around; then pull the thread strongly in these holes, then assemble the circle as you would assemble the dal, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and vinegar, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	In the division of stones, we have discussed the methods of cutting and extraction together with medicines; and I have explained the difference between a stone embedded in the kidneys and all signs, and in which kind of stone one should make an incision; and in the bladder, and in the urethra; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone embedded in the bladder is more common in children, and this is a sign that the sharp pain of the bladder resembles a sharp sting in its subtlety; and it has a hard shell, and great pain in the groin, and it can happen many times, and then it returns; and at most of these jumps, the foundations are affected; and it is light in the healing of children until they are four years old, and it is very painful in the elderly, and it is a constant problem for those between youth and old age; and its cure is less difficult for those who have large stones, than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, it is first necessary to cleanse the wound with cloth, to draw out all the matter that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it never clogs when seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the wound by the feet, and stand it upright and move it away from the body, so that the stone descends to the edge of the intestine, and never once rises above the leg; then place it between your hands and clean it, and its hands away from its thighs, so that the intestine is completely declining downwards; then remove and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in the space, then hurry to cut across the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if she does not cry out at all, then moisten your index finger of your right hand, if the pain is sharp, or your middle finger, if the pain is dull; and place it on her foundation, and press the stone, and when you feel it at your finger, then moisten the neck of the bladder; then press above your finger, and the stone where you see it cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend his right hand to the testicles above, and his left hand to remove the skin that is outside the testicles in the part where the cut is made; then cut the spongy tissue, of which this is the form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	When between the thighs and the base, not in the middle but on the right side of the naval; and straight up the stone, and your hands should be at the base or at the bottom, and the tail should be across so it is wide on one side and narrow on the other, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large; perhaps the pressure of the hands at the base causes them to slip out; and if there are pieces or edges, and margins: if they are greasy to remove; and if there are soft parts, similar to a gland, and rounded, from which the issue is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	When there are angles and margins where it should be cut, make the incision wider; and if it does not jump, it is necessary to strain it with nails that are as sharp as a lime at the head, for straining the stone so that it does not escape; or you drive out of the subtle instrument curved at the head; and if you cannot engage it thus, enlarge the little hole, and if there is no decortication, then strain it with vitriol; and if there are more than one stone, first cut the largest one at the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then remove the small ones afterwards if there are many.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	If it is very large, then it should be cut, and a larger wound made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the wound: either it dies, or the urine comes out through the opening that the flesh cannot close; but nevertheless you try to draw out, or to tear with pliers, until you pull it out in pieces; and when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it, and put a cold cloth on top of it, in oil and wine, or in oil and vinegar and cold rose water, to soothe the boil; then resolve the wound over its collarbone, and do not leave the thread in place until the next day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you reset it, the limb should rise well with oil and vinegar, then apply a healing ointment and basilicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if an abscess comes into the wound and corrosions, and clots of blood in the bladder, and is retained by the urine, which is known to be withheld without causing pain: then apply your hand to the wound, and extract that blood, because if it remains, it will rot the bladder, and cause harm; then lift the wound with vinegar and salt and oil, and assist in all ways that you can, until it is healed; and it is necessary that all the bandages that you apply, that you tie them to both thighs, and gather the medicines above the limb.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is guided by a rod, and tied with a thread, and the urine cannot be passed; then as I have said before, you must cut it many times, or excuse the cutting for this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have experienced this before.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take a piece of iron according to this form and be at three angles tied with a thread:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie the stone around the rod outside the urethra, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then gently push the iron along the rod until it reaches the stone; and slowly turn the iron in your hand into the stone until you can pierce it from the other side; if urine comes out immediately, then press your hand over what remains of the stone that is inside the rod.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is sometimes broken, and it jumps out with the urine, and it is sharp against the skin; and if you cannot do this for any reason, then take a thread and pull one end of the bone from below, and the other from above, then make the rod in the middle of the bone between the two ends, then extract it forcefully, and remove the bone, and clean the clotted blood that is in the wound; and treat until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It rarely happens that a stone is inserted in women, and if it ever does, the cure is difficult, and it is forbidden for three reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who is well-known to have done such a thing, specifically when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that by chance one cannot find a woman well versed in this art of hands; and the fourth way is that if the woman's stone is larger than the man's, because it must be cut deeper, and there is great fear involved. And if necessary, you should send for a wise woman, and have her hold the truth, and if you do not find one, then you should not do anything subtle; and present a wise woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command of the examination of the stone; and look very closely to see if the woman is a virgin: therefore it is necessary to put her hand on her fundament and ask for the stone; and if she finds it, she should constrain it outside her fundament, and recommend that she put her hand on her fundament or with the pain, and press her right hand firmly against the anus.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, it is necessary to move it great by great from the entrance of the bladder up to the outside, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then cut across the bone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the joint, where it is muscle-covered, and feel the bone in that part; and do not move her above the bone or outside, and let the tailor make a small opening in the first place; then push the arrow through the opening until it comes out far enough, and know that there are many ways of arrows: that is to say, small and large and sharp and blunt, long and round and with rain.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you recognize the similarities to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if you do not know, then apply the broken glass of vinegar to the wound, and keep it there for an hour until the wound is cleansed; then return to your work, until the stone is fully removed, and have the tools that I have told you about in the extraction of the stone to assist you in your work; and if you do not know, and it is the artery that is cut, then apply powder on the wound and bandages and tenting, and do not restart, and leave the stone and do not remove it, lest by chance the patient dies; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	When the heat of the blood is calmed, and the wound healed, then return to your work, until the stone is formed.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia carbuncle
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing other than an assembly of moisture or white sphacelus, which is outside the skin of the womb, which contains the womb; and it is called «sphacelus», and it is never properly in the membrane of the womb, if one thinks that it is another womb; and this is the skin of the womb between the white sphacelus that we have said; and it does not have any other.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this branch is due to weakness that comes from within, and it is spread out that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the joints, and this moisture has many colors: or it is the declining color to jaundice, or it is without red, or black, or watery white, and there are more; and these are the signs to know this assembly, for if it is white like we have said, then it is the abscesses we have mentioned, I poc long as the figure of an egg, and does not open the joints, for it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if it has moisture in its own skin, then it is the abscesses we have mentioned with part of an egg, and because people think it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the joints and the white like we have said, then it feels good; therefore when you see the color of the moisture, try all the previous forms.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes afterwards, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we heal it with iron, it is necessary to clean the hairs according to its power and the repletion of its body; then place it on its back, on something a little high, and cover it with much cloth; then bend towards its right side, and command the minister to bend to the left, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the ribs; then take the spatula and scrape the skin of the ribs from long to over the sharp, and gently scrape the skin according to its power; then cut the flat plain with a sharp wide opening, and remove all the sharp, and then put your forceps, and fix the flat above; do not touch the ribs except the flat itself; cover all or by pieces exactly the side of it subtly, if you do not cover it well enough, it will return to the sharp; and if the skin springs up at your work, then reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the flat; then gather the two flaps of the ribs into one seam, then treat them as the other wounds, until they are healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you try to remove the broken bone that has been corrupted by another disease, it is necessary to tie the vessels that are suspended, doubting the flow of blood; then cut the sinew at all the suspended parts, and remove the bone, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the bone is assembled in two parts together, as it is two branches; then tie the other part as you have done the first evenly, then suck the blood, and put in the wound a poultice of rose oil; and put on another poultice of linen and oil, and put on top of the two sinews, and put on doubled cloths, and tie it to all the limb that is in this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two pieces of cloth, and place them according to this appearance and gathered by sewing around the waist of the trousers, and one of the pieces of the patient is taken above the foundation just below the back, and the other at the part of the buttock; and the other two heads above the two angles, and all assembled is restricted in the loop of the trouser; and once this branch of the cautery in the form of iron, and it is that you take one cautery scalpel subtle, and cope the skin of the wounds, and it is heated as we have said, so that the white pus containing the pus is discovered; then take the cautery according to this form, and perforate this pus with small incisions, and the skin with this subtle cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	In all the ways you can, until you remove everything; and guard that the knife does not touch the bone; and make sure that this work is safer; and be careful of blood clotting, and be careful of the work of tailoring; and if nothing goes against you, or an abscess or bleeding or something else, cure what goes against you, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	If the pain is not severe, and does not want to endure this work due to its horror, then use perforation, as I have told you, and it is that when you are sure by the signs that we have said that abscess water is laid, then place the pain on the raised seat; then pierce the abscess at the part outside all the span wide, and put the perforation down the long of the body; and let the openings be wide so that all the sharp edge flows; then put cotton on the limb, and tie it, and let the remaining sharp edge heal, then treat until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not let the sharp edge issue from the mouth of the wound, then you must go in with a pen or the instrument that treats the sharp edge of dropsy, because its form is as before; and enlarge the wound, and let the sharp edge return, and is assembled after six months or within, and when it is assembled as before, and thus the pain passes its days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of abscesses of the groin
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	In the section of this branch, there are many different positions that cause fear in many people, and it seems to me that it is better to leave it alone; and I will tell you about the work and similar things of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Therefore, many abscesses come from the groin and immediately to the thighs; and this is often the case.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to know by excessive and acidic urine, which spreads in the groin, or from a blow; and the color of the abscess depends on the color of the blood; and it does not cause pain, and it is a severe abscess; and perhaps it is some gray and foul abscesses, and of yellowish color, and sometimes comes from an outlet of an artery, or a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is due to an artery, it is known by the appearance of an abscess, when you press it with your fingers; and you should not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	Those who are made of opening a vein are known by their appearance with gentle touching of the fingers, and can often make a cut above this resemblance, and on other parts; and it is that you should clean the wounds, then extend the wound upwards, and pull out the thread from the top, and deliver the suspended part from all parts of the wound.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the wound is already suppurating with these charges, then you should cut the wound and clean it; and if it is in the thread, or inside the vessels, then you should deliver all of that which is held, and clean it roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the horn of the char is located behind the shoulder, it is necessary that you cut it all, and extract the eye, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your surgeries are completed, apply the wound with a linen cloth soaked in rose oil and wine, then use other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess enveloped by an envelope resembling a barrel, with the softening of the testicles, and it causes great pain when moving; and the treatment of this disease is as difficult and frightening as the previous one, and therefore we will tell you the surgery for it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary to make the dislocated joint sit on its own seat, then lift it up with the suspensory ligament of the tendons to both sides, and all the veins that are close to the thigh, and the master's teignes, and extend them evenly; then cut the spatula sharply through the middle of the veins, as much as they are uncovered, and then scrape from each part, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples; then take an needle or a double-threaded one, and tie it to the first limb where the blood came out, and tie it at the other end; then put it straight in the middle, according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupted moisture; then cure the wound as the others or one enjoins to bandage, so that none of the veins burst; for by this there is no harm, and if all the veins come out visibly, it is necessary to pull the veins to all the veins; so that the eyes do not lose their sight due to the incision of the veins, and dry up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the toothache
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The causes of this branch are due to the section that comes from the toothache, or the extension on the belly in the part of the hips, because the intestines descend from that toothache to one of the kidneys; and this toothache is either from the section of it, or from its extension, and these two methods of many causes come: from impact, from jumping, from shouting, or from lifting a heavy weight, and similar things; and the signs that it is from the extension of the toothache are that it has pain and pain in the long tension, and does not come suddenly; and it is the abscesses equal to the front, because the toothache approaches the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it comes to the section of the tooth, which brings sudden pain at the beginning, and has various appearances of abscesses outside the skin, and it is for the end of the intestine and the heart behind the tooth.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the worms are found with the intestines, and they are retained inside, and cause great pain to suffer from the illness, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of iron with fear, because it should be avoided.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the way of the work is that you command or fear that the intestine be rolled up in your hand inside the wound, if it can be inserted; then place the neck above, and loosen the ribs; then the guts are on top of the ribs, and cover all the skin with coions from the long ones that you have to open the wound, as many as there are that can come out; then scrape the tooth that is outside the skin of the coions, until the white tooth is completely exposed from all parts; then put your first finger in the direction of the coion that leads to the wound, between the white tooth that is outside the skin of the coions and the second tooth, and between the second tooth and where it is behind the stomach, and between the second tooth; and move your right hand inside the skin of the coions, and place the white tooth on top of your left hand, and loosen the stomach over all the tooth below the belly; and command the assistant to stretch the stomach upwards, and remove what is behind the clothing; and if you find anything, if there is any intestine or white tooth remaining, put it in the stomach outside; then take a needle or a thick thread made of twelve threads, and insert it into the back part of the tooth, which is after the skin of the coions; then cover the threads with the skin of the coions, as many as there are four threads; then tie them together in the shape of a cross, and fasten them to the tooth that we have said is outside the skin of the coions, from one end of two threads; then cover the threads with the skin of the coions, so that no vessel that touches them can enter into them, as we have said before; then apply the first thread according to the first thread, and after these two threads leave the tooth that is outside the skin of the coions, the great one of a handbreadth; and then the other according to the roundness that the stomach carries; then cover in the part that is outside the skin of the coions, as many as there are without correcting and bowing, as we have said before; then apply oil-soaked linen to the wounds, and apply the thread that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never cauterize the white swelling that we have said, after incision, due to fear of bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this has happened many times, and let the wound remain until it heals by itself; and if it takes too long to heal, then sprinkle with hot vinegar, and put on what we have said, until it heals; then treat the wound with other treatments, until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia carcinoma
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch, I have never seen anyone dare to perform the cure by iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is done in a manner similar to the branch that is together with the viscera, by tying the vessels below lightly at the opening; then cover in a gentle manner, and treat the abscess with what works, until the vessels heal; and the treatment is as we have said, until it is completely healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Never comes a rip or tear, as we have said, and it opens the abdomen; and no one should draw out any of the intestines with their hands, and if they do, it is little, and they should repair it every hour; and in all ways, if it remains too long at this point, the wound or tear will believe the intestine to be dessent; and this happens by the extension of the intestine which is at the rip, as we have said, because it is extended, then it is softened and inflated and opened; and the cure is by cauterization, as we have already said; and it is never cured in this way: and the wound or tear should be closed with the fingers over the abdomen, then cover the intestine of the rip enfolded in a large amount according to the quantity of three fingers; then press the syphac which is outside the skin that it follows, then take the tail and put it on the intestine apparent of the syphac; and press the front of the belly, then cut the two intestines apparent of the syphac above the head of the tail, and both; then press the head of the tail, and do not cover the syphac or extend the wound or anything else, as I have told you in the cure of the intestines; then cure by the cure of the wound.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you remove the arrows, if you do not defile and heal the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The saphenous vein is constrained, and does not appear in the incision, and the cauteries are silent in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the leather of the boots
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the leather of the boots is softened in some men, because the charcoal that is inside is molded, and it is seen to be; and it is a matter, when one wants to cure, that one makes the wound lie on its back, and the skin that is molded over the natural skin; then assemble the two lips at one seam, and if you see, cut the excess of the molded skin at three seams or four firmly; then sew between the seams, and cure as with other wounds, until it is healed, and cut the thread.
dou chastrement	forcibly
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	However, I would prefer not to discuss this in this book; and it is only necessary for two reasons: one is that the sick person should answer questions and receive treatment while being forced; and the other is because we often have to forcefully treat some animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and rabbits and others.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	Therefore, I say that forcing is done in two ways: either by traction or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the one that we make by traction, place the animal in high heat until the muscles are softened and warm; then take them in your hand, until they are returned and you do not feel them anymore.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	For the chastisement of the tail: it is necessary that you dress the beast, and press the skin of the testicles with your right hand, then tie the suspensory ligament, and copulate with each bone at its head, when you have well scorched them; and leave no pus or subtle pus which is on the vessels; and this method of chastisement is more effective than that made by attraction, because at attraction remains by chance any thing of the testicles, by which the beast desires lust. Then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphrodite exists in two ways among men: one is that between the two testicles, open as the figure of nature of a woman, or with hair, and sometimes cutting the urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other way is in women, and has above the clitoris as a penis and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the care of the man and the woman is that you cut off all the injured parts, and treat them as other wounds; in the second way, of men whose urine jumps through the skin of the testicles, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tenting
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tentigenes are charred bones placed above the natural part, as it is too ugly to see; and some women have had them as large as a hand, and that is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You should clean the excess of the tentigene with your hand or a cloth, and wipe it gently; and do not let it touch too much blood, as there is no danger until it is healed; and for another char that comes out of the mouth of a marsh, and use it, and perhaps it will jump forward, and is according to the appearance of a cow, and for this reason they called the old «cow disease».
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary for you to grasp it, as we have said about the protrusion, and care for it until it is healed.
de erratique	If it is necessary for you to grasp it
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	If it is necessary for you to grasp it, as we have said about the protrusion, and care for it until it is healed.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling appears close to the surface, you can apply your fingers or a probe.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is very fine and subtle thread, and it is near the two eyes, if you hurry, and do as follows: put your two index fingers together, and the woman should be on her back, spread her legs; then form the two eyes together, until the subtle thread is removed, and is over the eyelids; then take linen, and dip it in oil, and place it on the eye, and bind the woman to a man every day, so that he cannot open.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the thread is hard and sharp, it is necessary that you soak it in the same way as vinegar leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the bone is broken, place it in its position and hold it with a bandage; and have cold medicines ready, such as dragon's blood, incense, and an abundance of frankincense; then apply a large piece of wet cloth, so that the wound does not dry out; and thus keep it long, and then apply a tent of dry linen; then treat other remedies until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the marsh there is a broken bone, cover it according to this method, unless it is an abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an abscess that has formed in the marsh, one should not touch it with fire.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that do not usually close, and when the hemorrhoids become old, they become thrombosed; and we have said in the division the similarities of them, and the signs, and I will say here those that require treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and thrombosed veins, when they are formed in the marsh, and do not appear until sensed, are only cured by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that can be felt at the edge of the marsh, are those that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore necessary to place the woman in a cold house, then stretch the altelul with tongs, and cut the copper at its roots, then powder over medicines restraining blood, such as acacia and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then boil her feet for an hour, then place her in a cold bath; if there is more bleeding, seat her in a decoction of sumac and scrapeings of green pomegranates and galls and similar things, and then take wheat flour, mix with honey and vinegar, and make an ointment on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if he faints, it's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, apply suction cups to the back and breasts without causing harm; then take the limb, and moisten it with plantain or agrimony juice mixed with old wine, and apply it to the joint.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess is ready to burst, treat the limb with poultices until it is healed; and the one called "albathir" is red and resembles a sharp chief, so cover it as I have said for the thelul; then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses from marshlands
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscesses come from marshlands, such as chancre and pustular abscess and herpes and esthenia and fistulas and hemorrhoids and chronic abscess, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	Therefore, it is necessary to say in this treatment about the chronic abscess that comes from marshlands, which is not one of the abscesses that burst; and if you know how to perform the operation with iron, look at whether the abscess is aggravated at the beginning of its appearance, and accompanied by fever and chills, and if it becomes red, then you should see.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore do not rush to pierce it, but let the pain be eased; and then place the hurt part on a seat, and have two small seats where it leans, and support it on its back and gather its feet on the sides of the leg; and let its knees be spread, and put its arms away from its knees, and tie them firmly with a good belt; then apply the bandage to the left side of the jaw, and soothe the instrument that works the mouth of the marsh, from which afterwards comes the form; and it is necessary that when you see this instrument being smoothed, you should first feel the depth of the marsh, so that what enters into the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not worsen the hurt; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the marsh with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt it; and it is necessary for him to put the horn of the instrument on top, and to stain the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	When abscesses are open and they are squeezed by hand, it is necessary to cover the head with a sponge soaked in warm water; and when the wound is empty, it is necessary to place moistened lint in the wound with rose oil or dry green oil; and place the tent from the wound to the edge of the marsh, and above the marsh and above the other clean moistened lint with hot water or hot vinegar; then after two hours of bandaging, as long as they are healed; and never lift the marsh and the wound by a poultice of hot water and honey, and then of hot water or roots of lis and aristolochia boiled; then reapply bandaging.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is closed with stitches, it is necessary to be careful not to use iron, but to treat it as we have said in the section on division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The midwife is first to the birth that she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs when you see the woman pressing down, and wanting to smell the ar: then hasten the infant to come out; therefore it is according to the natural figure, and it is its head and the shoulders with it; and when you see these signs, if you should gently press on its belly, so that the infant comes out quickly; for when it descends from its head, then the shoulders are with it, and it is washed in the womb of its superfluities by good cleaning; and this that comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it never comes above its feet, and comes often to the chest or the back, and the hands, or it comes up its belly, or sometimes, and is turned by chance onto its neck, and by other bad positions; so it is necessary for the ballerina that she be wise and skillful in these things, and if she makes a mistake and is deceived, and I will show you all the figures how one should help.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the infant comes up its head by natural issue, and the woman gives birth painfully, and her strength is weak, then let the midwife sit on a stool, or the women hold her; and apply to her nature some oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then give the midwife between her fingers the smallest spatula of which this is the shape:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and pierce the second joint, and cover it with its angle until the moisture that is inside is gone; and take the woman's belly so that the child descends, and if it does not, then you must apply a poultice of fenugreek seeds with mustard oil; then let her ingest and vomit the condition, and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour: then the child is now born.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands are dislocated, it is necessary to reset them gently and gradually; and if they cannot enter, then place the woman on a chair, and lift her feet up; then remove the chair from the ground, and tie the woman so that she does not fall during the lifting; and if the hands still cannot enter, and the child is dead, then cover the hands at the groin which was previously placed there, and extract the child, and reset them equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the issue of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes to its feet, it is necessary to place it on top; then turn it slowly and slowly until it is even; then take the feet and extend them slowly and slowly.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps up quickly, command it to hold, and make it spit out the food; if it jumps too much, God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not jump as we have said, turn it slowly and slowly until it is in the natural position.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	Then it is completely straight.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.
