And if it does not come as we have said, take a mussel shell, and oil of wormwood, and melted lead, and grind everything in the mortar; and put it on the woman's natural parts inside and outside this burning; then make her sit in a high chair until beyond the ribs; and when she is softened, take a garlic poultice, and put it on her, and let her rest for an hour; then make her sit on the seat, then make her spit and hold her mouth and nose, and lightly press her belly, for the child is now born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the child's feet above its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, one should gently place its hands on its back; then place it on its side, with its feet hanging down, and let it lie on the bed; then gently close its hands a little bit, and then grasp its hands on its belly, and remove the clothing from its buttocks until it is cleaned below; and if the child does not cry, one should move its legs up and down, then move its belly upwards, then gently stroke its back; and slowly feed the child a little bit; and command the woman to hold the child until it is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the child's hand that comes out widely with a hand
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to engineer to bring back the hand: if one cannot bring it back, then lift the woman, and go; if she cannot go, then make her lie on the bed, and unbend her legs; then soothe the muscles that I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, then make her sit on the chair, then study to bring back the hand; and bring the child according to its natural shape, and make it suckle, and command that she hold it until the child is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the child's head on its neck, and has spread its hands, and its face turned towards the back of its mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that the bath gives his hand, then turns it slowly and gently; and when it is even, if she puts on the natural oil of aloe, as we have said, then commands her to move slowly; and when you have done this, makes her sit on the seat, and commands her to defecate; and makes her spit.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same way, for all the others
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to this way for all the others, if the second one can reach your angle, until the moisture is drained; and if she can put her hand on her face and neck, cover the mouth, so it is not retained, and die the child; then give the child inside, until you have put it in the right place, and commands the woman to defecate once: then she urinates lightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the outlet of the testicles
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	It is often that twins are born, and sometimes they do not come out until three or four times; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens often.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	It is strange that they do not live, if they are not born; I know that they can be multiplied, and they are delivered by the midwife who delivers them, which is tied to the bed; and sometimes they come out as naturally as one at a time, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they are born harshly, as we have said the care should be, and if the afterbirth is subtle, and she does what she does quickly and lightly, then do so that it is good for their health.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	There are no cases where they are formed in the first or second or third or fourth or fifth or sixth or seventh, or more than ten, and all are formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the wise one, and it is best that the bailiff checks everything, because perhaps similar things happen to him; if so, do as necessary.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you care for the woman of the dead child or belly, as I have said in the division, and if there is no success, and you are forced to manual work; then it is necessary that you check whether the woman is of sound health and has no accidents or fear of death; then the woman should be placed on her back, and her arms leaning down, and her legs raised; then the minister applies two fingers to the woman's mouth, if she is lying in bed so that she is not treated for the delivery of the child; then rub the woman's mouth with moistened oil and fenugreek seeds and linseed, then apply the minister's hands with these oils and fenugreek; then lightly blow into the woman's mouth, then if she swallows the oncine that is suitable for her, and if the child is apparelled so that it descends on its head; then place the oncine in her eyes or her neck or her mouth or her palate or behind the beard or on the cheek or under the chin; and if the child descends above the feet, then apply the oncine to her teeth or her ribs or her middle; and it is necessary that the minister ties the oncine to his right hand, and places the forceps between his left thumb and index finger, and blows into his whole hand lightly, and applies the oncine in any of these ways until he comes to the empty thing; and this is the shape of the oncine:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then flip over to the other side, where the patient has the most skill, so that the extraction is equal; and then move it equally from one side to the other, to make it come out, and hold the teeth together as such, like this is the form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains, use some of his two oils, and blow them into that part, and pull out the other part; and if it does not remain, put this jawbone or higher up, and do this as much as it comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes in front of the other, and cannot be pulled back by the tightening, then you must wrap it over the bandage, as much as it comes out; then cover it at the joint of the foot or at the heel, and thus you must do in the other hand, and in both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	If the shoulder of the child is large and it is stuck in the outlet, or if it has a sharp angled assembly, then you must push the spatula-shaped instrument between your fingers, and make the angle and straighten the sharp; or you can break it with the tool called «almidach», of which the form comes with the tools or chapter that is after this one; and thus the same thing should be done with the child's head naturally; and then pull out the bones with pincers, and if the shoulder springs forward and it is held at the forceps, if they are broken, until the blood issues out; and if it cannot issue, then cover it with pieces of cloth that you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or outside the ribs, then you must prick it until the blood flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	If the infant is held above its feet, then the traction is light, and the pressure on the marsh is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	If the infant is stiff in the belly or the thigh, it is advisable to pull it out of the blanket wrapped around it; and when the belly or thigh is softened, as long as there are moistures that are there; and if the other members are broken, and the patient remains, then lift the hand over the mouth from the marsh, and pull it back to the mouth of the marsh; then bite once or twice, and pull out the tooth; and if the mouth of the marsh is retracted due to an abscess that has come, it is not advisable to force, but rather to manage moist and greasy things; and the management is plasters, and sieve in high moistening and softening.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the shoulder is dislocated above its socket, and you can put it back in place, follow what we have said about the live child; and if there is no way to do so, then try to move it by pieces, and leave nothing of the second part.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, follow what we have said about abscesses that come in the marsh; and if blood comes out, it should be tightly bandaged, and other treatments should be followed.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	I saw a woman in whose belly an infant had died, then consulted the other about that one, and he also died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, some abscesses appeared in the groin, and they swelled up so much that they burst, and then began to cause great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the patient, and I thought for a long time, and could not stop the bleeding.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied strong adhesive bandages, and then some bones were exposed, and after some time others appeared.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very surprised because the belly does not have any bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that it must be the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I examined the wound, and in it I found many bones, until the woman was much better; and then she saw the woman thus, and there remained a little blood in the wound; and I had not remembered this chapter before because when the masters find an unusual thing, they do not know how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	bring the marsh to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Here comes the form of pressure, with which we open the books; and to the two returns of the two questions of the two joints.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Therefore, the corners should be more subtle than the restrictive, and be made of flat or boxwood; and the mouth of the bottle should be two fingers wide, and the edge of the trees should be one palm and a half; and in the two joints, they should be two wedges of this same wood, which are firmly placed on both sides, half a palm or a little more; and these two wedges are inserted into the mouth of the bottle to open when turning the two corners.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, which appears more subtle and lighter, should be made of flat iron or boxwood, according to the appearance of pincers; and it should have two prongs, as you see, one palm long, and two wide; and when you want to open the mouth all the way with the instrument, place the woman on the bed, her feet together and her legs spread, then drive the two prongs into the mouth together, and hold the head of the instrument between her teeth; then work your hand with the instrument equally, according to the quantity you want to open the mouth of the patient, until the bone does what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all above, and they are multiplied in their similarities; and when the patient has them prepared, the more hasty the work, and the higher the cost for them because of their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not despise the instrument that you have not prepared, because their necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second instrument is held in childbirth, it is necessary to command the patient to hold his own saliva, and then let it out through a tube, and hold your hands on the mouth and nose; and if he spits out, well done.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take a pot, and make a sieve or cover, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the marsh, such as rue, anise, chamomile, cassialigne, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked or boiled over the fire; then put a cloth or sieve in the pot, and the other head in the mouth of the marsh, and let it steam for as long as the vapors come into the mouth; then make him spit, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second joint is broken harshly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment and is not healed, command the bath to massage her right hand in oil of sesame or musk mallow, and then put it back in its natural position, and find the second joint; and when she has found it, grasp it gently and straighten it little by little, so that the marsh does not break during extraction; but it should be moved slightly to the right and left, and then pull; it will come out and disappear.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the patient's mouth is closed from the marsh, we have said the cure of expectoration and fumigation of herbs; but if there is nothing that we have said, then guard that you do not follow the trail; but it is advisable that what is at the mouth of the marsh, that you tie to the woman's chin, then syringe with tetrafarmaçon ointment; if it will poop and be returned, and will come good; but nevertheless, when it poops if it comes bad smell to the stomach and head, and causes pain.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, it is advisable to use smoke therapies for this: none of the ancients have experienced fumigation of watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument used to smoke the woman during retention of flowers and the secondine is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is similar to a net, and one places the head subtly in the nature, and the threads wide above the fire; and the fumigations are done over the charcoal, and the lice until they are destroyed, and start another one.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who have not yet pierced the foundation, but it has been stopped by some subtle swelling: therefore it is necessary for the midwife to pierce that swelling at its proper place, and not to pierce the membrane too much, and to leave the lacing so that it does not touch; then place moistened linen on wine and oil, then the treatment of ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not reset, put or plug a splint, and let it lie for some time, and be supported as the child wants to go into the rooms.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And never comes this swelling of wound or abscess; if it covers the wound: if it is treated, as we have said of the splint.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from outside the foundation are nodulation, and grotesque that come from under the foundation or in the space of the two parts, if there is one fistula or more; and when that nodulation is old, it works, and becomes moist with blanche or subtle blood, and never are these fistulas persistent; and they are known by the fact that there is outflow or ventosity when the pain makes outflow, and perhaps some verses.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that perforate the bladder, and perforate the half of the penis; and they reach the joint of the thigh, and perforate the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the fistula passing through the base, and not passing: and it is that you should strike your finger or base on the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has twisting, if you strike a thin felt tent, or the hair of a horse, until you feel the tent or the hair at your finger; and if you do not feel it, and there is no perforation, egestion, or ventosity, as we have said: be careful that it does not perforate more; then hurry to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is persistent near the bladder or near a urinary tract, if it allows urine to pass, and cannot be cured by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is perceived near the hip joint, then the tendon is affected by the limb; if there is no twisting and the invention of the pain is not within, then it is held in place, and there is no cure by medicine or lancing; and in these persistent fistulas, there is no cure except labor, and the vanity of those who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one that is not persistent and not ancient, in hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the pain is hidden between your hands on its back; and the legs are lifted up to its knees, and its knees are bent towards its belly; then pour a bucket of water, or lead if there is twisting, until you remove or the bucket comes out.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the pain is felt around the base, then you should insert your index finger, so that it feels as if it has pierced through; and either reveal or feel between your thumb and the syringe or the needle, then remove it once you know it is positioned correctly; otherwise, there will be no benefit, as it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	It is possible to heal anyone, but this rarely happens; and the aid that is given, is that one warms the cauterizing needle according to the width of the fistula, as it was previously mentioned; and then insert it all the way into the fistula, until it reaches below the base; and do this two or three times, until you know that these charred pieces have been removed, which are similar to an arrowhead; then treat the wound with a poultice of burdock, until those charred pieces are removed, then treat the wound with an ointment of char and sealing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healthy, it is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If not, otherwise nothing can be healthy; and if he is between life and death, and does not pierce the wound at its base, and between the tent and his body a thick covering of char or syfac, and you see the fistula leading to the cure which the covering indicates; if the copper begins at the beginning of the fistula, and goes ahead of the tent, and then the cauterization after, until it comes to the top of the tent; and he will be delivered from the tent, and closed; then defecate those charred parts that seem like a quill of an eagle, and none remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if you cannot straighten it, and cut between you and the work, then cauterize with fire or medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cauterization gathers two things: that is to say, the burning of these charred parts, and the drainage of blood and the sealing of moisture; then the care of wounds dressed in butter or in thick, boiled rice, until the wound oozes, and if the charred parts are still in the wound; then care for the wound with dry, tough leather, and these medicines are dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes from just above the foundation, and is distant from the body, then press on the top or base, and look for it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and between them is the cloth or skin or charcoal where it is close to piercing, if there are no other remedies but hope and trust, by administration of one of the three methods: either cauterize as we have said, or cut just above the base, or if you can put tents and treat as first; do not remove too much from the front, so that you do not cover the foundation that holds the base, and bring the excretions out through the way you want; then cure it as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you move away that covering and uncover it when it is cut above the base, or by tent or other instrument appointed; then clean that charred part that is in the wound, as much as you can; then try to restore the wound and hold back the fistula in the part before the base: if there is a lighter thing at the pain.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are made in this way: and when you insert the probe into the fistula, it is where the base of the tent is above the skin, then take a probe that is pointed at the top like this:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And push the thread into the fistula, and push the probe through the entire thread in the fistula until it reaches the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is found on the edge of the base inside, then push out the thread from that one, so that you push your other or base; and pull the top of the thread, and bring together the two threads together, and hold them against each other, and let them stay in place for a while, until the thread covers these charred parts that are between them, and heal; then treat the wound until it is closed and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not open, try to puncture it in all the ways you can, unless it is too far back.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not matter to make the placement cover if it is too far back, and then treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spiny spinous bristle that is made for the fistula is very sharp and pointed on one side; and on the other part, not, because we do not know what we should not know, as you see here:
des emorroydes	Des emorroides
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Emorroides are of two kinds: either they are inside the fundament, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and some have blood in them, and others do not, and there are one or more, and some are outside the fundament and at the top of the fundament; but those that are outside have little moisture, and some have a little yellow citric acid or a little blood, and they have the color of the flesh; and the cure for those inside the fundament is that you command the patient to sweat in other rooms until the fundament is clean, and then open them; if you are hurried, and can do so with forceps, or hold it with your finger, then cut at their roots; and if they cannot be held by their moisture, take them with a needle, or a piece of cloth; and pull them out to both sides, then cut, and powder over some hot powders that are in the cautery chapter, or cauterize as it is said, and treat other ways until they are healed; and if the fundament cannot be opened, clean the patient with a lavage of bitter and rough substance so that it can open openly; and if the patient is not affected, and the flesh is strong from the fundament, then the cure is light; and it is that you take them with your finger or forceps, and cut, then treat as we have said, until they are healed, and do not fear the incision with a knife.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary to mend the seam in this manner: take a thread of wool, and pull it into an awl, and then pull the thread upwards and pierce the awl from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread away from the awl, and if it is too wide; and straighten the thread formally, then untie the thread, and remove the awl, and do the same with all the others, and leave one to let the excess blood out; then put above the foundation a piece of linen cloth dipped in rose oil or salve, and put above the foundation, and command the patient to rest; and then let him rest until they are healed, and when they are healed, treat them with ointment and other treatments until they are healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	dried and withered from the base
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	often found dried and withered in the intestines, and due to constriction of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary to scratch at the point of a spatula or with your nail, which does not let it moisten; then cure it as it should be while it is dry; and if it cannot be cured, start the scraping stronger than before, until it heals completely, and let it scar; then cure it as it should be while it is healed.
dou fremit	high fever
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formication is a small appearance like ants crawling on the skin, and it goes up in front; and sometimes the touch of the skin makes one feel as if one were dead from fever, and it comes throughout the body, and more so than any other part.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a quill of a goose pen, or a pen of a vulture very strong, and place that quill on the fever, until the circle around the fever encircles it entirely; then turn your hand all around the quill until you cover all around the fever, and put it in front, and remove the fever from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, do this according to the form of a rain or iron dog, and it is subtlely pushed out and pulled up:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not miss, to hold at the two, and press And if you see, if you cauterize the heat, as it is in front or chapter of cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the splint
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	No one ever made a splint of silver or tin, or lead melted or woven; and no one ever made of these small and large instruments, according to those with which they are accustomed.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, those who are to be treated in the care of children and those who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of this plaster is small and large if it is above wide, or the belly is tied according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there is an opening where the belly is tied, as you see, and the belt is inside perforated; and on one side it has two holes, and on the other one; and the belly or where one puts the medicines of a beast’s bladder or parchment, and it is perforated all around with small holes, and there is between each hole one inch of space, then sew in these holes with a thread twisted in X or around, and gather the belly as if it were a goat; and when the medicine is inside, if the belt is to the instrument before a strong thread, then plaster; and this is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and oil the head of the clyster with oil or a similar substance, then gently insert it; then the assistant applies the medicine to both hands together, until it is completely visible, then remove the clyster, and relieve the pain in his legs at once, and if the medicine wants to come out, let it come out as much as possible; and if he sleeps all night, it is a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you give the clyster in the disease of diarrhea, and the medicine wants to come out quickly, then restart it as long as it is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the callus is at its base or in an abscess, it should be removed as delicately as for a child; and this is the form of the delicate removal above where the skin is stretched:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the treatments for hands and medicines, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are different according to what they are made of, and according to the limbs or wounds that are made, and from what they are made of.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by piercing with a spear, and the cut of a sword or a dagger, or of a lance or a staff or an arrow, or similar things; or those that are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that goes through the neck, or the head, or the eye, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds of the head, because the remembrance will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes from the head or the bone is not broken, take care if it is from a piercing or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large, and you doubt slightly of an abscess: if you do this immediately cleanse the head itself if it comes from blood from the wound, and cleanse the opposite side if it is from the injured part; and avoid the evils of overeating wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to cleanse, let him eat his meat softly, and do not drink wine, and do not change his food; and put on the wound, if an abscess comes, cotton moistened in rose oil only, or in sterile wine; and if there is no abscess, put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by air, powder that I will say a little later; and if his arms have moved it, put on some ointments, as long as it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together by stitches, then bring them together by sewing, as I will say in wounds of the belly, from sewing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone, and can be moved, but only held by a little, then cover it; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore strength in the limb instead of skin, and instruct the patient to eat soft foods, such as tests and cooked grain, like chicken, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find skin or leather putrefaction, and it is not against the bone, then cover the entire putrefied part, and pour in vinegar, then treat; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, without cutting, and it cannot be stopped by medicines, then tie the artery, and if you find the vein dislocated, then tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the light remedy is to apply this powder that soothes as soon as the wound has moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is as follows: take a part of frankincense; dragon's blood two parts; fresh chalk three parts, and grind the powder finely, and apply it to the wound, and hold it together until it heals well and joins with all its skin; then bind it well, and leave it undisturbed if it does not swell; for one should not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And one should never use chalk alone when one does not have frankincense or dragon's blood, but that the wound has moved.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound has moved, immediately apply this powder; but put on some ointments digested, or flour of barley made from honey and water, as long as it boils; then treat with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the broken bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine forceps; and I will tell you about the main fractures afterwards.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound comes from the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between this and the main wound, but if the neck nerves or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is a bone, there is no other method than to let the care, and not put anything restricting, for it harms bones and makes them withdraw; and do not put anything sharp on the wound, for the substance of bones is cold, and its continuation with the brain, which is the highest member; but rather use soft medicines, such as chalk washed in warm sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and the wound washed likewise in warm sweet water, and other stones of this manner, and moist cloths.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then bandage it well and treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	If the wounds are deep and deep, and full of blood, then pierce or lower the bone; and if the artery is cut, and blood flows out, then remove the debris, and wipe, and cauterize as necessary; and if the spine of the neck is cut, or the nerves, and the conductor is kept, by which the flesh goes, if the throat is cut above the neck of the throat, and do not touch the throat but return it according to its natural shape; then gradually tighten, and leave it for some time, then cure the infections until they are healed; and if the wound has made impression on the bone, then remove it; and if there are pieces of bone, then remove them all if you can, and those that you cannot, leave until the wound can breathe, and be aligned and heal; and if the wound is fresh, then powder with the powder that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if he has bone in the wound and there is a fistula, then treat it as I have described in his chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from an arrow or a sword
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from an arrow or a sword, and the wound is deep, look to see if there are any hairs sticking out of the wound: cut them off as the pain will not go away; and if the wound is not deep, and it is fresh and full of pus, do not put powder on it or bind it in the first hour, but put attractive ointment on it twice a day; and if you do not have ointment, put old cotton in the wound to draw out the pus, and let it rest for three hours, four hours, or more; then there will be no spasms, nor will there be any trembling of the heart from elsewhere; and when you see good conditions, cut off the wound.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Heal the wounds of tents and other injuries, as long as they are healed; and if they cannot be healed, and work, then make incisions that there may be a fistula; if the treatment is as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife, and it is simple, or more or less in the back, then treat it as it should be; if it is large, stitch it up; if it is small, powder it, and if it has broken into the bone, and there are pieces, then apply the treatment to the wound, and remove the splinters if they are necessary; and if they are not necessary, leave the wound to heal, which will ease the extraction; and for other wounds in other members, as we have said, it is up to judgment.
dou derrompement dou ventre	belly rupture
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The belly rupture is great and medium and small; from the large wound, the intestines or the nerves of the intestines sometimes jump out once, by which the intestine insertion occurs; and the wound is worse, and often the small wound is worse than the large one, because one can more easily put back the intestines if they are not put back in the same way; for the intestines swell quickly when they feel the cold, so they are more easily put back if they are put back gently, and because the middle wound is worth less, because one can more easily sew up the intestine to its place than other wounds. And I say that there are four ways of rupturing the belly: the two common costures are in the costure of the belly, and the costure of the other wounds of the body and two other costures are proper to other wounds; and anyway, they are more proper with the costure of the belly, and I will say one by one and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the internal is protruding, and it is easy to replace, it is done in one of the two ways: either by the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the internal is swollen by the heat.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is hot, heat it in this manner: moisten a sponge or a handful of wool in cold water only, or cook in boiling vinegar and cider and spike, and roast the internal until the swelling is softened; and never do this with restraining, and it is better to let it cool for a while.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	When you see the swelling departing, if the intestine is moist from sharp or high and misaligned parts being cooked, because by this the entrance is close; and if it cannot enter, then make a small cut in the wound with the instrument used to remove tumors; and the first care is to still the pain, that no one should cut without great necessity, and this is the instrument for healing: if you cut from within the wound and not outside, and pull out the form.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine jumps out, if you can put it back according to its natural form in its own place, because this is good.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is wide, and it is in the part distant from the belly, it is necessary that you make the injured person lie on their back, and put their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the part distant from the belly, put the head and the foot higher than the other parts, and thus manage as I say for large and moderate wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	When the wounds are small, you should cover them with whatever is at hand, then put between your hands a healing ointment that covers the entire wound and brings together the lips; this is the common method of stitching, and it is that you hold a needle or several, according to the quantity of the wound's size, leaving a space of one finger's width from the edge of the wound, and then thread a needle with strong thread; then pierce the two layers of skin with the two needles, which are outside the skin, until you make them pierce that part, and bring together the two needles four times; then tie the thread into a double knot on both sides of the needle, then evenly stitch the wound edges, leaving a space of one finger's width, and then thread another needle; then tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and do not stop doing this according to what you have done with the needles, until the entire wound is closed; and let the needles be medium-sized, between thin and thick, because thin needles cover the entire skin, and too thick ones cannot enter well: for this reason, they should be medium-sized; and do not put the needles too far from the skin and flesh, so that they do not cut and open the wound before the sewing; then cover the edges of the needles, so that they do not bleed the injured person at night, and put bandages or cloths on the edges of the needles to keep them in place, and leave them until the wound is sewn; this method of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because it requires only one needle or two for the second stitch, which is common, and it is that you bring together the two layers of skin and the two layers of flesh to a needle with a medium-sized thread; when you have pierced these edges all four times, then re-thread the needle to the part where you started, as you would sew a dress; and leave a space between each stitch the thickness of one finger.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine after it had been there for 24 hours, and the wound was dressed after 15 hours, and I treated it, and it healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the mother thought he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with any remedy, for I was in a place where none were found, nor any medicines; and I placed gauze over the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until it healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	I will tell you the two main ways of sewing: take the needle and the thread from behind the skin; when it has pierced through the right side, place the head of the needle or the thread where you have started sewing from behind the skin, and pierce again on the other side of the part from behind the skin. The understanding of this sewing is that you sew as the furriers make the furs, and that you leave one side of the wound once, and then return to it until the sewing is all finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second way of sewing, which Galen properly calls, is such that everyone does, who assembles the two parts together naturally, and applies one of the main needles to the other main needle, in this way: stick a needle or main needle near, and make it pierce only that part alone, and leave the two threads of the main needle; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the front part just below, the two threads of the main needle; then pierce both from the front part just below, in two other needles that are on the other side; and this is the most common way of sewing.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	When these words are said, and no one testifies to them, it is necessary to sew the belly with two needles, or one in each; and it must be done by inserting one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew corsets; and it is more painful than any other sewing of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds: and it is that when you scrape the fresh wound to its blood, as soon as the wound has moved, you must replace the intestine and the cloth; then apply the powder with charcoal, and if the wound has moved, you must apply any ointment present, until the wound closes; then clean the wound and remove the bandage, and the splints, and the mirror; then treat the wound as other wounds, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, as soon as it begins to close, apply cotton, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you have no other medical knowledge in many situations where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound does not make communication with principal members, then it is necessary to treat lightly with oil of cool temperature, or rose oil, and place it around the angles, and remove from the joints; and if it causes pain or inflammation in the belly, and often happens, then you should counter it with black wine gauze, and immediately if the inflammation comes to the intestines; and pierce within, and cut out what is inside, as when it is the large intestines, it is lighter to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine called "jeun" cannot be healed when it is empty, because of the plants that are in it, and the subtlety of all the body, and its approach to the nature of the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the intestine jumps out of the wound, put it back in place as soon as possible; and if it is old and turned black, tie the leg that has turned black, because there are veins and arteries inside; then cut what is between the limbs, and hang the two ends down from the part away from the wound until the extraction when the intestine falls, and the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	of the breaking of a boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is punctured, and the wound is small, if it can be closed in some men, because I saw that one man was gutted or pierced by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and became prolapsed and became a fistula, and in this way there was discharge and ventilation; I placed care according to what I knew, and did not cease to subtilize until it was healed, and the men seemed healthy.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him sewn up, I doubted that the pain was not in his intestine; and there was no harm, but he remained in better conditions, and he drank and ate; and some experimenters said that when one has a small wound in the intestine, it should be closed in such a way: take a large needle, then gather the lips of the wound, and when the needle is over the mouth, place it across both lips, so that it holds his mouth open; then cover the wound with the other needle, and hold it so that he cannot move, then use the other needle in that way as before, until the wound is completely closed.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the shoulder blade is burned in the intestine, and no harm comes to the wound, and it can be stitched with a thin silk thread that is taken from the intestine of an animal, in this manner: take the end of the intestine thread that is very dirty, and then tie it to the end of this silk thread, then pull the thread into the needle, and through the intestine, and stitch it in the tear; and this method of sewing is no more than according to the way of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the intestines, there is no remedy or cure, only subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or that it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	All wounds or abscesses, when they become covered, are universally called "fistula", and specifically when they are cut open and reopened.
