Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to its hard and white scarring, where there is no pain, and it is cut open like the quill of an eye; and sometimes it clearly opens, and sometimes deeply; sometimes little, and sometimes enough; and I have spoken about it in the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed, and there is no scar, except by one of the EIGHT causes: that is to say, by the smallness of the blood or flesh; or by its malice; or because there is hard scar tissue underneath and on the lips, that does not allow new scar tissue to grow; or there is too much discharge; or the wound is poisoned, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is in the form of pestilence; or because the property in the region is late digestion, and late healing, and flows naturally; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, signs, and cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary for me to inform you of the treatment of fistulas that are made by the work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Fistulas can occur in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come to great veins, and to arteries, and to nerves, or to the face, or to the intestines, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and if they come to the property of the principal member, and similar things.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all fistulas of this kind are difficult to heal, and there is only labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come from the joint that I have said, and you have confidence in the cure, and you know how to treat it, if it is a straight fistula, take a lead or iron tent, if the fistula is crooked, take a subtle tent of plaster, because the plaster does not stick to the twists; and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot well cover it with tents, squeeze it through one of the openings, for the moisture will come out from one opening to another, and cleanse it; then carefully apply a clean bandage to it, that you know whether there is bone or nerve, and if it is deep and far from joint, nerve, artery, vein, or any of the places I have mentioned, cut according to what I have told you, and remove the cause and the corrupted flesh that is inside; and then treat it until it is healed, and if the fistula is very deep in the right place, cut as much as you can, then put soft tents of medicine at the head of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluity that remains at the bottom; and then apply ointments of clean, wholesome charcoal, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, cut.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or nerve does not cause pain in the principal members, as we have said; and if the tooth is exposed, and there is decay and blackness, then remove the corruption until it is completely removed, then treat the other things in order until they are healed; and if they are not healed, and remain as before, do not go further: if it is exposed and you want to remove as much as possible, expose the tooth and remove all the decay, then restore the tooth; and if it is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, it is because the corruption is too far advanced, that you cannot do anything; if there is no other remedy than patience; and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can extract it with forceps, if the instrument is suitable for this, and if there are many bones, take them all out, and do not leave any behind; and if the moisture makes it go against you, and there is no error or fear, if you cope with moisture and heat, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	If you cannot remove them within an hour, place something stinking on the wound to draw out the pus, and leave it until the flesh is surrounded by bone, and then they will be more easily set; and if it is a large bone, such as a leg or thigh, raise it so much that the corruption is completely detached from the bone, then cover the wound; and if there is a great part of the corruption left, and comes near to the end of the bone; if it must be covered and covered with everything near the corruption, and then cure it until it is sound; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	The youths were around thirty years old, who had pain in their leg from a cause that came from within the body, so that the matter came to the leg, and was filled with a large abscess, and there was no cause to open; but the foolish ones opened it so high that the abscess opened, and there were many matters flowing out, and became a fistula, and there was much pain due to the body's humors; and many more sought cure within two years, and there was no remedy in the art of hands, so that I was called, and saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating him, and what flowed through the fistula was great; and the body became red from the young man, and had a yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these holes, and then I searched all the holes, and found that one was coming into contact with the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then stood there, and dug into one of the holes until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it rotten and perforated, and the corruption was coming to the bone from within; I saw that what appeared on the rotten bone, and thought that there was no other corruption, except for what I had seen; and I began to treat the wound with salves for a long time, but I could not heal it; then I returned, and discovered the bone as before, and found the continuous corruption in the bone, and saw it, and then I removed it, and I could not heal the limb; but I could only wrap around a palm of the bone, and treat it entirely, then I returned it to salves; it was healed and healed quickly, and did not need to start the work again except for the weakness of the pain, which could not bear, and for the fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation of blood often caused harm, but he was completely healed, and in the place of the bone grew a hard callus, and it was of good disposition and had no harm or contradiction throughout, neither to the other nor to the coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be done in this way: take a bandage, and stretch it at the head of the bone that opens, and command that it be extended upwards; and put another thicker bandage than the first one on top of the callus that is on the bone, and extend the head, so that you remove the rotten callus from behind, and expose the callus above the part where you want to be, that it does not break the callus; and put a poultice or a tablet away from the bone to cover the rotten callus; and it should be done so that one can see and feel the corruption, and it should be done again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If the tooth is rotten and does not open, and the decay is in the middle or in one part, tear off the entire clothing; then put the silk from outside, and then sew from one part to the other the decay, and let the silk be of the same length as the decay, as we have said; and if the decay is in the joint, cut the joint where it is corrupted, and sew the bone or what it contains on the other side; and if the decay is in the continuation of the two joints, there is no other way than to cover it; and if the decay is at the tip of the finger or toe, this thing is very difficult, but nevertheless you should inquire how it opens; and clean it in all ways that you can, but do not let the vein or nerve go against it; and consider that the saw and the sutures to cover these bones are many, according to the shape of the bones and the appearance of the teeth, and their size and subtlety, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness; and for this reason you should prepare a tool for each kind of work, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of diseases; so consider the tool that you have in accordance with what it should be.
dou feu	with great fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The joints will rot either due to their own decay, or due to lack of use; and when you have medicated that corrosion with the cure of medicines, and it does not improve, then you must amputate that member up to the joint where the corrosion comes from, so that the pain may escape by death, or by malice, which is greater, due to the lack of the member; and the signs are that the member becomes black, so that it seems as if it were burned by fire, and afterward it becomes blacker, then those corrosive members spread from one member to another, and take hold throughout the body; if you hurry to amputate, and if the corrosion is at the head of the foot, then cut, and do not give it any space for the hand to come.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	If it comes from the hand, if the cloth is at the joint, so that the corrosion does not reach the arm; and if it comes to the arm, if the cloth is at the shoulder; and if it passes the shoulder, it is death, and there is no remedy except the quantity of its virtue; and thus do all that the corrosion comes or pierces: if it comes to the first joint, if the cloth after the other joint; and if it comes to the piercing, if the cloth pierces the whole piercing; and if it goes up the leg, if the cloth is at the hip joint; and if it comes above the hip, there is no other remedy than to let the hurt limb hang down and out, and stretch some ministers one of the two ends, and some other ministers the other end, and uncover the char between the two ends to the width of a span, until the bone is exposed; then the cloth or bandage, and put a piece of linen on each part so that the bandage does not touch the clean skin, and it comes to the hurt limb other injury and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	If blood comes out when you are working, cauterize the wound quickly, or put some powders that stop bleeding; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bandage the injured limb with a clean cloth, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in a very difficult case: he had a black spot that seemed like burning fire, and that corrosion first appeared on his face, taking over the whole face; and when the honorable people saw the corrosion, they covered the face, and was healed; and later on, the corrosion appeared on the other side of the hand, and it came to me, and I put some things that reflect after cleansing the body, and could not stop the corrosions; and he thought that I would cut off his hand, and I did not want, because I had hope of reflecting the matter; and he also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would not die, for the power of the man was weak; and he gave up all hope, and returned to his land, and covered his hand, and was healed; and I have not told this except for the purpose of showing how to do other things, if one has such a case.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Never does an abscess form in a bone that is too lean, and it delays for so long that it causes a great collection of pus; then it bursts and pierces, and the pus escapes, as if it were a vessel; and the skin above is also as thin as cloth, and does not corrode the bone, nor the nerve, and such diseases are called "sinuses", and are not called "fistulas"; but if it is so long that it reaches the bone on the outside, it is called a "fistula"; and the skin is that you cut all around, and immediately when it is thin, as if it were cloth; and it does not corrode for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	If the skin is hard and corruption has not yet set in, and the skin is charred, then the following remedy should be used: check if the breasts are large, and the nipples have a foul odor, then use the Egyptian remedy as follows: take equal amounts of oil, aloe, and litargire, heat them together in a small vessel over the fire until the medicine turns red and has the same thickness as honey; then take as much of this mixture as needed, make it into a paste with water or honey, and apply it to the breasts, and bandage the wound; leave the medicine on for two hours, then remove it by sponging; do this many times until the breasts are clean and healed; if the pain is too great, and the Egyptian remedy and water with ashes of grapevine cannot be tolerated, then use a mixture of water and honey with a little litargire, or water and melted honey with properties to clean and wash, and wine that makes the flesh sour; after doing this, if you are sure the breasts are clean, then apply a definite poultice made with rose oil and wine; or use some other remedies and ointments as I have described for treating wounds; if the nipple is small and the poultice cannot enter, then enlarge it slightly with a needle, and place an Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment inside; if the wound is too large, then leave it alone until it can be covered by the poultice or bandage.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	When the bone is broken, do not let it hang loose; and if you cannot cover the wound as you see fit, arrange it in such a way that the bone corre to the lowest part that is there, for when the bone is broken, do not let it hang loose, and if you cannot cover the wound as you see fit, arrange it in such a way: that the bone moves gently downwards, and leave nothing of the bone; and take consolidative medicines to put on the wound, and lay it on the cloth that covers all the wound; then cover the forces at the place of the bone injury a little larger than the first, for they are tightly tied on the other cloth according to the amount of the injury, and put it on the wound to align the bone, and do not remove the large cloth until after many days once; and the one who is on the cloth over the bone, often removes it to align the bone, and see what comes from the wound, whether it is poison or little or enough, or digested, or undigested; and take warning if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been spread in a certain way and you see the nature that goes over the cloth, then remove the bandage and approach health; and then remove it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you remove the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the bandaging.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breasts are not well digested after many hours, force them to be straight so that they do not become misshapen.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if the subtle poisons are cut after long time, do not despair of health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are men who take long to heal their wounds, and those who do the opposite; and if the breasts are not well digested after many hours, force them to be straight so that they do not become misshapen; and if the breasts are slow to harden, and are distant, then use medicines that are moist in substance but dry in virtue, such as ointment diaphoretic, for it has a great part of vitriol, and this is the last medicine; take ointment diaphoretic, and make it with rose oil, and the dew of old wine equal in substance; then cook and use it; and the same thing is done with honey when it is cooked and grows thick, where ointment diaphoretic is not present, or take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind them, and the powder on the honey as it is over the fire; then apply it to a cloth, and place it on the breast, and never administer an aristologue long, and roots of lily celestial, which is also like flour of wheat and centoire; and use simple or composite: grind them, and make powder, and put on the honey that I have said, and use it; and if the cure is long and not cured by this cure, then force the corruption to be removed, and make an impression in the bone, or in hard members, or in limbs; then the cure of the cure of fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises from the pouch under the nail of the hand, or foot, or sometimes in other places; and when it is opened, and no care is taken, if the abscess spreads, and corrodes and drips pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and perhaps corrodes it entirely; and then there are corrosions just above the bone, until there is painful putrefaction, and the affected part is red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	If you treat it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help much, then you must cut away all the excess that remains of the nail, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauterization is a great help if the bone is healthy and the joint is sound; but if the joint is close to the flesh, and begins to prick and smart, then you must remove the flesh from around the joint that does not hurt it, and place it high up, and gently and carefully cut off the remaining flesh, and apply hot and corrosive medicines until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cut it out and remove it, for as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot be healed; and if you see the other one becoming corrupted, then cut it off at the joint as previously described, and treat it until it is healed; but if it is fierce, and bleeding, and causing great pain, then first cleanse it; then carefully cut out the joint with a sharp knife, and be careful that the cut does not come into contact with the flesh that is outside the joint, for the hairs would cause too much pain; and if it happens, then apply something to soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of a sore hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The pain that arises in the hands of some men by chance is all charred, and by chance it has a tail or where it has bones, and once it has an angle, and none of them are born at the root of the joint, or where the birth is in any of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those who are born in no part of the finger do not move, and those who are born at the joint of the finger may move; the tail of the charred one is light, in a way: cut it at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those who are born at the root of the joint are difficult to cure: if you have the copper.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In those who are born or should be at the back, it is necessary that you first cut the rounded part of the bone to the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable silk for this, then care for it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The same things that come together in two ways, either by birth or by wounding, or by burning of fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If it is necessary that you cut the wound, so that the part that should return to its natural form; then put between two tents or cloths moistened in rose oil, so that they do not stick together; or you put between two pieces of thin plaster, until the wound is healed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If one of them comes with their palm, then apply it as it should be.
des vils	of the poor
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are large, swollen, full of superfluous melancholic humor, which come from many members of the body; and more so in the legs of those who walk and work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Then you must administer them purgative of clyster, and then the healthy one from the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cure of iron is done in two ways: one way is to apply it and remove the black blood; and the other way is to open the vein and draw all the blood.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The belly is done in this way: first, the leg of a high, very hot fire, until the large intestine is not subtly removed, then strain the leg with the bad side down, below the chest to the part of the genitals; then cut the vein in the belly, in one, two, or three, of a wide incision, then release and draw out the black blood from your hand, from one to the other, until so many can be borne by the strength of the bad side; then tie it, and command that he be given food seasoned with black pepper; and then repeat the evacuation and cleaning when the veins are flat, and no longer bleed.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	To treat the shoulder joint, if there is much hair, first shave the affected area, then place it in warm water until it becomes red and the veins swell; if you do not have warm water, heat it over a fire, and apply it to the affected area, either directly on the skin or on a cloth, at the top of the shoulder, or on the side of the arm; then rub the skin with oil, and scrape off any dead skin until it appears red and black, like a white cord; then bathe the area in warm water until it is clean, and then apply a light bandage to the affected area, and repeat this process three times; then scrape the skin again, and apply a new bandage, as you have done before; then apply another bandage, or more if necessary, and lift it up, and apply it to the second wound; then stretch the wound from one size to another, until it is completely healed, and then apply a bandage; and if you cannot pull and lift it, use a strong needle and thread to pull and lift it, and bathe the area in warm water, and turn your hand back and forth, until it is all done; be careful not to wrap it, because if it is wrapped, it cannot be pulled or lifted, and it will cause harm to the affected area; and when you have treated it, apply a soft cloth soaked in wine and rose oil to the wound, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	If the vision is blurred and twisted and covered altogether, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must torture it greatly, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have previously described.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of iron used to cover the eye is curved and does not cut into the vein; it has a large curve, because if it were fine, it would cut into the vein, but if it is large as we have said, this is the form:
de la voinne civile	of the vein of the eye
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is inserted in the legs, in the hot parts where there are no herbs or trees, and in dry land where there is no moisture; and by chance it may arise elsewhere than in the legs, and if it comes out through the skin, as it does from within the flesh and muscles, insert between the skin and the meat.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this wound are such that it comes in the leg a very great inflammation, then the limb changes, and the wound begins to protrude, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the wound is open, it is necessary to wrap around a piece of cloth of one and a half spans wide by two spans long, and the nose, and leave the cloth on the leg, and every time it is not under the influence, if it wraps around the cloth, and the nose; and if it is too long, then cut part of it, and wrap the remaining part, and do not cover it at its root, until it is all out; for if you cover it, it will retreat into the leg, and cause abscess and infection or damage to the limb, and severe disease; therefore it is necessary that it be treated little by little close to the head, and nothing remains or scars; and this wound never occurs when it is treated with palms of long, or ten, and some have come to me, to which it issues from ten palms of length, and when you cover it, if the pain or pus, and perforate it close to the bottom, so that everything comes out; and let the matter that is inside be drained, and administer medicines in a jar for infection any day, then cure as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes at this vein, and especially when it opens in the joint of the little finger, or the big toe, and much pain comes, and it jumps back; therefore, as we have said before, you should do as follows.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	between the skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "cow disease," because it often affects cows, and it is a small worm that grows between the skin and flesh, and goes up and down the body, and can be felt moving from member to member, until it burrows into the skin where it went, and jumps out; and it is caused by some humors, such as come from snakes and worms and tapeworms or intestines; and people doubt its harm, because as it goes through the body, and goes up to the head, and comes to the brain, perhaps it may enter, and destroy the brain; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see the patient and treat them, it is necessary that you hold the limb above and away from a very tightly bound place, then cut across and pull it out, and if it comes out in front of the char, and you do not extract it, then cauterize with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm it does is that it spreads oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming or near the oil, hold it away from it, then cut across and pull it out; and it is necessary to use the medicine of unguents for the evil humors of the body, and if it becomes swollen due to bad food.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of pain coming from the windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to some members, and then moves from member to member; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and I discovered one of her arms, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and soon afterwards, I saw it grow as high as an arrow in the shoulder, faster than anything, like live silver when it cuts through flesh; the pain departed from that arm, and went into the shoulder, and then a little afterwards, it spread throughout the body, until it reached the other arm; then she told me that she turned inside out around the body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly at how she moved from one limb to another, for I had never seen this disease in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had only heard of people moving from one limb to another in pain, but I had not seen it like this before; and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins were exposed, and because that constraint appeared; and it did not appear in the same way to those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see this disease and the pain that she feels as we have said, if it appears to you like this, then hold the limb above and below firmly, and then cauterize the limb; and if you do not see it at your eyes, then treat the cause of the constraint of the veins, such as fetid pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are various, according to their resemblances and according to the materials they are made of.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is such that there are arrows with large points, small points, barbed points, and soldered points; and there are those with two angles, and those with tails, and those with pieces; and the one that pierces any member in a way: whether it pierces a principal member as the neck, head, heart, lungs, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it pierces any of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, appears: then you must extract this arrow, for death comes after in many ways; and when this bad sign does not appear, and the arrow is not stuck in front, then pull it out, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the signs of the head when the arrow pierces and perforates the bone, and the sinus that is above the head, are blindness and dizziness and vertigo and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps without force of the nose, or of the ears; and perhaps also the speech and voice; and the white discharge from the wound like pus, and also like boiling water; and if these signs appear to you, then take care of the patient, and remove the arrow if it is not embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The symptoms of the shoulder when it is dislocated or out of place are that it is near the right breast, and it feels as if it has been stuck in a hard thing, without being able to move; and by chance the shoulder moves like the wings of a chicken, and there is black blood, and cold sweat, and syncope: therefore without doubt the patient will die.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign that the arrow has not been pulled out is that without any pain, bubbles come out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the limb changes color, and the patient breathes high and seeks for the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrowhead is embedded in the clothing on the lower part, it is behind the small ribs; and it causes great pain and shortness of breath; and moves all the members of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrowhead pierces the stomach, by chance if something undigested from the meat does not come out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrowhead pierces the abdomen, and nothing comes out through the intestines, there is no hope in the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrowhead pierces the bladder, and the urine comes out and flows out, and the pain is very great: it is likely that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, such as the hand and neck and throat and shoulder and elbow and back and spine and hip and knee and leg, and similar members, are safe according to many positions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or the artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because of what you were doing differently.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to the man who had an arrow in his thigh at the root of the knee: I tried it, and took it out from another side of the ear grease, and he was healed without pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And in one case, an arrow was shot into the oil paper outside the mat, and the arrow was removed, and it could only be reached to the tip towards the face, and the arrow was large like a Turkish bow, entirely made of iron without ears; the case was healed, and no bad accidents came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And an arrow was shot into the neck of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears: I cut off the barbs, and carefully removed it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And an arrow was shot into a man, who had it in his head or belly, and I thought he would die; and after he had passed thirty days without changing his condition, I cut across the arrow, and twisted it, and removed it, and no bad accident came to him.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you wish to heal a man who has an arrow stuck in him or on his back, and the wound was sewn up from above; and the arrow remained inside, and did not change its natural positions, nor found any harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And if you wish to heal another man who had an arrow stuck in his face, and the wound was sewn up; and it remained like that without suffering great pain; and many similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And if you remove an arrow from the man of the prince, the king, who had it in his neck, and was slightly leaning to the right side; and the wound was completely healed, I was called to cure after it had been three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If the wound is very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I applied a very thin tent to it, and I did not feel anything; but he felt pain and pricking in his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the point of the arrow; I put the eyebrow under the eye, with an attractive ointment, because the eyes do not swell; and I saw the arrows in the eyes.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the ointment again, and immediately healed the wound, and the pain lasted a long time, until he felt the arrow inside his nose; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I placed the medicine of ague corrosive on the wound by hand, as long as it was open, and I tried to touch it, and felt the tip of the arrow that was stuck in the limb; then I applied the medicine of ague corrosive through the opening of the wound until the head of the arrow appeared visible to me; and it passed well through the four months, and then I extracted the arrow, and the one from my side and the other, and could not get it out; therefore I did not stop and ingeniously devised ways of using instruments, until I got a good one on the day after, according to the form that will come at the end of this chapter, as long as I used it, and closed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the miracle worker judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored: I restored it then, and it was sewn up, and the wounds were healed entirely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you put your cure above what I do not say, for the books cannot comprehend everything; but the wise masters know well many things, and above what is present and lacking, they find new work, and new instrument, in the understanding of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not issue from the members in which they are embedded except in two ways: either by the way they enter, or by another part; and the one that pierces through the way it enters is an arrow that has entered into their flesh, and it has never happened now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if she does not jump now, let her stay until the charcoal is poured around, and the issue is alleviated; and similarly, if she is stuck in the bone, and cannot exit, let her stay thus for some time, and move her every day; and then she will jump, and if she does not jump, pierce all around until the forest is subtilized, and then remove it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and goes towards one of the bellies of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have mentioned cause pain to the patient: do not remove it immediately, but leave it until it is even after some time, because if the arrow comes towards the face, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not embedded in the bone only, and does not come to the surface, and remains there for several days without any bad event, then the engine of drawing should be used.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is very deeply embedded and cannot be drawn out, then administer tar as I have told you; then treat the limb until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is embedded in the body where it cannot be seen, then apply tar to the entire tent; and if you feel it, then remove it with any suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, then leave the arrow in place until the wound is large enough to be removed; and remove the arrow if you can, and if it has ears that hold it in place, then cut off the part that is deeply embedded on both sides where you can, and then break or pry open the ears of the arrow until you can remove it; and be careful not to break the arrow when removing it.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	If you cannot do it once, if the leg is completely inside the thigh, then cut it off, for the extraction has failed.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the flow of blood contradicts what we have said about the treatment in its chapter, then withhold the incision of the nerve and the vein, and proceed as you can draw out the arrow safely, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and put the hairs according to the form it was in when the arrow fell, for this is the greatest help that there is, and if you cannot, then follow what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, where it opens nothing of it, or the skin is swollen in a place so that one can see or feel it: cut then above, as much as the tongs can take, and then extract it: if it now shoots out.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, then round your hand and push it into the bone, until it enters the bone, and expands the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, then leave it and then restart the extraction until it comes out; and if there is an arrow in it, and you see that it is stuck, and you are administering gently, if you are administering the instrument with a hook, so that the point of the arrow enters the hook's hair; and then pull out, and if the arrow is hooked, then push the instrument into the hook entering in, to facilitate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is lodged, it is necessary that you cut out all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as it should be.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow has penetrated or stuck in the belly or bladder or ribs, and it is close, and you can cut through it, then cut across it; do not cut into the vein and nerve, and then extract it, and then treat the wound as necessary; and the treatment until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the hooks used to extract arrows resembles an owl's beak, and here is its form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, medium, and small, depending on the amount of blood.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the needle is also like the beak of a bird, to pierce at the tip of the blood, like this:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the needles for pricking and for drawing is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Veins common to the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	Of the veins that are common to the body, there are 31, of which there are sixteen heads, that is: two battans that are after the ears, which are called the "herbech"; and the two arteries that are in the two temples appearing; and two veins that are in the two arms of the two eyes, which are called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the front; and the vein that is at the top of the nose; and the two jugulars that are on the neck; and the two veins that are in the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and two veins that are outside the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that are commonly opened are five in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it is on the right side, and it is called "the main vein" by the people; and the middle one is called "the basilic", and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilic, and it is called "the main vein" by the people; and the basilic is on the left side, and it is called "the vein of the belly", and it is above the fossil, and it is that which is opened, which opens clearly above the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the savathe is the vein that is between the earlobe and the ring, and it is in the right arm; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is outside the bone of the right side costeit, and the second one is at the knee of the left costeit; and the vein which is called "the neck", which is at the knee of the other costei; and in the other leg are three veins.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The first sentence is not provided for translation. Please provide the next sentence.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre. Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The treatment of the vein in the forehead is as valuable as the treatment of headache diseases, facial ancient maladies, and migraine; and the quality of the instrument is such that the pain is strange, twisting the neck until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosser", which has this form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point above the vein, and hold it with your hand or another thing, and let the blood issue according to the quantity you see; then release the neck from the pain, and tie the vein until it is healed and not once in a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Therefore, it is not necessary for the flames to be too hot; and the straight angle, because the bone is close, and perhaps breaks the flames when they are thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The straight angle of the second veins that are in the two armpits helps with the elbow, and the wrist, and the hand, and the shoulder in the oil, and in diseases of the face; and the quality of their straight angle is such that the pain is strained by twisting from any direction, as before; then the straight angle, and let the straight angle be at a slight angle, a little long of the flame, a little wide, because there is no char.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is thin, it may break; then correct the bleeding, as much as you have skill, and then tie with a thread, and bind it well.
