Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The vein of the nose should be bled if it is too full, and if there is a fever, and diseases of the face, such as headaches and redness that comes to the face, and always when it is old; and the quality of the bleeding is that the pains are relieved, then strain the nostril with your right hand, and take the thin flame long, and put it on the lip in the space between the two noses, because the vein does not open well, and the blood will begin to flow; and do not move too much, and bleed according to your need, then tie it for one night, because it is soon restored; and this is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The salve of the second kind helps to narrow the veins, and at the beginning of menstruation, and with many diseases, and with impetigo, and with corrosions, and with herpes, and estiomenes; and the quality of the salve is that the pains strangely pull their necks from one and the other, as we have said; and so the masters are above the chief of the pains, and the pains sit on one seat, then clean the vein along the long one, a little broadly, then drain the blood temprementally, or as much as the matter requires; then do the other side in the other vein, then unloose the lien, and strain the veins gently, that the pains do not strangle; and leave it just before morning, that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the health of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the liver above helps to cool in the mouth, and prevents tooth decay, and cracks in the lips, and dry throat and inside.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of this health is to make the pain disappear in front of you, and hold its neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and they are known by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that small black veins are around them: compare both, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, compare the largest of each part, and do the same with the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same way.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the health of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The health of the veins that are outside the tongue helps after the health of the head, and it is the narrowing of the throat, and diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the healer is that the illnesses cease between your hands before the sun, and you lie down the tongue, and look outside each side one black vein: healthy then both, and do not move too much, for outside are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the ear that are commonly healed are healed in two ways: either by pinching all the flame in a wide manner, or by cutting thinly as if they are slicing, and it is called "anesil"; and they are wide and thin according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame is very famous, and is as wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it has the task of opening veins that are closed flat with large blood clots visible, and that contain large clots and turbulence; and this is the form of the flame siphon.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more subtlely pointed, and is for cleaning fine veins, where there is fine blood clots.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The cleaning of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are outside the neck, and in the collarbone, and in the ribs, and in the stomach; and it is necessary for the cleaner to clean properly, and to avoid the artery that is outside.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	If he cuts the artery, and blood flows out, then it should be cooled, as I have said; and it should not be pinched with the fire, but cut off as I have said.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica does not open clearly, then it is necessary to extract and change it; or you want any rain of it, or you save in its place the vein from the arm: it opens clearly; and it is cut off with the fire as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you know the vein of the sinew, then it is necessary to extract and touch the vein until you know the tendon; then sign the vein of the elbow, and then bind the arm, and cut the vein with the fire as we have said; and beware that you do not cut into the artery when you see the vein swell, for it is the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it emerging high as the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, it is from an artery: then quickly place your hand longwise, then remove your hand without stopping, which has often been done; hold the arm still, and let the pain not move it; and do so with fear, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stopped, and it hurts, and the medicine is not present, then cut the artery if it opens, for the main part of the wound heals; and stop the blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a small piece of honey, and make it into a poultice, and take one half and apply it to the other side; if it is not stained, it is good; if not, then the cure, as we have said, with powders that stop bleeding; and the staining does not occur in many positions for the small wound of the sore, and the position of the limb of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vein in the middle is helpful because it treats blood from the top and the body, since it is composed of basilica and cephalic, as we have said; and it is necessary for the vein to be pricked through all the nerves that are out, and if it does not go too deep, and he finds the nerve, and he inflates and the wound is stained, and perhaps cannot be healed; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any man due to its subtlety, then you should use the vein from the instrument anesil; and protect the nerve to your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has a vein between the two nerves, make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The cleansing of the cephalic vein helps, as it draws blood from the head, and helps with the eyes; and it is necessary to cleanse by pricking with a lancet or a needle, for this is the safest of all veins, as it has no nerve or artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is necessary to ask for the lightest vein, and not to cause any harm if it is not found the first time, and then start again; and sometimes the veins swell in some people, but it does not cause any harm the first time.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health depends on your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about health is that healing is only done to maintain health and to ward off diseases that may come; and health should be done in one of the three ways that are either costly: namely, cephalic, fasting, and basilic; and if you should heal at the beginning of spring, autumn, and winter after fasting, when the sign of repletion appears; and if you should heal on the first day or the third, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The salve that is administered for diseases has no fixed time determined, but rather it should be applied as needed, at all hours and in all circumstances; and one should not sain the children until they are fourteen years old, nor a pregnant woman except during the first three months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	One should also not sain the elderly who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when anyone wishes to sain, in whatever manner they do so, it is necessary for them to first cleanse the intestines of a light clyster, if they have too much feces retained, so that the veins do not draw the superfluous noxious humors into the principal members; and one should not sain those who are too full of meat, nor those who are bloated, as much as they may be, nor hydropiques; and if one wishes to sain after a colic attack, vomiting, diarrhea, and frequent pregnancy, travel, watch, and fasting, and all the virtues of the arm or body; then subtly draw out the humors, as long as they are not too thick, by foods and drinks and medicines, if you have them; then take a bath, if nothing prevents it, to further purify the blood, and sain from the vein in the morning, as we have said; and guard against that day of work, and pain, and luxury, and similar things; and be linked and joined, and let the saining be higher than that which is given, and let the arm be rubbed twice or three times, then gently move the joint above the middle, for when it is too stiff or loose, it cannot be corrected; and then rub the arm with the hand until the veins swell, and feel the pain; then moisten the saining with a drop of old oil, then put its proper amount on their right hand over the vein of the arm where they wish to sain, that the vein does not fail to draw.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	Because there are veins that flee as quickly as strings to the leech, and there are some that are plain of moistness, so that when one puts on the flame, they draw back from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus are those; and if he opens the vein, then the wound is too tight, because it is necessary that the leech be advised in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good; but if not, then he should start again a little below that vein or above the hand, as long as the veins are not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the joint is inflamed, and the pain subsides within one or two days, do not bind the arm tightly: perhaps it may become infected; do not enter water, then restart the healing process if it pleases him; and if the wound is small, or without a deep cut, gently and subtly apply the cauterization directly to the wound itself, as you have seen that there may be less blood than you expected, if you trust in that wound alone to the full flame; and work gently, provided that the joint is inflamed.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	And if you see the joint swelling, do not restart the healing process, and put a little oil on it, for it reduces the flow of blood, and is soothing to this joint like the oil; and thus administer oil in every healing, as you heal the wounds, to stop the flow of blood; and this also makes a triangular and bandage of muslin, when it is put on the joint; gently apply it to the wound and separate it when it becomes too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	If there are large abscesses that often occur, even when they are not drained except at this time or when the vein opening is small, hurry and place a soft sponge soaked in boiling and cold water on the limb for an hour; and it is necessary to do this after the discharge of the blood from the vein, and if it remains on the limb for any time without turning black or green, do not remove it; and if you see, place anything of aloes or myrrh mixed with honey or mustard on it.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there is an abscess and the appearance of the sinus of the basilica: therefore place your hand on it, and if you feel the limb very soft under the pressure of the hand, this is a bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, do not put anything on it that we have said, for perhaps you will cut into an artery; but apply a dry poultice to harden the limb, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to the quantity of its virtue and the color of the wound.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it bleed until it becomes red; and if you see it swollen, let it bleed until it becomes thinned out; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is appropriate for one who is strong and able to extract blood, to make a larger wound and make the flames wide; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and heal it quickly and often, and it should be healed by cutting across, not by pinching; and this method of healing is safe from the corruption of blood and the breaking of nerves, and it is better than healing by long or wide cuts.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And to the one who has a weak heart, it is appropriate to give bread soaked in juice of crushed pomegranates; if it is heated, take three or four drops of fresh blood and mix it with the juice. And if it is of cold complexion, before the sweat change the bread soaked in honey syrup, or aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and coriander, and a strong-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints during the sweat, after much blood loss, it is appropriate to give him a broth of charcoal, and a subtle-smelling syrup, and use the other things that we have said in the chapter or section on syncope, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to exercise his arm, and strengthen it again, if necessary, when it is weakened by great injury, that he should strengthen it gradually, according to the quantity of its continuous virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he wants to exercise his arm after the first strengthening, and he has strong pain, then he should strengthen it again seven hours after the first strengthening, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if he wants to strengthen on the other side, then he should strengthen it again on the second day or the third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For he has much blood inside the body which is already hot, and causes fever; so you should draw out a great quantity, and widen the vein until it bursts; then you should fulfill all the conditions of strengthening, and place your hand on his pulse as he strengthens, that the dead does not return in the place of the pulse, and this has often happened when the strengthening is neglected; and you should not do it unless you see the arm becoming loose, and draw out blood the second time, and the vein is closed, that you press firmly against; or if it is swollen, that you extend the arm quickly, for this would be bad; but let him rest until he strengthens the second time; or you are at the tip of the flame, as long as the blood that is frozen in the vein of the arm does not come out, and put a little oil on it to cool, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the swelling is present, let it be and do not hold it tightly until the abscess is calmed down.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessary to draw out blood from the second vein, if the healthy one in the same limb or another arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins are healthy in place of the main vein because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the method of this vein is that if the hairs are pricked at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow; and if the swelling is present, let it be and do not hold it tightly until the abscess is calmed down.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The salve of the hand from the right side cures all diseases of the liver, and this is how: strain the hand, and boil in hot water until the blood flows out, if one can see it; and if the salve is against the direction, and if you apply it with everything together, it will not hurt anything; and do not move too much afterward, because the nerves are all exposed to the bone, and then put the hand in hot water, if it is not frozen in the wound, and it cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the arrow as much as is necessary for you, put oil on the wound and tie it with a thread quickly, and thus do to each one.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The healthy sign of the left hand is valuable for the disease of the mouse, and do everything as I have told you on the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The healthy sign of the shoulder is valuable for all diseases that are outside the body, such as marrow diseases, and retention of urine, and disease of the knees, and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its healthy sign is that diseases are poured out in sharp hot, and rubbed on the vein until it perishes, and bound above the joint; and the vein is at the elbow, and through the sharp one goes much of urine; therefore, a wider vein, or at the elbow, which is more valuable.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you have healthy bones above the flesh, and if you are surrounded by those who are sick, and the healthy ones cross as if in a pan; and let the flames be similar.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot issue from the bone, put the flesh in the hot water, and let the wound well drain.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if it needs to be done for the first time, then start the second one above a little, because the legs are salty; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and thus make the other bone equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein of the ankle is at the knee of the foot, and its healing is equal to the pain of the back, when it is for an abscess.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of his health is such that the hairs between or in bathing, and it is stretched above the ankle four times in twisting, because otherwise it does not open the vein; and if it opens, then heal it in all ways that you can, and crosswise; and it is best to cover it, for the legs are clean, and it is very prone to infection by hand.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not treat it, it will heal of its own accord, from any opening or two piercings, and it will grow to the little toe, and keep away from the nerves; and drain as much blood as you see, and then release the ligament, and put cotton on it and stretch it; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of suction wounds
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Suction wounds are made of needles, or of iron, or of glass; and suction is done in two ways: either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this suction without pricking is done in two ways: either all at once, or without fire; and suction done by pricking and drawing blood is done in 14 places on the body, of which one is all over the chest; and the others are under the collarbone; and the other two are on the sides of the collarbone; and the suction from outside the mouth; and the suction on the shoulders; and the suction on the hips; and the suction on the arms; and the suction on the legs; and the suction on the ankles; and the suction does not treat blood, but only the small veins that are scattered in the body, and for this reason it does not weaken anyone, as one does with the evacuation of a vein; and it should not be administered, either with or without fire, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	If necessary due to illness, or by habit, we should venesect every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in every ten days; for there are some who, when they have need of venesection, have heavy veins; and there are some who experience repletion and dizziness in their face, and head, and neck, and darkness before their eyes; and there are some who taste blood in their mouth, and extend their tongue, and swallow blood; and there are some who dream, and see through blood and tears and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the month of May, we command them to fast for three hours after midday.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The fasting of the mucous membrane helps with the grievousness of the head … that comes to them, and it should only be after the evacuation of all the body; and this fasting is in place of the fasting of the cephalic, and it should not be used by those who are of cold complexion, or who have diarrhea, for this does much harm; and therefore it should not be used by those who are of cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often feel ill, become forgetful, and therefore it is necessary to place the suction cup a little lower due to the doubt of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The suction cup on the neck is in place of the head and the back, and therefore it is good for narrowing the throat, and breaking up the channel of the stomach, and all, and for replenishment; and one should not put it on too tightly, for if it holds too tightly, it causes forgetfulness or stomach pain and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The suction cup on the two sides of the neck is good for head pain, and obtuse pain, and emaciation, and strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is in place of the relief of the back; and one should command the sick person to put their hand when placing it, that they do not press the artery, and do not cause bleeding from blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The winds of the mouth cause disease in the mouth, and corruption of the teeth, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The winds of the shoulders cause disease that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The winds of the elbows are as important as three veins of the arm, for they draw blood from these large veins; and command the healer that he does not pierce too deeply, for the veins are bare of flesh, and can be damaged by nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup that is on the back should be used for emergency situations, and for diseases that are not treatable by other means, and it should be large and made of metal, so it can properly draw out; and if it is too delicate, it may break, and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	Leg suction cups heal openly, as they draw out blood from the entire body, and are good for old pains of the rain, and marsh, and bladder, and relieve the flowers; and they are in the place of the two knees, and everywhere they weaken the body over time, and bring on fainting in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the cupping glass is that you first place it empty and suction is applied immediately, and it is pressed firmly and moved evenly, and you should not stop doing this until you see the flesh turn red and swell, and the appearance of fresh blood; then stop, and replace the cups, and take care in the positioning of the body, for there are some who have tender skin and clear pores: it is necessary to strike once only, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and a few deep ones; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the cupping glass is large, it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to thinly cut through the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if it is very painful, you must prick the third time; and when we want to draw out the arrow slowly and slowly, we should only prick once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want much blood, we should often reapply; and if the pain is not alleviated, we should prick in front, and the end should be that the wound is pierced deeply, and it is suitable for those who have thick skin and are hard, and who have sharp pores, that you use the tips of oil-sucking vaccuums: if it is in this state, of violet oil, or of sweet almond oil, or of cucumber seed oil; and if it is in winter, of pennyroyal, or of lily, or of chamomile, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take oil of marjoram, or balm, or aniseed oil, and the likes.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one who is to be bled has wide and open pores, then one should not put any oil, but rather wash after the venesection of high rosewater, or high cold water, or myrtle water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or other similar thing.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, if they rise from ash, or high myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have excessive flesh rise from old wine, or from sour water, or from the decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things; and they should not be immediately purged after the bath, but an hour or two after, and they should not sleep immediately after being purged, and it is good for them to move around, when they should be purged and while they are being purged.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And if those who are constipated are also angry, and their stomach is too full and inflamed; then it is good for them to take cold things, such as large green apples and endives and lettuces in the sauce, and similar things; and thin broth, and cinnamon, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold constitution should take honey syrup, aromatic wine between old and new, and a little broth, and small pinches of spices and peppercorns; and on the day they are to fast, they must drink more than eat; and it is recommended to give some figs or raisins to certain people before or after fasting, to strengthen the main members; but one should not give this to everyone, only those who are strong.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are placed on the skin are those that are placed on the liver, and on the lungs, and on the gout, and on the stomach and the bladder and the rectum and the buttocks, because these members do not suffer from being pricked with needles, and no one does this except to draw blood from member to member, as we put suction cups on the breasts when the infant is born; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we place suction cups on the stomach and on the bladder to soothe the member; and to relieve pain, when there is an abscess or a stone, if by its attractive power it happens to draw out the abscess, or dislodge the stone from its place; and thus it is done when placed on the liver and on the lungs when there is retained viscosity, and these suction cups are administered empty for sweating only; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes with hot water, as in diseases of pleurisy, and in such a way that one fills the suction cup with hot boiling water, or hot water in which there have been cooked harmful herbs.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the vacuum administered by fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it has two inches of width and half a palm of length, and has or costs around the middle one small hole, as to put an needle, and it is of tin, sulfur before so that it does not burn the hair when putting on the member; and it has in the middle a rod of tin or iron, for putting a candle held, and they are large and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them; for the vacuums of children are other than of old people, and of thin ones than of fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should place this suction cup on the member: take the wax or wick, and put it inside the suction cup through the rod that is inside the suction cup, so that the light may be at the bottom of the suction cup so it does not burn the hair; then put it on the member, and you must place it as we have said, so that when one wants, if the vapor goes, and remove the suction cup; and take the wick again as before, and repeat often, if you have the skill.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the suction cup therefore that is administered in the disease of pleurisy, at all acute, has no rod or prick; and it is not administered unless it is full of acute, and is placed on the member alone; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Sansues are not used unless in members where one cannot place suction for their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar things; and in similar places, remove the clothing, such as two or ears, and other similar things; and the quality of using sansues is that when you trueve sansues that are in soft waters without pressure, take them; and put them in a soft water, until they are familiar, and have nothing in their bellies; then cleanse from blood and suction, then rub the member until it is red, and put on the sansues; and when they are plain, and healed, if it is a place where one can place suction, place it, for this is very helpful.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, first lift the limb from the affected side, and then from the high side, very well, and then wipe it; and if the wound is too large after the course of the sinews, then dip a linen cloth in cold water, and place it on, until the wound is cleansed; and if the wound multiplies, then place on it broken glass or salt, and similar things, until it is cleansed; or you put half of pounded flesh on the limb, and leave it until it dries to the limb, it will stop now; and if you have more trouble, take other sinews.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the wounds do not want to take, rub the flesh of blood fresh, or you have inserted a needle so that the wound does not open, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will close; and when you see that they are closing, powder with a little aloe and broken silk, or ash, if they will now heal.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it restores fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Be careful, dear child, that the foolish look at this chapter, that they have never seen any of the ancient books, nor lettered in them; and for this reason the science is hidden in our land, because I found none good; and I know nothing, except by the science of the ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have treated it, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and I have abbreviated it at the end, and I have shown clearly the forms of the instruments that are needed, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say or preface of this book the sums of the language and the chapters where the wise put their understanding, and dwell on the truth, so that those who are experienced find and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when fracture or dislocation or twisting or contusion comes to any part, it is necessary that you hasten to clean the wound on both sides, if nothing happens, as in weak people, children, or elderly; or if the tension is not very tight, or too stiff; and use cold remedies, such as cold oils, and eagle and chicken broth, and do not drink wine, and do not use any heavy meats, and do not fill up too much with food that fills the veins with blood, until you have no doubt of abscess formation, or spread of matter to the member; so return the wounds to their first proper governance that they had used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to grind the meat that causes large swelling, or has viscosity, such as cooked wheat, and rice, and tests, and pie, and pancakes of milk, and eggs, and fish, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For the grinding, it is better to do it sooner rather than later.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the broken bones of the old and the elderly cannot be properly healed or glued according to their nature due to the decay of the limbs, nor those who are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but rather, reset the broken bone above the bone, using large strong ones that fit and join the member together, until it enforces as it was before; and do not leave any part of its work, and for this reason, it is necessary to grind large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And the fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot, and I will tell you all the ways of fracture in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go around, and others in soaking, like the shape of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture all in a small cut.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each kind has its own method and proper tool in restoration, according to what the memory brings to its mind; and the fracture of the bone is known by the fact that the bone is twisted, and open wide by deficiency, and it is to the pressure of the hand; and when there is no tortuosity or it is not to the touch, and the pain is not great, if there is no fracture; but it can still have tortuosity, or cut, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not necessary that you move it with your hand, but place the remedies that come after this, and then gently hold it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And if the fracture that was in arvule, and the two parts are disjointed, you should now put them evenly, as soon as abscesses come out; and if abscesses come out, if it leaves no jor, until the abscesses are calmed; then place it evenly to the muscles that you can lightly and safely, and if the restoration of this is lighter than the restorations of that where he has pieces; then hold, as it should be after this.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if the bone is broken into pieces, if it is a hand or foot, or if it is small members, or to two strings, or to one string and your hand; and put the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are joined, you should gently move them in the way you can, and guard that by your work no harmful injury or pain comes; and well set the two ends of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel well in your hand if it seems to you that it is not quite right: if it is well dressed, and do not hold it too tightly, nor press it as those who bring by their work abscess and contraction to the member, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the member is straight, well chastise the painful part so it does not move, whether awake or asleep, turning or in any other way; and guard well that the member is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it feels no pain, it is almost straight, and you should put it in the right disposition so it feels no pain; and guard that it is put straight, for crookedness does not come when it is restored; and the quality of the member broken is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The members broken are different in smallness and in greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small members, such as arms and legs and similar ones: if they are thin, cover them with soft linen cloths; and those that are thick, such as thighs and legs: if they are thick, cover them with a wide and strong bandage, for the wide bands embrace the whole member evenly, and hold it equally in all parts, so that there is no gap; then wrap around lighter sterile dressings, three or four times according to the length of the member, and hold your hand a little on every part of the bandage, then go above the wound and hold it less, than the wound slowly moves away from the wound; and soften the bandage little by little, until you grasp a large part of the healthy flesh, then take another bandage and return around the same way behind the wounded part; then return to the part away from the wound, and hold it gently, neither too hard nor too painfully, as we have said in the first part above; then place between the bandages sterile linen or cloth, until they are all even, then tie everything from above with a bendeil, and then put your well-made stitches on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is an inflammation or abscess, put something soothing on the abscess and what opens the inflammation, and leave it like that for some time; then apply pressure with a clean cloth, or a stick made into a clip, or a palm leaf, and they should be according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But the cloth that one puts on the wound should be slightly larger and wider than the others; and it should also be as long as the limb of small size or great size; then apply pressure with the cloths as you did in the first layer, then tie up under a thread evenly, as in the first layer over the break; the tighter the better; and it should be that the threads are medium, not too thick or too thin, and they should be of fine linen; for if the threads are thick, as I have seen works of people who make their cords of twisted linen, and this is great error, because the layer cannot be even if it is too fine, and it should only have a space of about two fingers between each cloth.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the hairs are pricked by the thorns after straightening them in their natural position, then soak them in linen or some other clean cloth, so they do not become inflamed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the bone fractured, and the bones are broken, I will tell you the treatment afterwards.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And do not strain all the broken limbs at once on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not advisable to put them in plaster immediately after 5 or 7 days, or more depending on your risk of abscess; and take the method of ancient plasters to restore fracture, dislocation, and torsion: and you should take flour that is kept around the walls of the mill, and mix it with abundant water, and make this mixture, not too clear or too thick, and use it, and this is the common method of the plaster restoring the fracture to many positions, and especially to women and small children, for it is neither too hard nor too soft.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way to remedy fractures, dislocations, and twists: take alabaster and lavender, and pound and sift it, and add Arabic gum and mugwort, 10 grams; myrrh and aloes, 5 grams; alecost, 8 grams. Grind them into powder and mix with honey; if the patient's constitution is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and it will quickly heal broken bones and is beneficial to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another plaster that is good for twists: take mugwort and valerian, 10 grams; myrrh and aloes, 8 grams; acacia, 6 grams; Armenian bole, 10 grams. Pound them well and mix with vinegar or honey, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to heal joints and bones is to apply them with their own juices, and alleviate the pain, and use the tail of the bone, and the broken piece: take a new one, and moisten it in oil and warm oil, and place it on the wound.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not heal immediately, but it is good for alleviating abscess pain, and properly relieves the pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to heal broken bones: take dried fig leaves and earthworm leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of healing a broken bone and to ease the remaining pus of an abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the root of valerian, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of wheat, from each one a part; and grind, and make into a paste with wine, and if the member is hot, apply the paste with moist coriander juice, or dry, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method of healing more than the first, when an abscess is difficult to restore the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take the root of valerian, and linseed, balm, melissa, and mint, and flowers of violets and chamomile, from each one a part; and grind, and make into a paste with salty water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates said in his book that one should not put on a broken limb to restore it, except for a mixture of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he said that it should be between two things, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen said that one should put on a broken limb to restore it, things dry and slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to treat an injury and pain: take mugwort and horsehair, or feathers of an owl, and wax, and silk equally, and grind them, and make a plaster and the bandage.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then release the joint slightly afterward, and be careful if the hairs do not feel any pain, or if the bones of the limb are not misaligned; then do not release it by force again. If pain comes to the limb, or itching, without rest or inflammation, then hurry and release it, remove the poultice now; and take a clean cloth, and moisten it with sea water, and soak it in hot water, and raise the limb until the itching stops, and ease the pain. Then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, moistened in hot oil or rose oil, and tie a nut around it, as long as you are sure of no abscess forming; and reduce the inflammation of the limb, and relieve the pain, then resume the fine poultice, and a little of the plaster, but do not strain it too hard as before; subtly until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is filled with pus and redness and pain and swelling, and you have the skill of plasters and liniments, then restart it as you did before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if the limb does not return to its place within three days or four or five or seven; and you leave it for twenty days, as long as the injury is evident, and approaches the joint above; then restrain it more than before, and increase its flesh, as I have said before; and if you see that the limb dries up more than is necessary, then scrape the skin with a sharp knife every time you dislocate it, and this should be done every day, and loosen the ligament slightly; by this method, then, the skin is scraped off from the limb, and it is healed hastily as the foolish ones do, who restore the limb painfully: this is bad, and if it is not done properly, I see nothing else but suffering and doing it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various methods of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many methods of breaking are, and various shapes, and the causes are distinguished; for there are breaks that are made by percussion of spear, and the collarbone completely fractures the bone just below it which is outside the bone, as if it were cut or broken; and for this reason this method of breakage is called «haichure».
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or the spear pierces the bone from above, and this method of breakage is called «absolute»; and it is the wound of these two breaks, great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is percussion from above, or cutting or from the neck of the spear, or to fall on the stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if he has a broken bone that approaches the skin, which is outside the bone, or above the bone, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.
