And if the wound that is set in the bone as thin as a hair, and the fracture is small, and for this reason it is called "capillary" breakage; and if the wound made by being struck by an arrow, or falling, or something similar, and makes the piece of the bone enter below, and the threads are like those used by cooks when they pierce the pots; then the arrow enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And there are more cases where the bones are moist, such as in children; and they have all these ways of breaking, as small pieces are dislodged like these; and I will speak about them in their place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all ways of breaking by pulling on them, and by the inspection of tented parts, and by the rotten flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of the hairy part is known because when the bone is exposed and rubbed with it, if there is an open black break.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the break, be careful of accidents of evil, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, and loss of understanding, and extension, and paleness, and fever ague, and the eyes to issue forth and redden, and other similar things in more dispositions, then it cannot be healed without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any obvious injury, and you hope for recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fracture comes first to you, and it is in the bone, then you must remove the bone before the fourteenth day or you will not be able to.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the soft tissue, then you must remove the bone before the seventh day, provided that the skin over the bone is not rotten, and the injuries that we have mentioned occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone comes just under the skin that covers the skull, then it is necessary to cut out the part of the wound in this way: and you should grasp the head of the painful wound, and uncover the bone in all ways that you can, and over the shape of the wound as softly as you can, and if blood comes out when removing the bone, or an abscess forms, help it according to what is necessary, and it is necessary to fill the wound with moist cloths in red oil; and let the wound rest until the abscess is soothed, and make sure that no more blood comes out; then begin around the bone to remove, and this is done according to the two methods of work: one method is that you cut close to the edge in front, and this is the form.
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	Then make another cut larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have many different cuts, some narrow and others wide, and they are sharp and made of iron; and work gently, so as not to wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the tooth is very hard and outside, it is necessary that you perforate around it, as long as you administer cuts with awls, not in front of the tooth, but underneath; and above the point should have a margin or a circle, which does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and you should have many, so that each one comes in its own place of the surface of the bone, so that you have awls for all teeth; and this is the form of the three methods of awls:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	To pierce the bone through a broken one is to put the needle through the bone, and turn to your right until you feel that the bone is pierced; then move the needle to another part a little later, and so do all around, then cover the incisions the space of the bone that is between the teeth, and do it more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you remove the bone to your hand, or to any of the tools you have like forceps, pliers; and beware that you do not touch the brain or the sinus.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and removed the bone, it is advisable to close the opening that remains on all other tools similar to a needle, but it should be more flexible and more subtle than the other needle; and if there remain any small bones, or scales, remove them gently with the tools; then treat the wound with tents and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way of working is as the Gauls say, which is more safe; and the law is very strong, and that is their word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is first necessary that you remove a part of the bone where the break is open, so that when you have exposed that part, you can place the lens shape of this eyelid, which is why it is shaped like this:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one part, and the broken part is in two pieces, so that the cutter is against the bone; then use a small hammer on top, so that you lightly tap the bone all around, and be careful of the thread that is outside; if it is against the bone, lightly tap the bone, because it is done well without causing harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break in the bone does not pierce through the skin, and the bone is broken only from above, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to remove those sharpness, and to scrape off the scales with the fine razor that you should have various quantities of, to manage each limb in the most convenient way, according to the work and the shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If before large razors, and then more subtle ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair-cutting and subtle break, it is necessary that you manage according to its advancement; and this is a thing that is not replied to by him who has put his study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	If the wound is exposed, it is necessary to apply a cloth of linen according to the size of the wound, and moisten it with rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another cloth doubled in two or three, and moisten it with wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth; and do this more gently than you can, so as not to irritate the wound, then administer by pouring over another liquid, and do not restrain it except until the wound is healed only; and leave it in this way for one or two days, until the abscess is calmed, then remove it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, flour of vetch, frankincense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; and from these things make a powder, and place it on the wound, and administer liquid medicines without irritation; and keep the wound clean, so that you do not leave any bandage, or any dirt, because when dirt accumulates on top of the brain, it causes great harm; for when something sharp is placed on the wound, it does not heal.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	If no accidents occur, as we have said, then it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no other harm comes except what the medicine has put on it, which has virtue, then you should apply a part of honey, and three parts of red oil and one cloth, and put it on the wound; then cure it by various methods of cures until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Sometimes both bones of the elbow are broken, or one by itself, because they are two; and the other is cartilaginous, and does not break, unless it is dislocated or twisted, and then it is healed.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you break your small nail or needle at the tip of your finger, and place the broken part inside your index finger, and in the palm by default, until the bone regains its natural shape; and do this lightly, and keep in mind that the pain should not be felt through your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the broken part is in the part above the nail, and cannot reach the finger, then it is necessary that you place it at the top of a small bone.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the broken part is from both parts, then make another one, and hasten to restore the first joint, if you can; otherwise, after the seventh or eighth day, when the swelling of the wound is calmed, then break at the top of the finger, using pieces of linen cloth, if the broken part is in one piece.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	When you move from one side to the other, if the fracture is there; and if the tents are so large that they fill the pores of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And no one said how to boil the tents in water, and to kill each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I do not think that this is good, but it should be boiled in a confection of egg and powdered alum; then leave the tent until the bone is hard, and the cartilages are hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never use feathers in place of tents, and if you have some swan down, and if the fracture is present, and if you blow the pain away; now do what you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes to the nose while you are working, put a piece of cotton or a cotton swab in rose oil or a drop of iodine.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess does not come to the nose, then apply a paste of mustard flour and incense powder mixed with egg yolk, then place light cloths over it, but do not tie the nose too tightly; and if the broken pieces of the nose are small and in many pieces, then extract them with suitable instruments, then cut out the wound, and care for the injured parts as appropriate, and bandage them as appropriate; and if there is no wound inside the nose, then treat it with tents, and put in hot poultices until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is fractured without an open wound, and the break is not complete but only partially, and it is not broken in two pieces, but rather bent inside, if one knows this clearly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the break is in the right part, you should push your right index finger into the mouth of the patient; and if the break is in the left jaw, push your right index finger with your right hand, and gently push the break inside, and bring it to the other hand by force, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break in the jaw is displaced in two pieces, it is necessary that you administer traction of two parts until it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movements of the teeth cause breakage, or if they are broken, then strain them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place it on the broken jawbone, and place a cloth over it; and place on the cloth a great well-made plaster, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the jaw, and fasten it with a muscle that you can, and command the patient not to move, and give them light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the shape changes, then remove it from the animal immediately, and then put back what was changed; and place a plaster on top, of flour from the mill with an abundance of egg or bran of linseed, after you have removed the broken jawbone; and place on the plaster another light one, and if the plasters stick together, and the position of the patient does not change, leave it until it is healed; often it is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses come, as we have said many times, apply what we have advised.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, wrap no part of the bone in its place; instead, carefully remove it with uncovenable tools to that end.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, enlarge it as needed by fire.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there is none left, clean the wound if it is wide, and apply uncovenable plasters to that end, to stop bleeding until they are healed.
de la forcele	of the elbow
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The elbow breaks many times in front of and behind the shoulder, and the break is in three ways: it is broken and dislocated into two, and there are pieces, and it is the least heavy to restore; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work regarding the break with a wound is that you have two assistants, one of whom tends to the injury of the elbow broken; and the other stretches the collar towards the affected part; then set the break to your hands, so that it is as it should be, and there is no appearance or movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	If you have the task to extend further, place a rounded ball of cloth or linen, as needed and according to your necessity, under the shoulder against the pain; and extend and relieve the pressure, and hold the ball in your hand, so that you make the fracture even, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the shoulder downwards, because it comes out in front, then it is necessary that the painful parts be gently moved up and down over their place, and place something under the shoulder, a moderately sized earthenware jar, and push up the shoulder until the bone of the shoulder is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then apply the fracture to your own, and if you have true teeth broken, it is necessary that you cut above; and carefully file the pieces lightly, and if the bone cannot join for any reason, then use one of the instruments you have; but put the forceps of this instrument aside to guard against the gum:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and it seems like a spoon, and is not too sharp, and should be as wide as needed, according to the size of the bone and the skill of the work; and have two prongs, if you see, and one large and one small, if the tear in the wound that you made when you cut the bones; and when you are sure of an abscess, clean the wound, and if the tear is small, or you doubt an abscess, use the wound with bandages and tents, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess comes, if it is heated, soak the cloth in rose oil and vinegar and wine, and put it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The application of the bone fracture, when it is in pain and in cutting, is that you put the plaster of the mill powder and some egg on top of the bone, and put light dressings on it, and put a sphere outside the wound, if you have the skill; then take a very large bandage of one palm wide, then put the cloth double over the dressing and the plaster; then take a thin needle of three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage, so that the head of the bandage hangs down; and put the needle on the fracture, and turn the bandage over the neck, and remove the sphere outside the wound, and remove the sphere of the bad part; and splint each part, and when you see that the bandage holds the fracture evenly, and you see clearly that the needle does not move over the broken bone, reward it every day, and when the bandage is released, restrain it; and let the bad part lie on its back, and put what little ointment outside the wound as you sleep; to raise the fracture high; then align the fracture by the alignment of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not remove the bandage if no evil accident happens, for up to 20 days; then restart the plaster, if you see that it has a skill, and hold and let it be so until it is restored; it is restored in the most in 28 days, and less to some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It rarely happens that the shoulder is broken or the bone is not in its place, and it is not possible to move it except by touch; then apply the splint according to the shape of the fracture, and put it back according to its natural form, in all ways you can; then apply powder from the mill with plenty of honey, and light dressings, and put on a double cloth; then put on a wide and delicate splint, a little wider than the shoulder, and if the splint is not in any part of the shoulder, then use a linen strip to tie it evenly; and then tighten it firmly with a large bandage so that the splint does not move from its place, and watch it every day; and every time it breaks, tighten it again if it is still in its place, and cover the pain on its side; and the shoulder is restored in 20 days or 25 days. And when this number is completed, remove it, and be careful, for it is not bone that heals quickly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone is sticking out before, and not removed immediately, then cutting it off, and the bone, and do what we have said in the breaking of the mallet to relieve an abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the hammer
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The hammer is never broken in the middle, but it happens sometimes; but it breaks often at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it leans to one side, and the patient feels great pain, and there is no relief, and everything, and possibly vomiting blood, and the jaw is open in the broken bone, and the patient feels very ill.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And for the restoration, it is that the hairs are pulled gently up over their backs, and the medicine is placed between the shoulder blades, then press the shoulders, and gather the ribs of the two ribcages in your hands, and subtly place them evenly in all ways you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then place salves and ointments on top of the thin layer of salt, or another light one, and wrap it in a cloth, and tie it to the broken bone so it does not move; then round the limb gently to the back, and gradually tighten, and every hour rewrap the bandage, and if it loosens, if necessary, quickly remove it, and remove the plaster, and address what has come from various methods of treatment; then replace the plaster, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of rib fractures
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	that the rib fracturer comes only from great blows to the back and at the back of the neck, and does not occur from anything else because they are brittle; and it is felt well in the examination as such.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatment is that you set the fracture as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply the plaster and splint it with a splint, if you know how to do so.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the rib fracture is declining inwards, it feels great pain and tenderness, as if of pleurisy, because the ribs press on the lungs; and there is much blood, and all is bloody, and there is great suffering, and this is a grievous sickness, and the ancients have put much effort into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And for those who say it is necessary to administer foods that swell the stomach, to push the broken bone out of place.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this mistake, unless there is no pus if it has not come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then cleanse it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they said that no one puts suction on the limb, for it draws out harmful substances, and this is reasonable; however, doubt remains because of the weakness of the limb's position.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they said that no one should cover the limb with linen dipped in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to even out the lung around it, then treat the care of pleurisy, food, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the pain is great that he cannot bear it because of the bone that does not pierce the skin, and there is doubt, then one must cut across the broken rib on the side, and it is necessary to put a splint for the wound; and then one must saw the bone, and gently pull it out, and then stitch the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and treat them with ointments, until they are healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes on the chest, put moist cloths soaked in rose oil on it; and treat it while the wound is being cared for, and let it lie quietly near the chest where it should be, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	There is never a breaker of the neck bones, and very little that it bleeds; and so at the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to anyone, and you want to know if they will be healthy or not, if you see their hands softened and swollen and dead, and they cannot move or extend them, and when you touch them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	It is often deadly in many conditions, and if they move and feel well when you press on them, but not when you do not, it means that the joint of the bone is saved, and the pains are healed, if they are treated.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	If a similar thing comes to the spine of the back, and you see if it is healthy or not, if you take warning if the feet are soft, and if the accidents that are in their hands, and above the back there is a certain sensibility and involuntary evacuation; and when it is laid on its belly, there is involuntary evacitation.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is laid on its back and it wants to sit up, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	It is dangerous: do not labor in its care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to it, then the thing is less serious.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the care is that you reward if there is an abscess, apply rose oil or goose fat to the spine until it is calmed; then apply one of the healing plasters and drying, and tie with a bandage, and command the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where he feels the pain, until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is splintered, it should be covered with a clean cloth; then take the bone, and gather the two lips of the wound together, if it is large, at a seam, then treat the wound with a poultice of charcoal until it is healed; and if the patient's fractured bone is broken, which is called the "bone of the cow", if you have a pouch in your right hand, put it on the other hand to your power, then place the plaster and the bandage on top, if you have skill; then bind it, and if there is any splintered bone, do the same, and take the bone, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the ribs in the back
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It rarely happens that the ribs in the back are broken, and if it does, it is not much different from a slight pain to the head; and lengthening it, and declining towards the parietal, and coming to the skin, and pointing, and swelling as what is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over it, as far as you are over the broken part; and cut away what is broken and its shape; and if the break is only at the top, then set it straight until it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it inclines inward, then make the patient lie on their back until the healing of this fracture is complete.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it even, then place the poultice on top, then place a splint of wood or cloth, and hold the fractured part still so it does not move; and apply the bandage around the sides, until the limb is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess occurs, do not touch it until the abscess is calmed, and follow what we have previously said; then return to the healing process, and hold it as it should be, if there is no bad accident; and this is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder dislocation
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is located between the neck and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, one must restore it according to one of the two methods: one of which is that you take a piece of bone of equal thickness, in this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two ends together, and let them hang down, and saw through the broken bone above the seat; then pour some water over the broken piece of bone until it becomes easy to move, and put a hook on it, then let it hang on any heavy object or tool that extends it downwards; then place the broken pieces of bone together in their hands, until the broken person returns as it should be.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that one should prick the hairs above their temple, and then hold the patient's hand on their collarbone, then command two ministers to have one tug on the part that is above the broken bone at their hands, and the other tug outside of everything, and stretch each one to their part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is too far, then hold the patient's limb outside of everything, and above the broken bone, and stretch each one of the ministers to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the broken bone is near the top of the shoulder, then you should hold the middle part outside of everything, and the other towards the back, outside of the broken bone; and similarly, if the broken bone is towards the back, then it is necessary to gently move it, without pain, until the broken bone is even with the shoulder, and the back, then equalize the fracture, as it should be, and hold it in place, if there are no signs of infection.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	If an abscess appears and comes out, if it is not pressed within seven days, and put on a poultice of linseed and rose oil, until the abscess is soothed; then press it, and the way to press it is that you place the plaster over the affected area, then bring the arm up with the assistance, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and put the bandage, and press over the assistance, and over the arm, so that the arm is in its place, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone does not move.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	If you doubt that the bone does not move, use splints, and place a wider and stronger one than the others on the fracture, and have two inches of space between each splint, and let each splint be so large that it passes the fracture three inches from each side; then strain upon the splints, as I said at the beginning of this chapter, more strongly and less distantly.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the position of the splints and the straining, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the abscess is not healed, let it lie for seven days, as we have said; then look at the joint every three days, that it does not prick or swell, or the pus does not come to the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents occur within three days or more, and the pain remains on his back, and his hands are on his stomach; and he places the remedy on a cloth equally, and looks at it every hour of the day or night, that the figure of the member does not move, or that the ligaments are not softened; then by the power of medicine, and give him the food we have previously put in front of him, in such a way that the food is at first subtle; and when he begins to recover, it should be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be reset in 40 hours after everything; and then one must apply heat and medications of ointments for the limb to recover.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	If its structure is ugly and swollen, it may take 1 month or 2 months to reset.
de la brisure du bras	of the break of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "humerus," one of which is small and is the one that makes the pouch; and the other is large and is the one that is outside, towards the small end; perhaps the large humerus breaks alone, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When small bones are broken, the restoration is light, and the healing; and when large bones are broken, the healing is poor, and more painful than when they are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small bones that are broken, then it should be slightly extended and aligned.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large bones, then it should be stretched more forcefully; and extend it over the cushion, and tuck the hand pouch higher than the others, and the small fingers lower than the others, and let the hairs cross over themselves, and the cushion in front of him higher, so that the hairs do not cause any labor; then stretch the ministers to the part outside his hand, or to the other, and other ministers to the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then he puts the mirror evenly, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it breaks into pieces, put each in its place, and if there is no way to hold the bone together, and you cannot restore it to its place, then do as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the broken piece there is a wound, I have spoken about it to the chapter; take care of the wound.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if at the beginning of the restoration abscesses appear, then make an oiled cloth with red oil and white wax, which is not too hard or too soft; and tie the cloth gently, until the abscesses are relieved.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the splint, and put the plaster of the powder from the mill with abundant oil, then place the splints, and let the splint of the broken part be a bit further outside, and a bit wider than the others; and make sure it has six splints or more: whether the broken part is in one of the bones, or in two; and hold it higher than the broken part than any other part, and always less in moving away, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the cloths that are on the broken part be soft and moist, and not too hard or sharp; and let the thread, by which it is held, be linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	Reward the member and the limb after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any accident occurs to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you must raise the limb in hot water, until those itches are soothed; and let the limb rest loosely.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	Then restart the restriction, and if the limb is broken and the bones are dislocated, and similar things, then advise.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the bruises cannot come to the limb, because it is too tight, then you must soften it a little, and leave it like that for some days, until the bruises have healed, and then restrict.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	If none of these things we have said come to pass, then do not delay in seeking help for up to 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Or if it is inside, then place your hands on his neck, and make his neck even, and guard against movement and degitement, and lie on his back; and wait for this fracture to be restored in 30 days or 50 days, and perhaps in 20 days, according to the constitutions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the broken hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Wait until the back of the hand and as we have said before, there are few fractures, and it does not come but many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	When the bone of the hand is broken or dislocated, it is necessary that the hairs be cut straight and evenly; then place your hand on the flat surface, and extend the ministers' broken bones, and place them evenly in their places, until they are well joined; then apply the plaster and bandages, if there are no abscesses, then put a splint according to the size of the limb; and let it be wrapped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the broken bone is on the inner side of the sole of the foot, make a sphere of cloth, and command the patient to press it against his broken foot; then wrap him in a long cloak, and place the splint as wide as the sole of the foot, and apply it as appropriate.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the forearm, it is necessary to place one splint above and another below the hand, so that the hand is open and straight, then bind it completely around the arm, and stitch the ligament between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to any of the two, whether it is the little finger or another, straighten it as it should be; and bind it with the palm, and if you see that it does not move, place a straight small splint to lift the fractured part, and do not let it move; and if the fracture is in the other fingers, whether it is the index or another, straighten it as it should be, and bind it with the healthy finger that is next to it; or you can tie them all together, as long as it does not hurt, or place a splint above, as you would for the little finger; and pay attention to restoration and positioning of abscess, and take care of what comes out, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken rib
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The ribs of the rib cage are often broken, and one can see when they return in front and behind; and the restoration is such that one lies above the broken part, and the other outside.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the broken parts are set on their face, then each minister extends his side equally; and it is when the break is inserted into the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is close to the root of the rib cage, then one of the ribs should be on top of the other, and the other ribs outside the broken part.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it is close to the shoulder, and then one of the ribs should be on top of the shoulder, and the other ribs below; then put the bone evenly in your two hands, as long as it is according to its natural shape, and then put the plaster, and the bandage, unless there is no healing.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	If there is an abscess that has burst, let it calm down first, then return to your work and treatment; the matter is done in a similar way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary to wrap the injured area with a bandage rolled up in two or three layers, and let the excess remain, then return the leg until the toes reach the root of the foot, and tie a long thread between the thigh and the leg, below the knee joint, and bring the upper end of the thread above; then return to the leg and thigh, and tie the bandage, then place the injured area on top of the bone of the leg; then apply the bandage between the leg and thigh with soft cloth to equalize the pressure, then begin to bind firmly three or four times over the injured area; and as you go higher than the injured area, and less tight; then check the two ends of the thread that you tied between the leg and thigh, and the three bands above, then return to the top of the thread, until you reach below the knee joint; and if it does not move from its place, then let it remain, so that there is no abscess or swelling or similar.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If it is, release it, and direct it to where it comes from, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of the bone that can be gripped, they should be removed if possible; and if not, the limb should be cut and the fragments removed; and the treatment should be done as we have said until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never break the bone in such a way that these are inserted, as in the dislocation and with the arm; however, in such a restoration, it does not hurt the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And it is said that the bone is restored at different times, according to the variety of constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the way of the gentleman
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	It is said that in the way of the gentleman, there is little breakage, but it often weeps.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is only a small cut, or a puncture, and it has to all wounds, and without wound, and it feels good.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that one puts together what is broken to its two ends, as much as it can be assembled, then put on the ointment, and if you have skill, put a round bandage, and hold it as it should be, then warm all the preparations that we have said in other breakages, such as abscess and similar; and for each accident that it needs, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the broken leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is called "tibia" and the other "fibula"; and they are all as fragile as those in the arm, and for this reason the restoration is the same as that of the arm equally, and the work is all the same. And if both these bones are broken at once, then the leg returns to its former state in all parts.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, then it heals in front.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, then it causes great pain and can be seen easily; and it heals outside.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Therefore apply counter-extension, and make it even, and tie the fractures equally; but nevertheless, it is necessary to have a break that is ugly, and there are many pieces, so that the extension is less and lighter; and the bandage according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two strips of cloth that gird the leg on one side and the other, and be long enough from the knee to the ankle; then wrap around the leg above and below, and tie in the middle as well, and at this point it will not bend the leg to the right or left, and thus it is good; and no one administers the long cloth of the leg, and it is made of fustian, and properly placed on the fracture where it has a wound; and move the leg every day to see if there is an abscess or other accident; if the cure until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of bone fractures
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but of bone fractures, it never comes and it is rare, and there are no other dispositions except for a slight bruise in some cases.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a bone fracture, and you see these bones overhanging each other, if you put them on the ground, they will move like they want to walk, then place your foot on the side where the bones are raised, then press them until they return to their original position; then apply the ointment and poultice on top of the wound, and put a small cloth soaked in oil on the wound, then bandage the limb evenly, then wrap bandages around it, and other things that you know how to do.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, if you relocate the joint, you will find the bones even, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the two broken, if you mend them as we have said about the two bones of the hand; then place a splint along the length of the bone, and it should be slightly wider, then put the bandage as I have said, and tighten it gently; and if there are two or three or more broken, place a splint according to each bone's quantity, wrapped in a piece of linen, and fasten the bandage outside the bone; and let it be above the head of the bone below the belly of the wound, so that it heals well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is important that you do not forget the other things I have mentioned about other fractures, as we have said; and treat each case as it should be.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the finger bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bones of the woman are broken, if the pain is too great, then sit her upright, then lean her to the part of the back, and hold her from behind; then fill the wound with cotton, and put in as much as possible; then lift the woman, and gently raise the back, and slowly pull out the cotton, until it reaches the entrance of the wound, and the bone returns with the cotton; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has finished, return it, and thus do this for seven days: then the fracture will be restored, and if you see that it is not healing, take a bladder of goat's milk, and tie a pad to the wound, and blow all the milk into the wound; then inflate the pad repeatedly until the milk is fully absorbed inside: nature will restore the fracture; then fill it with cotton, and leave it in place for several days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the tooth of the finger of the man or woman is broken, if it is restored as we have said in the bone of the shoulder; and these broken fragments are not hidden from him who puts his study and use to this book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the broken tooth means in many ways the right way of restoration, understand therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the wand, when it is broken, take a goose gut and blow the wand; then wrap it in cloths and leave it for three days or around, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of broken with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a broken bone with a wound, even if it is large, such as the bones of the ribs or shoulder or similar, that they be cleansed immediately, so that the cleansings that we have mentioned bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is clean, and if the wound is dressed with vitriol, if you have no other means, then begin to restore the broken bone in the same hour or the next day, before the wound becomes infected.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the wound becomes infected, then leave the restoration until the next day, until the infection is calmed, and do not touch it on the following day or the fourth, for you will bring about bad events.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the teeth are broken and appear above the gum line, it is necessary that you gently place them in your hands, with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not equipped to be placed evenly in your hands, use an iron tool with seven or eight inches of length, and its width according to the size of the wound; and it is necessary for the mirror to have three or four, according to the number needed for each treatment of broken teeth; and let it be round and somewhat thick, so that it does not pierce through the member at your work, and let it be sharp in front, and thick in the middle, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", because the patient must place the broken bones on top of the head of the visible bone; and it is struck once, as much as it returns, and they are evenly aligned one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instruments cannot well take the bone, then you must cut the head of the bone until the instruments have hold.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring back the bone as we have said, then use the appropriate cutting tool, whether an saw or a chisel, to your power; then file what remains in the bone of sharpness and small scratches.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned to its place, and the pain is great afterwards, advise that it not remain in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If it is in its place, then apply a stiff black wine bandage properly if necessary; and do not put anything on the wound or oil where it has been cut, so that there is no moisture and corruption; then administer these things as you have restored the bone, and leave the wound exposed, and cover the entire covering around, according to the size of the wound, and be careful that the wound is not stretched with the break; many times the fool has done this, and has caused the pain or death or corrosion in no case; and let the strains be softer and more supple than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that no harm has come to it, as we have said, and you relieve pain at the limb, then do not place anything on top of it; but around it, in place of anything, wrap hard cloths, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after an hour or two that the bleeding has stopped, remove what you have placed on top of everything, and put healing ointment on the wound, such as quadruple antifarmacological ointment and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary to clean the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is sound and healthy.
