Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limbs be aligned in such a way that the bow can move freely.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if they continue to exceed, and it cannot be sutured but remains dislocated, there are small pieces of bone, so it is necessary that you tear the wound with a tent, and remove all those unnecessary pieces that cause that pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the limb, or another way of corruption, then it is necessary that you treat it, according to what it says in its chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken, and open above the limb, like the bones of the thigh or shoulder, and similar large limbs, do not remove it, for many times death comes, but leave it until it can heal; perhaps it will fall off after twenty days or thirty, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of sudden blows that come to the suture
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come after the healing of the broken bone, immediately near the joint, and it is a bad thing to see the shape of the limb; and perhaps it cannot do its natural workings.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore, if we find it fresh: if you administer stanching medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocollis, acacia, and similar things, in such a way that you take any of these or all together, and mix them with strengthening wine or plenty of blood or with oil; and put it on the nail on the opening, and hold it well, and do not let it out in your hands later; then loosen it, and start another, until the swelling is gone; or you hold a piece of bread well made; because the property of the bread is that it removes all swellings above the limbs; and if the swelling has become hard like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, so the cover over, and making the excess apparent; or you cut it with any razor, as long as it is removed, and cure it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	a weak limb that is after the garrison
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored, and it remains after the limbs are weak and subtle, there are many causes for this: one is because it was tied too tightly, and was not loosened as it should have been; or because there were too many bindings, and could not come to the proper settings of the limb; or because of too much swelling; or because of too great movements, not in its proper time; or because it has little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you lessen the pain, and make the body tense, until the swelling is not multiplied in it; and administer baths, and give joy and ease; then put poultice on the limb, so that the poultice attracts to the great setting, and the swelling often of high temperature, until the setting comes to the limb; and returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	a dislocated limb after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limbs are twisted after restoration, and the bones are broken open, and the shape of the limb is deformed, yet it does not harm its original nature: therefore do not believe those who say that one must break the limb entirely in new, and many have done this in our land; and these practices are blamed, and great evils come from it, and perhaps death; however, if the joints and the twisting are fresh, then it is necessary to apply hot water, or softening herbs that are cooked, such as willow bark, roots, and meadowsweet, and similar things; and the mollifying ointment, such as balm made well, and you take the willow bark powder, and mix it with goose grease or sesame oil, and apply the ointment; or you take figs, and grind them with linseed, and similar medicines that soothe the pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is it necessary to apply continuous and prolonged pressure with wet hands on a dislocation.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And you should allow movement to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is awake and hardened, as a stone, and it needs to be removed with iron, if it covers just to the bone, make a subtle incision; and put in a cup and let it rest in care.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to none, it must now be returned to its proper place.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if it is delayed, the joint swells, and if it is reset, it may be moved to a wrong place; for it is not good to move it to where it has swollen: many times it causes vomiting and other pains; however, when that happens, first clean the wound, then leave it, until the abscess is soothed; then raise the limb with hot and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each member as it comes back to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on the dislocations of the shoulder joint from the elbow to the fingers.
des mandibules	of the mandibles
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Sometimes the mandibles are dislocated and the dislocations of the mandibles occur in two ways: either they are slightly misaligned from their place and a little soft; or they are completely dislocated, hanging downwards, and they cannot hold the saliva of the mouth, nor can they close their mouth, and they wrap their tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it often returns to its place in many positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if she is whole and complete, it is necessary that you reset it quickly, and not delay; and in such a way that the assistant holds the chin of the painful part, and pushes the fingers somewhat into the root of the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and the other hand should be outside, to hold even; and command the pain to soften, its jaws, and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the fingers push evenly until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is difficult to return, immediately apply hot and oil, until it is reset lightly; do not delay the resetting as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are returned evenly, and the jaw with the bad pain is well closed to soften, then put on bandages made of cloth moistened with rose oil and wax, then lightly bind it with thin strips; let the pains lie on their back, and their jaws being between two cushions, so that they do not move to the right or left, nor make any effort to open their mouth, but take light food, until the pains are gone, and the jaws are healed; then change what they want lightly, and do not labor much to open the mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaw is well healed and healthy.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	If the two mandibles cannot be reset to their proper place within an hour and are not converted to their original position, then fevers and sweating become customary, and possibly diarrhea, and possibly vomiting of black bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then it is certain that it is a bad sign; and many times those who have it die in seven days.
de la forcelle	of the forceps
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot be used from the side without continuing to the other side and the worst part, and it is not reset once dislocated, and it is well felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the hairs are gently pulled to their back, and the arms are extended; then press the joint firmly against your palm, and it will return; then apply the bandage and bind it, and hold it; and the patient who is on the side cannot be dislocated; if not, and if it is dislocated once, then reset it to its place, as we have said; then apply the bandage and bind it, and hold it, and command the patient to rest until it is healed; and thus the same is returned when the patient is free from his joint.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	There are three ways that the shoulder may be dislocated: one is that it is dislocated at the part of the armpit to the outside; and the second is at the part of the elbow; and sometimes it is dislocated at the part above, and this happens rarely; and it does not dislocate backwards for the shoulder, and it does not dislocate inwards through the nerves; and many times it is dislocated outwards towards the armpit, especially to those who have little strength, because for these it is very difficult; to those who have enough strength, it is easily dislocated, and easily returns.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to some men, a blow or a fracture, and the shoulder swells with an abscess, and they think it is dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you must first examine him until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that the dislocation is when it is towards the acromion, and it distinguishes between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between them clear differences; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a groove, and below the acromion the top of the shoulder, as if it were an ossicle; and it cannot move its hand to its neck, nor move any movements; and in the same way, if it is dislocated above, it is not hidden, because you can see it clearly at the back; and this method of dislocation is not hidden, when it is new, or if the pain is severe.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the healers lift their hand to the bad joint at the top, then place their chisels outside the joint, and forcefully lift the joint upwards to the shoulder; and the healers lift their hand and extend it upwards, so they put it aside; then it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said before, then it is necessary that the joint be soaked in hot water; and the healer softens and moistens it with a decoction of althea and fenugreek and melilot in hot water, and apply it; then place the joint on its back, and put a cloth of even thickness, neither too soft nor too hard, under the joint, then place the heel of the shoulder on top of the cloth, and lift the head of the shoulder gently, and pull the hand of the joint; and other healers wet the head of the joint, so that it does not move downwards; this shoulder is now all right, and you must see if the joint is reset according to this method: and you must make sure that the person who is stronger than the joint is facing towards the side, and pull the shoulder away from the joint, and lift the joint upwards, so that the joint hangs in the air; and other healers take the hand of the joint down towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	If the pain is too light, it can move with anything heavy, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And the resetting is done in another way: and it is that one puts a long thin stick on the ground, which the patient should hold like a spear, but not too heavy or too hard; then it is placed away from the pain, but with a soft cloth underneath, and the joint should be on the long side of the fist; then the hand is extended down from the other side, forming a circle, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not want to return for all these things we have said, do this cure: take a stick of two arms and four fingers wide, which has the head rounded off outside the elbow, in this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then tie above the injured shoulder with soft cloths, which does not cause the injury to bleed more, then remove it from the shoulder of the injury; and extend one arm over the long one, and tie the assistance over the injury, and the arm at the head of the hand, then place the arm over the broad end of a spoon, and extend the hands downwards, and leave the body hanging on the other side: the joint is now healed.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is healed in any way, it is necessary to place a soft cloth under the shoulder, then apply the plaster evenly with powder from the mill, with incense and a little honey, over the entire shoulder and around, then remove it from under the shoulder gradually, and return the limb to the plaster, and embrace the hand at its neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he should change little, until the limbs are strengthened, for it will heal sooner; and then change after five or seven days, and move it; and if it is stiff and it is not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is strong from moisture that has come, or for another reason, then it is necessary to administer cautery at three points, as it is placed in front or in the chapter of cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it dislocates again after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot lift the arm up, then cut the nerve at the head of the shoulder is torn or stretched or softened; and cut that the joint has never been fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that occurs at the wrist and the fingers, or behind, is caused by impact and stretching of the hands, and it is treated with another bandage; and it is cured until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing the member becomes stiff and does not move, then use the hairs many times in a bath until that stiffness is relieved and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	The joint of the shoulder is often dislocated and returns; and it is dislocated from all parts, both in front and behind, and the dislocation does not return, for it can be seen and felt well; and it is dislocated according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the dislocated shoulder with its healthy counterpart, ensure the patient can see clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is sore, and it cannot bear the weight of the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary to reset the shoulder joint as soon as possible when it becomes dislocated, for if it becomes dislocated again, it would be painful to reset; and perhaps it cannot be reset entirely in every case, especially when it is at the back; rather, it is better than other dislocations, and causes more great pain, and perhaps it kills the patient.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, when it can be reset, that you extend your hand to their two hands; and their arms should be spread out, and their hands on either side of the shoulder, in and out, and push the joint back together, or at the root of their palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and holds the root of the palm which is misaligned.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if he does not want to return to its place, then apply strong extension; and let two ministers extend the arm, and tie it with two ministers, so that it does not move at extension; then turn the arm from each part, then when you have enveloped a double long and wide cloth; and when the patient sees the joint approaching his hand, if he holds any oil to soften the joint, then press the joint together, as much as it returns; and when it is in its place, put a dry plaster with some honey on top, and let it rest, and place the arm against the bad side, and leave it for some time, then remove it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, then release the limb and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, then restart the bandage and the limb, and leave it thus for some time, until it is firmly set; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the readjustment of the joint and it moves, then bathe and rub him well, and press until it is relieved; or place a piece of fat lamb fat on the joint, leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and put in a bath; and when he urinates, then rub the joint immediately, then place the fat again, and then put in a bath; and do this twice or three times until it is healed; and if you see that it is swollen, then place a piece of moist, warm chafed butter on it, and press it; it will return to its normal position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and its return is lighter than other joints. Therefore, it should be returned to its place immediately after it is dislocated, as long as the limb is swollen or if there is an abscess present.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the return is that you place the misaligned hand on a table, and extend the fingers of the hand, and place the palm on the appearance of the joint, and push it until it returns. Then, you should check if it is well placed; then, place the misaligned hand on a table for extension and return.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, put the patient's back of their hand on the table, and the other person puts their hand over the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, it is good. If not, apply the ointment of calming remedies to abscesses and leave it thus to begin again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place after some time, the joint will remain twisted; and do not pull anything on the patient until the hand is washed, and nothing can be stretched at all: then cut the nerve or artery; if there is no other means except to stretch by cautery through the skin, and perhaps nothing else is worth it.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put the plaster we have mentioned above it, then tighten and leave it for five days, then remove and leave it like this.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot be moved well, and there is no pain, then apply hot water and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the two fingers
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Never dislocate the two fingers in any part, never at the back of the palm or on the wrist; then straighten the two fingers, and reset the dislocation to your fists as it returns, then support the head of the finger, and pull it towards the part where it is disjointed; and leave it for five days, and then put it back that day; and tie it as we have said, and remove the bandage the next day, and move it, and reattach it; and do this often, until it is tight, and do the same if it is dislocated on the wrist of the hand, and do as you did before, until it is healed; and do the same when it is dislocated in other parts.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	back pain from the curvature of the spine
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the curvature of the spine or neck is dislocated, and there are many dislocations, there is no cure, for the patient dies from the pain.

And the signs are that the excretions jump without volition, cannot be held, and often the member is softened, such as the two elbows or the two arms or one, and often the spine moves to the fourth part; that which moves to the back is called "gilbositez": the cure is that you reward the gilbositez if it came from childhood: if there is no cure or healing at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And those that come from falling or from blows or similar things, they say of the old ways of cures by great words, which do not have much benefit; but I have abbreviated them according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the case of a fracture that comes from the front, there is no engineering or healing; and also the one that comes directly in the second rib, and one cannot cure it other than by the proper one that comes to the back, as I say; and it is that the wounds should be stretched over his face evenly, and have some straw away from him, so that he does not bleed; then make a bandage at the top in earth form, and the other at the bottom, and tie a ligature outside the fracture, and the other at the hips, and at the knees, and at the ankles; and the nurse should secure the ligatures, one at the top and the others at the bottom, among the two bandages; and they should be well tied, the bandage as we have said, and the fingers put her palms on the spine properly, until she recovers.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return by this cure, take a long table of three arms' length, and lift the patient from the ground, and place the painful side down, and press the head of the table away from the ground, then place the middle of the table on the spine; and place the mire's feet on the other end of the table, and press firmly, until it returns to its place; and if you see, do the same with the one who turns to the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And you should tie two straps at the head of the painful arm of a long arm, and on the side of the feet two more, and between each strap, outside and inside, a space of length; and in each strap one hole, or the turner corrects and they are the straps firmly on the ground so that they do not move; and between the two straps a strap turning, following the turner's turn, and in the two turns two small straps of length to turn the turner; and then tie the ligament that is among the tendons to the turner's head, and the other ligament to the feet of the other turner, and each minister turns his turner along the whole ligament, and the masters put the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, apply a drying ointment with plenty of honey, then wrap it, and then place it on a plate of three finger widths, to support the spine and the affected part of the spine, then tie it with a bandage as we have said, and use subtle pressure until it is healed; and if there is nothing in the end of the health, then you must administer medicines that are softening and soothing, with the method that we have mentioned before; and never give one piece of plaster, and never does it appear in the back spine of the back, and be careful that this is dislocation; and this is the bone that opens, because one should not have any presumption: by chance it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of shoulder dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	that the joints of the shoulder and the joints of the back do not come out except as dislocations only, and they do not come out like other joints; and the joint of the back is dislocated in four parts: inwards and outwards, and front and back; and more inwards than that, and less dislocated in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of inward dislocations is such that when one joints the crooked leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and more open than the healthy ones, and cannot double its calf at the fire; and it is the legs that are swollen from abscesses, because the one who has the back pain comes late.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of those who come after is that this accident is contrary to what has been mentioned before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of those who come before are that they have a well-set leg according to completion; however, their knee does not double over with pain, and if one wants to make it move forward, it cannot do so, and they retain their urine, and swell their anger, and when they walk, they pass over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of those who come after are that they cannot spread their knee, nor double over, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the anger is softened, and they have a pain in the ribs on the side.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The symptoms of this type of dislocation are such that if you return the joint to its place, it will stay in position according to its nature, and there is no cure; and there is no need for any presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in this case where the dislocation is fresh, and it is of four types, you must quickly return the joint, and extend and flex it to both sides; perhaps it will return again, and there is no need for other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, then you must use one or two strong assistants, and extend the leg strongly to both sides, or to the side that is lying on the bed; and others place their hands under the patient's armpits in a similar manner as they would to lift something heavy, then they lift him up by his shoulders; and others grip his head; and extend him above and below all at once, until the pain is lifted from the ground at once, and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common for four similar cases, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, it is necessary to treat its similarity. When the dislocation is in the shoulder, it is necessary to support the painful part on its healthy side, then place the ligament above the root of the neck, and the limb that is outside the shoulder, then extend the ligament above the shoulder blade and the spine; then take other ministers to hold the large muscle of the shoulder, and stretch it back into its proper place: if it returns to its limb now, this method of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you do not hold the two bones of the dislocation together in this manner that we have said, it is necessary that you tie the two legs of the painful part together with a strong rope above the two heels, and above the two knees, and let the painful leg be stretched two fingers more than the other; then hang it over the top of a stick, and let it be held two arms' length from the ground; then command the minister to grasp the neck of the chicken, and let another minister hang with the dislocation, who should firmly grasp the neck, for the joint is now approaching rapidly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is weak, grind the painful parts, as we have said in the one with gout, and stretch the rope properly above the painful leg and on the foot; then put two ties, one at the head and one at the foot, then fold the tie between the chicken's wings at the dislocation in the correct form; and wrap moist cloths around it, so that it does not become stiff, then extend each minister towards him, and the master puts the dislocation equal to his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place it on the flat surface, and press as we have described in the grease, and cut the hairs off the sound side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to stretch the injured leg quickly, as I have said; and place the fingers of the pain above the crooked part, then press with the other hand, and extend it downwards towards the groin.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is at the back, it is not necessary to extend the injured leg downwards, nor to raise it upwards, but it should be as it was dislocated at the back, as we have described in the couching of the two hips; and it should be on its face, and the limb extended as we have said before, and one should press on the joint on the table; and it will be all right when the hairs extend their legs, and they will be even; then bend the knees, and put the plaster, and the strap of a bandage, so that the hip does not move; and let it rest for three days or four, then release it, and put the plaster on; and if you see that they are even, then extend it as before, and leave it for three days; then release it, and make the limb move well, until the members are comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the shoulder dislocation
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The shoulder is dislocated in three ways: namely, from the inside and outside, and from behind; but not from the front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend his leg at his hip, and if he cannot do so, it indicates that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg as much as possible, and put your back against his face, and put his foot on your feet; then take his shoulder to your palms, and draw them together, then bend the two sides of the shoulder firmly; and another minister extends his foot, until the shoulder returns to its place, and the sign is that he can easily bend his leg at his hip; and put the plaster on, and rub the leg against the hip, and loosen it firmly for three or four hours, then release it; and do not work on the patient any more until his limbs are strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limbs are not in place, administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the back, until they are healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocated ankle
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The ankles are never bruised and never fully dislocated, neither inside nor outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the bone is dislocated and bent forward to the part where it is dislocated: the retraction is light, and one should gently extend it with their hands when it is only bruised.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is fully dislocated, you should sit the bone straight and hold it with your hands, above the ankle; then pull the bone to you with your right hand, and then with your left hand twice, then extend it upwards, and strongly tap the bone upwards; do this twice, as we have said, pushing and pulling the bone; if it returns, it is good; if not, start the work again, for it will return; and if it cannot return in this way, place the dislocated bone on its back on the ground, and firmly press between its thighs, and wrap cloths around it so that it does not move the bone; then hold the hands of the ministers on the thigh, and other ministers extend the bone to its hands or to the ligament, so that they hold the bone above the dislocation as you stretch it; then stretch all the ministers equally, and the cloths should be between the thighs of the dislocated bone to hold it as you stretch it; then place the minister with the dislocation at its hands, and other ministers hold the leg straight at the side, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when she does not go, apply the plaster and lance above, and let the wound heal, and tie the leg to the foot, and keep the nerves that are above the ankle behind, so that the joints are not too stretched; then leave it two or three days, and if the joints become loose, lance again; then release it on the third or fourth day, and defend against the evil for four days; and if it goes before this term, it is certain that it will not heal yet.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes, it is necessary to treat it as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	for two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, if they should be extended evenly with work, it is a simple matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any other part of the body, it is necessary that you make the patient sit with the injured limb straight out or on a table, and put your hand over what opens from these joints, then press firmly with your hand until it reverts; and when it is even, and there is nothing open, put the sole of the foot on a table for the injured part, then strain it firmly, and leave it three hours, then release it; and let him rest, until he is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and of dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When wounds come with dislocation, and one wants to restore them, often times the pain dies: if you are not presumptuous in the cure, and if you are not wise in the art and have not used it long, and if you are not pitiful and merciful and patient, do not be hard; and at the beginning of things, appease the abscess with heat, and leave the pain in God’s hands, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset the member now, as long as the abscesses are coming; and when the member is in place, then administer things to appease the abscess with heat, and cure the wound, as it should be, with dry compresses; and if with dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones are broken, then remove them, and do what we have said in simple diseases; and guard against entering the path of fear, according to what I have said, for it is better for you according to your Creator, and for the knowledge of your armor and your body.
Amen	Amen.
